    • DISA ASD STIG [APSC_DV]
      • APSC_DV-000160 The application must implement DoD-approved encryption to protect the confidentiality of remote access sessions. [APSC_DV-000160]
        • Do not use weak encryption functions [APSC_DV-000160-a-2]

      • APSC_DV-001995 The application must not be vulnerable to race conditions. [APSC_DV-001995]
        • Avoid race conditions when using fork and file descriptors [APSC_DV-001995-a-2]
        • Avoid race conditions while checking for the existence of a symbolic link [APSC_DV-001995-b-2]
        • Avoid race conditions while accessing files [APSC_DV-001995-c-2]
        • Use locks to prevent race conditions when modifying bit fields [APSC_DV-001995-d-2]
        • Do not use global variable with different locks set [APSC_DV-001995-e-2]
        • Avoid using thread-unsafe functions [APSC_DV-001995-f-2]
        • Usage of functions prone to race is not allowed [APSC_DV-001995-g-2]
        • Avoid using the 'vfork()' function [APSC_DV-001995-h-2]
        • Properly define signal handlers [APSC_DV-001995-i-2]

      • APSC_DV-002290 The application must use the Federal Information Processing Standard (FIPS) 140-2-validated cryptographic modules and random number generator if the application implements encryption, key exchange, digital signature, and hash functionality. [APSC_DV-002290]

        • Do not use weak encryption functions [APSC_DV-002350-a-2]
      • APSC_DV-002390 XML-based applications must mitigate DoS attacks by using XML filters, parser options, or gateways. [APSC_DV-002390]

    • AUTOSAR C++14 Coding Guidelines [AUTOSAR]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-1 A project shall not contain instances of non-volatile variables being given values that are not subsequently used [AUTOSAR-A0_1_1]
        • Avoid unused values [AUTOSAR-A0_1_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-2 The value returned by a function having a non-void return type that is not an overloaded operator shall be used [AUTOSAR-A0_1_2]
        • The value returned by a function having a non-void return type that is not an overloaded operator shall always be used [AUTOSAR-A0_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-3 Every function defined in an anonymous namespace, or static function with internal linkage, or private member function shall be used [AUTOSAR-A0_1_3]
        • Every defined function with internal linkage shall be used at least once [AUTOSAR-A0_1_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-4 There shall be no unused named parameters in non-virtual functions [AUTOSAR-A0_1_4]
        • Eliminate unused parameters [AUTOSAR-A0_1_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-5 There shall be no unused named parameters in the set of parameters for a virtual function and all the functions that override it [AUTOSAR-A0_1_5]
        • There shall be no unused named parameters in virtual functions [AUTOSAR-A0_1_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-1-6 There should be no unused type declarations [AUTOSAR-A0_1_6]
        • A project shall not contain unused type declarations [AUTOSAR-A0_1_6-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A0-4-2 Type long double shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A0_4_2]
        • Type long double shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A0_4_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A0-4-4 Range, domain and pole errors shall be checked when using math functions [AUTOSAR-A0_4_4]
        • Validate values passed to library functions [AUTOSAR-A0_4_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-1-1 Class shall not be derived from more than one base class which is not an interface class [AUTOSAR-A10_1_1]
        • Be wary about using multiple inheritance of classes that are not abstract interfaces [AUTOSAR-A10_1_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-2-1 Non-virtual member functions shall not be redefined in derived classes [AUTOSAR-A10_2_1]
        • Never redefine an inherited nonvirtual function [AUTOSAR-A10_2_1-a-2]
        • Member functions declared in derived class should not hide functions declared in base classes [AUTOSAR-A10_2_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-3-1 Virtual function declaration shall contain exactly one of the three specifiers: [AUTOSAR-A10_3_1]
        • Only one of virtual, override or final should be specified in a member function declaration [AUTOSAR-A10_3_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-3-2 Each overriding virtual function shall be declared with the override or final specifier [AUTOSAR-A10_3_2]
        • Each overriding virtual function shall be declared with the override or final specifier [AUTOSAR-A10_3_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-3-3 Virtual functions shall not be introduced in a final class [AUTOSAR-A10_3_3]
        • Do not introduce virtual functions in a final class [AUTOSAR-A10_3_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-3-5 A user-defined assignment operator shall not be virtual [AUTOSAR-A10_3_5]
        • A user-defined assignment operator shall not be virtual [AUTOSAR-A10_3_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A10-4-1 Hierarchies should be based on interface classes [AUTOSAR-A10_4_1]
        • Hierarchies should be based on abstract classes [AUTOSAR-A10_4_1-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A11-0-1 A non-POD type should be defined as class [AUTOSAR-A11_0_1]
        • A non-POD type should be defined as class [AUTOSAR-A11_0_1-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A11-0-2 A type defined as struct shall: (1) provide only public data members, (2) not provide any special member functions or methods, (3) not be a base of another struct or class, (4) not inherit from another struct or class [AUTOSAR-A11_0_2]
        • Structs should only contain public data members and should not be a base or inherit [AUTOSAR-A11_0_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A11-3-1 Friend declarations shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A11_3_1]
        • Friend declarations shall not be used except declarations of comparison operators [AUTOSAR-A11_3_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-0-1 If a class declares a copy or move operation, or a destructor, either via "=default", "=delete", or via a user-provided declaration, then all others of these five special member functions shall be declared as well [AUTOSAR-A12_0_1]
        • If a class declares a copy or move operation, or a destructor, either via '=default', '=delete', or via a user-provided declaration, then all others of these five special member functions shall be declared as well [AUTOSAR-A12_0_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-0-2 Bitwise operations and operations that assume data representation in memory shall not be performed on objects [AUTOSAR-A12_0_2]
        • Do not compare objects of a class that may contain padding bits with C standard library functions [AUTOSAR-A12_0_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-1 Constructors shall explicitly initialize all virtual base classes, all direct non-virtual base classes and all non-static data members [AUTOSAR-A12_1_1]
        • All constructors of a class should explicitly call a constructor for all of its immediate base classes and all virtual base classes [AUTOSAR-A12_1_1-a-2]
        • All member variables should be initialized in constructor [AUTOSAR-A12_1_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-2 Both NSDMI and a non-static member initializer in a constructor shall not be used in the same type [AUTOSAR-A12_1_2]
        • Both NSDMI and a non-static member initializer in a constructor shall not be used in the same type [AUTOSAR-A12_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-3 If all user-defined constructors of a class initialize data members with constant values that are the same across all constructors, then data members shall be initialized using NSDMI instead [AUTOSAR-A12_1_3]
        • User-defined constructors that initialize data members with the same constant values across all constructors should initialize using NSDMI instead [AUTOSAR-A12_1_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-4 All constructors that are callable with a single argument of fundamental type shall be declared explicit [AUTOSAR-A12_1_4]
        • All constructors that are callable with a single argument of fundamental type shall be declared explicit [AUTOSAR-A12_1_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-5 Common class initialization for non-constant members shall be done by a delegating constructor [AUTOSAR-A12_1_5]
        • Use delegating constructors to reduce code duplication [AUTOSAR-A12_1_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-1-6 Derived classes that do not need further explicit initialization and require all the constructors from the base class shall use inheriting constructors [AUTOSAR-A12_1_6]
        • Derived classes that do not need further explicit initialization and require all the constructors from the base class shall use inheriting constructors [AUTOSAR-A12_1_6-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-4-1 Destructor of a base class shall be public virtual, public override or protected non-virtual [AUTOSAR-A12_4_1]
        • Make base class destructors public and virtual, or protected and nonvirtual [AUTOSAR-A12_4_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-4-2 If a public destructor of a class is non-virtual, then the class should be declared final [AUTOSAR-A12_4_2]
        • If a public destructor of a class is non-virtual, then the class should be declared final [AUTOSAR-A12_4_2-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A12-6-1 All class data members that are initialized by the constructor shall be initialized using member initializers [AUTOSAR-A12_6_1]
        • Prefer initialization to assignment in constructors [AUTOSAR-A12_6_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-7-1 If the behavior of a user-defined special member function is identical to implicitly defined special member function, then it shall be defined "=default" or be left undefined [AUTOSAR-A12_7_1]
        • Define special members as =default when the behavior is equivalent to the compiler's behavior [AUTOSAR-A12_7_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-1 Move and copy constructors shall move and respectively copy base classes and data members of a class, without any side effects [AUTOSAR-A12_8_1]
        • A copy constructor shall only initialize its base classes and the non-static members of the class of which it is a member [AUTOSAR-A12_8_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-2 User-defined copy and move assignment operators should use user-defined no-throw swap function [AUTOSAR-A12_8_2]
        • User-defined copy and move assignment operators should use user-defined no-throw swap function [AUTOSAR-A12_8_2-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-3 Moved-from object shall not be read-accessed [AUTOSAR-A12_8_3]
        • Do not rely on the value of a moved-from object [AUTOSAR-A12_8_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-4 Move constructor shall not initialize its class members and base classes using copy semantics [AUTOSAR-A12_8_4]
        • Use std::move() on rvalue references and std::forward() on forwarding references [AUTOSAR-A12_8_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-5 A copy assignment and a move assignment operators shall handle self-assignment [AUTOSAR-A12_8_5]
        • Check for assignment to self in operator= [AUTOSAR-A12_8_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-6 Copy and move constructors and copy assignment and move assignment operators shall be declared protected or defined "=delete" in base class [AUTOSAR-A12_8_6]
        • Avoid public copy constructors and assignment operators in base classes [AUTOSAR-A12_8_6-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A12-8-7 Assignment operators should be declared with the ref-qualifier & [AUTOSAR-A12_8_7]
        • Declare assignment operators with the ref-qualifier & [AUTOSAR-A12_8_7-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A13-1-2 User defined suffixes of the user defined literal operators shall start with underscore followed by one or more letters [AUTOSAR-A13_1_2]
        • User defined suffixes of the user defined literal operators shall start with underscore followed by one or more letters [AUTOSAR-A13_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-1-3 User defined literals operators shall only perform conversion of passed parameters [AUTOSAR-A13_1_3]
        • User defined literals operators shall only perform conversion of passed parameters [AUTOSAR-A13_1_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-2-1 An assignment operator shall return a reference to "this" [AUTOSAR-A13_2_1]
        • Have assignment operator returns a reference to *this; make assignment operator's return type a non-const reference to it's class' type [AUTOSAR-A13_2_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-2-2 A binary arithmetic operator and a bitwise operator shall return a "prvalue" [AUTOSAR-A13_2_2]
        • A binary arithmetic operator and a bitwise operator shall return a 'prvalue' [AUTOSAR-A13_2_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-2-3 A relational operator shall return a boolean value [AUTOSAR-A13_2_3]
        • A relational operator shall return a boolean value [AUTOSAR-A13_2_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-3-1 A function that contains "forwarding reference" as its argument shall not be overloaded [AUTOSAR-A13_3_1]
        • Avoid Overloading on Forwarding References [AUTOSAR-A13_3_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-5-1 If "operator[]" is to be overloaded with a non-const version, const version shall also be implemented [AUTOSAR-A13_5_1]
        • When overloading the subscript operator (operator[]), implement both const and non-const versions [AUTOSAR-A13_5_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-5-2 All user-defined conversion operators shall be defined explicit [AUTOSAR-A13_5_2]
        • User-conversion cast operators should be made explicit [AUTOSAR-A13_5_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-5-3 User-defined conversion operators should not be used [AUTOSAR-A13_5_3]
        • Do not use user-defined conversion functions [AUTOSAR-A13_5_3-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A13-5-4 If two opposite operators are defined, one shall be defined in terms of the other [AUTOSAR-A13_5_4]
        • If two opposite equality operators ('==', '!=') are defined in a class, one shall be defined in terms of the other [AUTOSAR-A13_5_4-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-5-5 Comparison operators shall be non-member functions with identical parameter types and noexcept [AUTOSAR-A13_5_5]
        • Comparison operators shall be non-member functions [AUTOSAR-A13_5_5-a-2]
        • Comparison operators shall be non-member functions with identical parameter types and noexcept [AUTOSAR-A13_5_5-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A13-6-1 Digit sequences separators ' shall only be used as follows: (1) for decimal, every 3 digits, (2) for hexadecimal, every 2 digits, (3) for binary, every 4 digits [AUTOSAR-A13_6_1]
        • Digit sequences separators ' shall only be used consistently [AUTOSAR-A13_6_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A14-5-1 A template constructor shall not participate in overload resolution for a single argument of the enclosing class type [AUTOSAR-A14_5_1]
        • A copy constructor shall be declared when there is a template constructor with a single parameter that is a generic parameter [AUTOSAR-A14_5_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A14-5-3 A non-member generic operator shall only be declared in a namespace that does not contain class (struct) type, enum type or union type declarations. [AUTOSAR-A14_5_3]
        • A non-member generic operator shall only be declared in a namespace that does not contain class (struct) type, enum type or union type declarations [AUTOSAR-A14_5_3-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A14-7-2 Template specialization shall be declared in the same file (1) as the primary template (2) as a user-defined type, for which the specialization is declared [AUTOSAR-A14_7_2]
        • Template specialization shall be declared in the same file as the primary template or a user-defined type, for which the specialization is declared [AUTOSAR-A14_7_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A14-8-2 Explicit specializations of function templates shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A14_8_2]
        • Overloaded function templates shall not be explicitly specialized [AUTOSAR-A14_8_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-0-2 At least the basic guarantee for exception safety shall be provided for all operations. In addition, each function may offer either the strong guarantee or the nothrow guarantee [AUTOSAR-A15_0_2]
        • Ensure resources are freed [AUTOSAR-A15_0_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-1-1 Only instances of types derived from std::exception shall be thrown [AUTOSAR-A15_1_1]
        • Only use instances of std::exception for exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_1_1-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A15-1-2 An exception object shall not be a pointer [AUTOSAR-A15_1_2]
        • An exception object should not have pointer type [AUTOSAR-A15_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-1-4 If a function exits with an exception, then before a throw, the function shall place all objects/resources that the function constructed in valid states or it shall delete them [AUTOSAR-A15_1_4]
        • Ensure resources are freed [AUTOSAR-A15_1_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-1-5 Exceptions shall not be thrown across execution boundaries [AUTOSAR-A15_1_5]
        • Do not throw an exception across execution boundaries [AUTOSAR-A15_1_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-2-1 Constructors that are not noexcept shall not be invoked before program startup [AUTOSAR-A15_2_1]
        • Function called in global or namespace scope shall not throw unhandled exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_2_1-a-2]
        • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [AUTOSAR-A15_2_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-3-2 If a function throws an exception, it shall be handled when meaningful actions can be taken, otherwise it shall be propagated [AUTOSAR-A15_3_2]
        • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [AUTOSAR-A15_3_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-3-3 Main function and a task main function shall catch at least: base class exceptions from all third-party libraries used, std::exception and all otherwise unhandled exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_3_3]
        • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_3_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-3-4 Catch-all (ellipsis and std::exception) handlers shall be used only in (a) main, (b) task main functions, (c) in functions that are supposed to isolate independent components and (d) when calling third-party code that uses exceptions not according to AUTOSAR C++14 guidelines [AUTOSAR-A15_3_4]
        • Avoid using catch-all exception handlers [AUTOSAR-A15_3_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-3-5 A class type exception shall be caught by reference or const reference [AUTOSAR-A15_3_5]
        • A class type exception shall always be caught by reference [AUTOSAR-A15_3_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-4-1 Dynamic exception-specification shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A15_4_1]
        • Do not use throw exception specifications [AUTOSAR-A15_4_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-4-2 If a function is declared to be noexcept, noexcept(true) or noexcept(), then it shall not exit with an exception [AUTOSAR-A15_4_2]
        • Avoid throwing exceptions from functions that are declared not to throw [AUTOSAR-A15_4_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-4-3 The noexcept specification of a function shall either be identical across all translation units, or identical or more restrictive between a virtual member function and an overrider [AUTOSAR-A15_4_3]
        • If a function is declared with an exception-specification, then all declarations of the same function (in other translation units) shall be declared with the same set of type-ids [AUTOSAR-A15_4_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-4-4 A declaration of non-throwing function shall contain noexcept specification [AUTOSAR-A15_4_4]
        • Declare functions 'noexcept' if they will not emit exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_4_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-4-5 Checked exceptions that could be thrown from a function shall be specified together with the function declaration and they shall be identical in all function declarations and for all its overriders [AUTOSAR-A15_4_5]
        • Checked exceptions that could be thrown from a function shall be specified in the comment directly before the function declaration [AUTOSAR-A15_4_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-5-1 All user-provided class destructors, deallocation functions, move constructors, move assignment operators and swap functions shall not exit with an exception. A noexcept exception specification shall be added to these functions as appropriate [AUTOSAR-A15_5_1]
        • Never allow an exception to be thrown from a destructor, deallocation, and swap [AUTOSAR-A15_5_1-a-2]
        • All user-provided move constructors and move assignment operators shall not exit with an exception [AUTOSAR-A15_5_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-5-2 Program shall not be abruptly terminated. In particular, an implicit or explicit invocation of std::abort(), std::quick_exit(), std::_Exit(), std::terminate() shall not be done [AUTOSAR-A15_5_2]
        • The execution of a function registered with 'std::atexit()' or 'std::at_quick_exit()' should not exit via an exception [AUTOSAR-A15_5_2-a-2]
        • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A15_5_2-b-2]
        • The 'quick_exit()' and '_Exit()' functions from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A15_5_2-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A15-5-3 The std::terminate() function shall not be called implicitly [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3]
        • The execution of a function registered with 'std::atexit()' or 'std::at_quick_exit()' should not exit via an exception [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-a-2]
        • Never allow an exception to be thrown from a destructor, deallocation, and swap [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-b-2]
        • Do not throw from within destructor [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-c-2]
        • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-d-2]
        • An empty throw (throw;) shall only be used in the compound-statement of a catch handler [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-e-2]
        • Exceptions shall be raised only after start-up and before termination of the program [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-f-2]
        • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-g-2]
        • Where a function's declaration includes an exception-specification, the function shall only be capable of throwing exceptions of the indicated type(s) [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-h-2]
        • Function called in global or namespace scope shall not throw unhandled exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-i-2]
        • Always catch exceptions [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-j-2]
        • Properly define exit handlers [AUTOSAR-A15_5_3-k-2]
      • AUTOSAR A16-0-1 The pre-processor shall only be used for unconditional and conditional file inclusion and include guards, and using the following directives: (1) #ifndef, (2) #ifdef, (3) #if, (4) #if defined, (5) #elif, (6) #else, (7) #define, (8) #endif, (9) #include [AUTOSAR-A16_0_1]
        • The #ifndef, #ifdef, #if, #elif, #else, and #endif pre-processor directives shall only be used for conditional file inclusion and include guards [AUTOSAR-A16_0_1-a-2]
        • #error directive shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A16_0_1-b-2]
        • The #pragma directive shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A16_0_1-c-2]

        • #undef shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A16_0_1-e-2]

        • Reserved identifiers, macros and functions in the standard library, shall not be defined, redefined or undefined (C99 code) [AUTOSAR-A17_0_1-b-2]
        • Reserved identifiers, macros and functions in the standard library, shall not be defined, redefined or undefined (C90 code) [AUTOSAR-A17_0_1-c-2]

        • The C library shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A18_0_1-a-2]

      • AUTOSAR A18-5-10 Placement new shall be used only with properly aligned pointers to sufficient storage capacity [AUTOSAR-A18_5_10]

        • Always provide empty brackets ([]) for delete when deallocating arrays [AUTOSAR-A18_5_3-b-2]

      • AUTOSAR A18-5-4 If a project has sized or unsized version of operator "delete" globally defined, then both sized and unsized versions shall be defined [AUTOSAR-A18_5_4]

      • AUTOSAR A18-5-5 Memory management functions shall ensure the following: (a) deterministic behavior resulting with the existence of worst-case execution time, (b) avoiding memory fragmentation, (c) avoid running out of memory, (d) avoiding mismatched allocations or deallocations, (e) no dependence on non-deterministic calls to kernel [AUTOSAR-A18_5_5]
        • Use the same form in corresponding calls to new/malloc and delete/free [AUTOSAR-A18_5_5-a-2]
        • Freed memory shouldn't be accessed under any circumstances [AUTOSAR-A18_5_5-b-2]
        • Properly define new handlers [AUTOSAR-A18_5_5-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A18-5-8 Objects that do not outlive a function shall have automatic storage duration [AUTOSAR-A18_5_8]

        • The 'std::move' function should be used to forward rvalue references [AUTOSAR-A18_9_2-b-2]

      • AUTOSAR A2-13-2 String literals with different encoding prefixes shall not be concatenated [AUTOSAR-A2_13_2]
        • String literals with different encoding prefixes shall not be concatenated [AUTOSAR-A2_13_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-13-3 Type wchar_t shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_13_3]
        • Type wchar_t shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_13_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-13-4 String literals shall not be assigned to non-constant pointers [AUTOSAR-A2_13_4]
        • A string literal shall not be modified [AUTOSAR-A2_13_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-13-5 Hexadecimal constants should be upper case [AUTOSAR-A2_13_5]
        • Hexadecimal constants will be represented using all uppercase letters [AUTOSAR-A2_13_5-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A2-13-6 Universal character names shall be used only inside character or string literals [AUTOSAR-A2_13_6]
        • Universal character names shall be used only inside character or string literals [AUTOSAR-A2_13_6-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-3-1 Only those characters specified in the C++ Language Standard basic source character set shall be used in the source code [AUTOSAR-A2_3_1]
        • Only use characters defined in the ISO C standard [AUTOSAR-A2_3_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-5-1 Trigraphs shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_5_1]
        • Trigraphs shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_5_1-a-2]
        • Trigraphs shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_5_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-5-2 Digraphs shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A2_5_2]
        • Do not use the following digraphs: <%, %>, <:, :>, %:, %:%: [AUTOSAR-A2_5_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-7-1 The character \ shall not occur as a last character of a C++ comment [AUTOSAR-A2_7_1]
        • Line-splicing shall not be used in // comments [AUTOSAR-A2_7_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-7-2 Sections of code shall not be "commented out" [AUTOSAR-A2_7_2]
        • Sections of code should not be "commented out" [AUTOSAR-A2_7_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-7-3 All declarations of "user-defined" types, static and non-static data members, functions and methods shall be preceded by documentation using "///" comments and "@tag" tags [AUTOSAR-A2_7_3]
        • All declarations of types, data members, and functions should be preceded by a comment annotated with the '@brief' tag [AUTOSAR-A2_7_3-a-2]
        • Function parameters and return type should be documented in a comment that precedes the function declaration [AUTOSAR-A2_7_3-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A2-8-1 A header file name shall be identical to a type name declared in it if it declares a type [AUTOSAR-A2_8_1]
        • An include file for a class should have a file name of the form <class name> + extension [AUTOSAR-A2_8_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-1 It shall be possible to include any header file in multiple translation units without violating the One Definition Rule [AUTOSAR-A3_1_1]
        • Don't define entities with linkage in a header file [AUTOSAR-A3_1_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-2 Header files, that are defined locally in the project, shall have a file name extension of one of: ".h", ".hpp" or ".hxx" [AUTOSAR-A3_1_2]
        • Header files should have a file extension of: ".h", ".hpp" or ".hxx" [AUTOSAR-A3_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-3 Implementation files, that are defined locally in the project, should have a file name extension of ".cpp" [AUTOSAR-A3_1_3]
        • Implementation files in C++ will always have a file name extension of ".cpp" [AUTOSAR-A3_1_3-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-4 When an array with external linkage is declared, its size shall be stated explicitly [AUTOSAR-A3_1_4]
        • When an array is declared with external linkage, its size shall be stated explicitly or defined implicitly by initialisation [AUTOSAR-A3_1_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-5 A function definition shall only be placed in a class definition if (1) the function is intended to be inlined (2) it is a member function template (3) it is a member function of a class template [AUTOSAR-A3_1_5]
        • A function definition should not be placed in a class specification unless the function is intended to be inlined [AUTOSAR-A3_1_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-1-6 Trivial accessor and mutator functions should be inlined [AUTOSAR-A3_1_6]
        • Trivial accessor and mutator functions should be inlined [AUTOSAR-A3_1_6-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A3-3-1 Objects or functions with external linkage (including members of named namespaces) shall be declared in a header file [AUTOSAR-A3_3_1]
        • Objects or functions with external linkage shall be declared in a header file [AUTOSAR-A3_3_1-a-2]
        • Don't define entities with linkage in a header file [AUTOSAR-A3_3_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-3-2 Static and thread-local objects shall be constant-initialized [AUTOSAR-A3_3_2]
        • Static and thread-local objects shall be constant-initialized [AUTOSAR-A3_3_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-8-1 An object shall not be accessed outside of its lifetime [AUTOSAR-A3_8_1]
        • Do not use resources that have been freed [AUTOSAR-A3_8_1-a-2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be returned from a function [AUTOSAR-A3_8_1-b-2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be assigned to another object that may persist after the first object has ceased to exist [AUTOSAR-A3_8_1-c-2]
        • Do not point to a wrapped object that has been freed [AUTOSAR-A3_8_1-d-2]
      • AUTOSAR A3-9-1 Fixed width integer types from , indicating the size and signedness, shall be used in place of the basic numerical types [AUTOSAR-A3_9_1]
        • Fixed width integer types from <cstdint>, indicating the size and signedness, shall be used in place of the basic numerical types [AUTOSAR-A3_9_1-b-2]
        • A typedef should be used in place of the plain char type [AUTOSAR-A3_9_1-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A4-10-1 Only nullptr literal shall be used as the null-pointer-constant [AUTOSAR-A4_10_1]
        • NULL shall not be used as an integer value [AUTOSAR-A4_10_1-a-2]
        • Prefer 'nullptr' over 'NULL' or '0'(zero) [AUTOSAR-A4_10_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A4-5-1 Expressions with type enum or enum class shall not be used as operands to built-in and overloaded operators other than the subscript operator [ ], the assignment operator =, the equality operators == and !=, the unary & operator, and the relational operators <, <=, >, >= [AUTOSAR-A4_5_1]
        • Expressions with type enum shall not be used as operands to built-in operators other than  [ ],  =, ==, !=, <, <=, >, >=, and the unary & operator [AUTOSAR-A4_5_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A4-7-1 An integer expression shall not lead to data loss [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1]
        • Avoid implicit conversions from signed to unsigned type [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-a-2]
        • Implicit conversions from integral constant to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-b-2]
        • Avoid conversions of constant values to a narrower type [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-c-2]
        • Implicit conversions from wider to narrower integral type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-d-2]
        • Avoid implicit conversions from wider to narrower floating type [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-e-2]
        • Avoid implicit conversions from floating to integral type [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-f-2]
        • Implicit conversions from integral to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-g-2]
        • Avoid wraparounds when performing arithmetic integer operations [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-h-2]
        • Avoid data loss when converting between integer types [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-i-2]
        • Avoid signed integer overflows [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-j-2]
        • Avoid value change when converting between integer types [AUTOSAR-A4_7_1-k-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-0-1 The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function calls [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-a-2]
        • Do not use more than one volatile between two adjacent sequence points [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-b-2]
        • Between sequence points an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-c-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of expression that involves a function call [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-d-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function designator and function arguments [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-e-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function arguments [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-f-2]
        • The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [AUTOSAR-A5_0_1-g-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-0-2 The condition of an if-statement and the condition of an iteration statement shall have type bool [AUTOSAR-A5_0_2]
        • The condition of an if-statement and the condition of an iteration-statement shall have type bool [AUTOSAR-A5_0_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-0-3 The declaration of objects shall contain no more than two levels of pointer indirection [AUTOSAR-A5_0_3]
        • The declaration of objects should contain no more than 2 levels of pointer indirection [AUTOSAR-A5_0_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-0-4 Pointer arithmetic shall not be used with pointers to non-final classes [AUTOSAR-A5_0_4]
        • Don't treat arrays polymorphically [AUTOSAR-A5_0_4-a-2]
        • A pointer to an array of derived class objects should not be converted to a base class pointer [AUTOSAR-A5_0_4-b-2]
        • Do not treat arrays polymorphically [AUTOSAR-A5_0_4-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-10-1 A pointer to member virtual function shall only be tested for equality with null-pointer-constant [AUTOSAR-A5_10_1]
        • A pointer to member virtual function shall only be tested for equality with null-pointer-constant [AUTOSAR-A5_10_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-16-1 The ternary conditional operator shall not be used as a sub-expression [AUTOSAR-A5_16_1]
        • The conditional operator should not be used as a sub-expression [AUTOSAR-A5_16_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-1 Literal values shall not be used apart from type initialization, otherwise symbolic names shall be used instead [AUTOSAR-A5_1_1]
        • Avoid magic numbers [AUTOSAR-A5_1_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-2 Variables shall not be implicitly captured in a lambda expression [AUTOSAR-A5_1_2]
        • Avoid default capture modes [AUTOSAR-A5_1_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-3 Parameter list (possibly empty) shall be included in every lambda expression [AUTOSAR-A5_1_3]
        • Include a parameter list in every lambda expression [AUTOSAR-A5_1_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-4 A lambda expression object shall not outlive any of its reference-captured objects [AUTOSAR-A5_1_4]
        • Never return lambdas that capture local objects by reference [AUTOSAR-A5_1_4-a-2]
        • Never capture local objects from an outer lambda by reference [AUTOSAR-A5_1_4-b-2]
        • The lambda that captures local objects by reference should not be assigned to the variable with a greater lifetime [AUTOSAR-A5_1_4-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-6 Return type of a non-void return type lambda expression should be explicitly specified [AUTOSAR-A5_1_6]
        • Return type of a non-void return type lambda expression should be explicitly specified [AUTOSAR-A5_1_6-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-7 A lambda shall not be an operand to decltype or typeid [AUTOSAR-A5_1_7]
        • A lambda shall not be an operand to typeid [AUTOSAR-A5_1_7-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-1-8 Lambda expressions should not be defined inside another lambda expression [AUTOSAR-A5_1_8]
        • Lambda expressions should not be defined inside another lambda expression [AUTOSAR-A5_1_8-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-1 dynamic_cast should not be used [AUTOSAR-A5_2_1]
        • Avoid dynamic_casts [AUTOSAR-A5_2_1-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-2 Traditional C-style casts shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A5_2_2]
        • C-style casts should not be used [AUTOSAR-A5_2_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-3 A cast shall not remove any const or volatile qualification from the type of a pointer or reference [AUTOSAR-A5_2_3]
        • A cast shall not remove any 'const' or 'volatile' qualification from the type of a pointer or reference [AUTOSAR-A5_2_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-4 reinterpret_cast shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A5_2_4]
        • Avoid using reinterpret_cast [AUTOSAR-A5_2_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-5 An array or container shall not be accessed beyond its range [AUTOSAR-A5_2_5]
        • Avoid accessing arrays out of bounds [AUTOSAR-A5_2_5-a-2]
        • Avoid accessing arrays and pointers out of bounds [AUTOSAR-A5_2_5-b-2]
        • A pointer operand and any pointer resulting from pointer arithmetic using that operand shall both address elements of the same array [AUTOSAR-A5_2_5-c-2]
        • Avoid tainted data in array indexes [AUTOSAR-A5_2_5-d-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-2-6 The operands of a logical && or || shall be parenthesized if the operands contain binary operators [AUTOSAR-A5_2_6]
        • The operands of a logical && or || shall be parenthesized if the operands contain binary operators [AUTOSAR-A5_2_6-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-3-1 Evaluation of the operand to the typeid operator shall not contain side effects [AUTOSAR-A5_3_1]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain any expression that has side effects [AUTOSAR-A5_3_1-a-2]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain a function call that causes side effects [AUTOSAR-A5_3_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-3-2 Null pointers shall not be dereferenced [AUTOSAR-A5_3_2]
        • Avoid null pointer dereferencing [AUTOSAR-A5_3_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-3-3 Pointers to incomplete class types shall not be deleted [AUTOSAR-A5_3_3]
        • Do not delete objects with incomplete class at the point of deletion [AUTOSAR-A5_3_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-5-1 A pointer to member shall not access non-existent class members [AUTOSAR-A5_5_1]
        • A cast shall not convert a pointer to a function to any other pointer type, including a pointer to function type [AUTOSAR-A5_5_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A5-6-1 The right hand operand of the integer division or remainder operators shall not be equal to zero [AUTOSAR-A5_6_1]
        • Avoid division by zero [AUTOSAR-A5_6_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-2-1 Move and copy assignment operators shall either move or respectively copy base classes and data members of a class, without any side effects [AUTOSAR-A6_2_1]
        • Copy assignment operators should not have side effects that could affect copying the object [AUTOSAR-A6_2_1-a-2]
        • Move assignment operators should not have side effects that could affect moving the object [AUTOSAR-A6_2_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-2-2 Expression statements shall not be explicit calls to constructors of temporary objects only [AUTOSAR-A6_2_2]
        • Expression statements shall not be explicit calls to constructors of temporary objects only [AUTOSAR-A6_2_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-4-1 A switch statement shall have at least two case-clauses, distinct from the default label [AUTOSAR-A6_4_1]
        • Every switch statement will have at least two cases and a potential default [AUTOSAR-A6_4_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-5-1 A for-loop that loops through all elements of the container and does not use its loop-counter shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A6_5_1]
        • A for-loop that loops through all elements of the container and does not use its loop-counter shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A6_5_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-5-2 A for loop shall contain a single loop-counter which shall not have floating-point type [AUTOSAR-A6_5_2]
        • A for loop shall contain a single loop-counter which shall not have floating type [AUTOSAR-A6_5_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A6-5-3 Do statements should not be used [AUTOSAR-A6_5_3]
        • 'Do' statements should not be used except in a function-like macro [AUTOSAR-A6_5_3-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A6-5-4 For-init-statement and expression should not perform actions other than loop-counter initialization and modification [AUTOSAR-A6_5_4]
        • The initialization expression in a for loop will perform no actions other than to initialize the value of a single for loop parameter [AUTOSAR-A6_5_4-a-4]
        • The increment expression in a for loop will perform no action other than to change a single loop parameter to the next value for the loop [AUTOSAR-A6_5_4-b-4]
      • AUTOSAR A6-6-1 The goto statement shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A6_6_1]
        • The goto statement shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A6_6_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-1 Constexpr or const specifiers shall be used for immutable data declaration [AUTOSAR-A7_1_1]
        • Declare local variable as const whenever possible [AUTOSAR-A7_1_1-a-2]
        • Declare parameters as const whenever possible [AUTOSAR-A7_1_1-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-2 The constexpr specifier shall be used for values that can be determined at compile time [AUTOSAR-A7_1_2]
        • Use constexpr to declare const variables whenever possible [AUTOSAR-A7_1_2-a-2]
        • Use constexpr to declare functions whenever possible [AUTOSAR-A7_1_2-b-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-3 CV-qualifiers shall be placed on the right hand side of the type that is a typedef or a using name [AUTOSAR-A7_1_3]
        • CV-qualifiers shall be placed on the right hand side of the type that is a typedef or a using name [AUTOSAR-A7_1_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-4 The register keyword shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A7_1_4]
        • The 'register' storage class specifier shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A7_1_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-5 The auto specifier shall not be used apart from following cases: (1) to declare that a variable has the same type as return type of a function call, (2) to declare that a variable has the same type as initializer of non-fundamental type, (3) to declare parameters of a generic lambda expression, (4) to declare a function template using trailing return type syntax [AUTOSAR-A7_1_5]
        • Do not overuse 'auto' specifier [AUTOSAR-A7_1_5-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-6 The typedef specifier shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A7_1_6]
        • Prefer alias declarations to typedefs [AUTOSAR-A7_1_6-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-7 Each expression statement and identifier declaration shall be placed on a separate line [AUTOSAR-A7_1_7]
        • Only one statement shall be allowed per line [AUTOSAR-A7_1_7-a-2]
        • Multiple variable declarations shall not be allowed on the same line [AUTOSAR-A7_1_7-b-2]
        • Each variable should be declared in a separate declaration statement [AUTOSAR-A7_1_7-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-8 A non-type specifier shall be placed before a type specifier in a declaration [AUTOSAR-A7_1_8]
        • Do not place type specifiers before non-type specifiers in a declaration [AUTOSAR-A7_1_8-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-1-9 A class, structure, or enumeration shall not be declared in the definition of its type [AUTOSAR-A7_1_9]
        • A class, structure, or enumeration will not be declared in the definition of its type [AUTOSAR-A7_1_9-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-2-1 An expression with enum underlying type shall only have values corresponding to the enumerators of the enumeration [AUTOSAR-A7_2_1]
        • An expression with enum underlying type shall only have values corresponding to the enumerators of the enumeration [AUTOSAR-A7_2_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-2-2 Enumeration underlying base type shall be explicitly defined [AUTOSAR-A7_2_2]
        • Use an explicit enumeration base and ensure that it is large enough to store all enumerators [AUTOSAR-A7_2_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-2-3 Enumerations shall be declared as scoped enum classes [AUTOSAR-A7_2_3]
        • Prefer Scoped Enums to Unscoped Enums [AUTOSAR-A7_2_3-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-2-4 In an enumeration, either (1) none, (2) the first or (3) all enumerators shall be initialized [AUTOSAR-A7_2_4]
        • In an enumerator list, the "=" construct shall not be used to explicitly initialise members other than the first, unless all items are explicitly initialised [AUTOSAR-A7_2_4-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-2-5 Enumerations should be used to represent sets of related named constants [AUTOSAR-A7_2_5]
        • Enumeration types shall be used instead of integer types (and constants) as case labels [AUTOSAR-A7_2_5-a-4]
      • AUTOSAR A7-3-1 All overloads of a function shall be visible from where it is called [AUTOSAR-A7_3_1]
        • Member functions declared in derived class should not hide functions declared in base classes [AUTOSAR-A7_3_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A7-4-1 The asm declaration shall not be used [AUTOSAR-A7_4_1]

        • Functions shall not call themselves, either directly or indirectly [AUTOSAR-A7_5_2-a-2]

        • Never return from functions that should not return [AUTOSAR-A7_6_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-2-1 When declaring function templates, the trailing return type syntax shall be used if the return type depends on the type of parameters [AUTOSAR-A8_2_1]

      • AUTOSAR A8-4-1 Functions shall not be defined using the ellipsis notation [AUTOSAR-A8_4_1]
        • Do not use functions with variable numbers of arguments [AUTOSAR-A8_4_1-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-10 A parameter shall be passed by reference if it can't be NULL [AUTOSAR-A8_4_10]
        • A parameter shall be passed by reference if it can't be NULL [AUTOSAR-A8_4_10-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-11 A smart pointer shall only be used as a parameter type if it expresses lifetime semantics [AUTOSAR-A8_4_11]
        • A smart pointer shall only be used as a parameter type if it expresses lifetime semantics [AUTOSAR-A8_4_11-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-12 A std::unique_ptr shall be passed to a function as: (1) a copy to express the function assumes ownership (2) an lvalue reference to express that the function replaces the managed object [AUTOSAR-A8_4_12]
        • Do not pass std::unique_ptr by const reference [AUTOSAR-A8_4_12-a-2]
        • A smart pointer shall only be used as a parameter type if it expresses lifetime semantics [AUTOSAR-A8_4_12-b-2]
        • A parameter should only be declared as a non-const lvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' if the function replaces the managed object [AUTOSAR-A8_4_12-c-2]
        • Do not declare the type of a parameter as an rvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' [AUTOSAR-A8_4_12-d-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-13 A std::shared_ptr shall be passed to a function as: (1) a copy to express the function shares ownership (2) an lvalue reference to express that the function replaces the managed object (3) a const lvalue reference to express that the function retains a reference count [AUTOSAR-A8_4_13]
        • A smart pointer shall only be used as a parameter type if it expresses lifetime semantics [AUTOSAR-A8_4_13-a-2]
        • A parameter should only be declared as a non-const lvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' if the function replaces the managed object [AUTOSAR-A8_4_13-b-2]
        • Do not declare the type of a parameter as an rvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' [AUTOSAR-A8_4_13-c-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-2 All exit paths from a function with non-void return type shall have an explicit return statement with an expression [AUTOSAR-A8_4_2]
        • All exit paths from a function, except main(), with non-void return type shall have an explicit return statement with an expression [AUTOSAR-A8_4_2-a-2]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-3 Common ways of passing parameters should be used [AUTOSAR-A8_4_3]
        • A parameter of a type that is not 'cheap to copy' should be passed by reference [AUTOSAR-A8_4_3-a-4]
        • Declare reference parameters as const references whenever possible [AUTOSAR-A8_4_3-b-4]
      • AUTOSAR A8-4-4 Multiple output values from a function should be returned as a struct or tuple [AUTOSAR-A8_4_4]
        • Multiple output values from a function should be returned as a struct or tuple [AUTOSAR-A8_4_4-a-4]

    • Flow Analysis [BD]
      • Incorrect API usage [BD-API]
        • Do not pass incorrect values to library functions [BD-API-BADPARAM-1]
        • Do not pass incorrect values to ctype.h library functions [BD-API-CTYPE-2]
        • Do not pass negative values to functions expecting non-negative arguments [BD-API-NEGPARAM-1]
        • Do not pass 0 value as a size argument to the realloc function [BD-API-REALLOC-2]
        • Do not check for a non-negative value after passing as a non-negative argument [BD-API-REVNEGPARAM-2]
        • The size_t argument passed to any function in string.h shall have an appropriate value [BD-API-STRSIZE-2]
        • Validate values passed to library functions [BD-API-VALPARAM-2]
      • Containers [BD-CO]
        • Do not pass empty container iterators to std algorithms as destinations [BD-CO-EMPCON-2]
        • Do not compare iterators from different containers [BD-CO-ITINVCOMP-2]
        • Do not modify container while iterating over it [BD-CO-ITMOD-2]
        • Do not access iterator out of range [BD-CO-ITOUT-1]
        • Use valid references, pointers, and iterators to reference elements of a basic_string [BD-CO-STRMOD-1]
      • Miscellaneous [BD-MISC]
        • Prevent calling unsafe functions (custom rule) [BD-MISC-DC-5]
        • Always close transactions [BD-MISC-TRANS-1]
      • Possible Bugs [BD-PB]
        • Avoid accessing arrays out of bounds [BD-PB-ARRAY-2]
        • A pointer pointing to an element of an array of objects shall not be passed to a smart pointer of single object type [BD-PB-ARRPTR-2]
        • Avoid incorrect shift operations [BD-PB-BADSHIFT-2]
        • Use the correct byte ordering when transferring data between systems [BD-PB-BYTEORD-2]
        • Avoid conditions that always evaluate to the same value [BD-PB-CC-2]
        • Consistently check the returned value of non-void functions [BD-PB-CHECKRET-2]
        • Always check the returned value of non-void function [BD-PB-CHECKRETGEN-2]
        • Do not check for null after dereferencing [BD-PB-DEREF-2]
        • Do not modify the alignment of objects by calling realloc() [BD-PB-DNMPTR-2]
        • The macro EOF should be compared with the unmodified return value from the Standard Library function [BD-PB-EOFCOMP-2]
        • Properly use errno value [BD-PB-ERRNO-2]
        • Always catch exceptions [BD-PB-EXCEPT-1]
        • Properly define exit handlers [BD-PB-EXITHAN-2]
        • Reset strings on fgets() or fgetws() failure [BD-PB-FGETS-2]
        • Only use values for fsetpos() that are returned from fgetpos() [BD-PB-FSETPOS-2]
        • Avoid infinite recursion [BD-PB-INFREC-2]
        • Avoid data loss when converting between integer types [BD-PB-INTDL-2]
        • Avoid integer overflows [BD-PB-INTOVERF-3]
        • Avoid signed integer overflows [BD-PB-INTUB-1]
        • Avoid value change when converting between integer types [BD-PB-INTVC-3]
        • Avoid wraparounds when performing arithmetic integer operations [BD-PB-INTWRAP-3]
        • Do not rely on an environment pointer following an operation that may invalidate it [BD-PB-INVENV-2]
        • Pointers returned by certain Standard Library functions should not be used following a subsequent call to the same or related function [BD-PB-INVRET-2]
        • Do not use an object after its lifetime has ended [BD-PB-LIFETIME-2]
        • The Standard Library function memcmp shall not be used to compare null terminated strings [BD-PB-MCCSTR-2]
        • Avoid calls to memory-setting functions that can be optimized out by the compiler [BD-PB-MEMOPT-2]
        • Do not modify string literals [BD-PB-MODSTR-1]

        • Do not read the value of a non-active union field [BD-PB-NAUNF-1]

        • Avoid throwing exceptions from functions that are declared not to throw [BD-PB-NOEXCEPT-2]
        • Declare non-returning functions with the attribute that specifies that they do not return [BD-PB-NORETDECL-2]
        • Never return from functions that should not return [BD-PB-NORETURN-2]
        • Avoid use before initialization [BD-PB-NOTINIT-1]
        • Atomic objects shall be properly initialized before being accessed [BD-PB-NOTINITAT-1]
        • Avoid null pointer dereferencing [BD-PB-NP-1]
        • Ensure strings are zero terminated [BD-PB-NZTS-3]

        • Avoid overflow due to reading a not zero terminated string [BD-PB-OVERFNZT-1]
        • Avoid overflow when reading from a buffer [BD-PB-OVERFRD-1]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [BD-PB-OVERFWR-1]
        • An object shall not be assigned or copied to an overlapping object [BD-PB-OVERLAP-2]
        • Ensure the output buffer is large enough when using path manipulation functions [BD-PB-PATHBUF-3]
        • Do not treat arrays polymorphically [BD-PB-POLARR-2]
        • Avoid overwriting method parameters [BD-PB-POVR-1]
        • A pointer operand and any pointer resulting from pointer arithmetic using that operand shall both address elements of the same array [BD-PB-PTRARR-2]
        • Do not compare two unrelated pointers [BD-PB-PTRCMP-2]
        • Do not subtract two pointers that do not address elements of the same array [BD-PB-PTRSUB-2]
        • Do not store an already-owned pointer value in an unrelated smart pointer [BD-PB-PTRVALUE-2]
        • Do not call putenv() with a pointer to an automatic variable as the argument [BD-PB-PUTENV-2]
        • Do not use recursion [BD-PB-RECFUN-5]
        • A parameter shall be passed by reference if it can't be NULL [BD-PB-REFPARAM-3]
        • Properly define signal handlers [BD-PB-SIGHAN-2]
        • Do not return from a computational exception signal handler [BD-PB-SIGRETURN-2]
        • Always throw the created std::exception object [BD-PB-STDEXC-3]
        • Suspicious setting of stream flags [BD-PB-STREAMFLAGS-3]
        • Restore stream format [BD-PB-STREAMFMT-3]
        • Do not alternately input and output from a stream without an intervening flush or positioning call [BD-PB-STREAMINOUT-2]

        • Do not rely on the value of a moved-from object [BD-PB-SUBSEQMOVE-2]

        • Properly define terminate handlers [BD-PB-TERMHAN-2]
        • Avoid unreachable methods [BD-PB-UCMETH-4]
        • Properly define unexpected handlers [BD-PB-UNEXPHAN-2]
        • Do not use the ungetc function on a stream with the file position indicator zero [BD-PB-UNGETC-2]
        • Guarantee that container indices are within the valid range [BD-PB-VALRANGE-4]
        • Use macros for variable arguments correctly [BD-PB-VARARGS-3]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under construction [BD-PB-VCTOR-2]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under destruction [BD-PB-VDTOR-2]
        • Ensure the size of the variable length array is in valid range [BD-PB-VLASIZE-2]
        • Avoid unused values [BD-PB-VOVR-3]
        • Do not point to a wrapped object that has been freed [BD-PB-WRAPESC-1]
        • The same file shall not be opened for read and write access at the same time on different streams [BD-PB-WRRDSTR-2]
        • Avoid writing to a stream which has been opened as read only [BD-PB-WRROS-2]
        • Avoid division by zero [BD-PB-ZERO-1]

      • Threads & Synchronization [BD-TRS]
        • Declare objects shared between POSIX threads with appropriate storage durations [BD-TRS-ARG-2]
        • Use locks to prevent race conditions when modifying bit fields [BD-TRS-BITLOCK-3]
        • Make const member functions thread-safe [BD-TRS-CMF-2]
        • Variable should be used in context of single critical section [BD-TRS-DIFCS-2]
        • Avoid double locking [BD-TRS-DLOCK-1]
        • Do not destroy another thread's mutex [BD-TRS-DSTRLOCK-3]
        • Avoid race conditions when using fork and file descriptors [BD-TRS-FORKFILE-1]
        • Avoid race conditions while accessing files [BD-TRS-FRC-2]
        • Do not join or detach a thread that was previously joined or detached [BD-TRS-JOINDETACH-2]
        • Do not abandon unreleased locks [BD-TRS-LOCK-1]
        • Do not use global variable with different locks set [BD-TRS-MLOCK-1]
        • Do not acquire locks in different order [BD-TRS-ORDER-1]
        • Do not release a lock that has not been acquired [BD-TRS-REVLOCK-3]
        • Avoid race conditions while checking for the existence of a symbolic link [BD-TRS-SYMLINK-1]
        • There shall be no data races between threads [BD-TRS-THRDR-3]
        • A thread synchronization object should not be destroyed by a thread [BD-TRS-THRDSTR-3]
        • A thread synchronization object should not be initialized by a thread [BD-TRS-THRINIT-3]
        • A thread should not be created by another thread [BD-TRS-THRTHR-3]
        • A thread-specific storage should not be created by a thread [BD-TRS-THRTSS-3]
        • The Standard Library function mtx_timedlock() shall not be invoked on a mutex that does not support timeout [BD-TRS-TIMEDLOCK-2]
        • Do not use blocking functions while holding a lock [BD-TRS-TSHL-1]

    • SEI CERT C [CERT_C]
      • CERT-API00_C (REC) Functions should validate their parameters [CERT_C-API00]

      • CERT-ARR38_C (RULE) Guarantee that library functions do not form invalid pointers [CERT_C-ARR38]
        • Avoid overflow when reading from a buffer [CERT_C-ARR38-a-1]

        • Pointer arithmetic should not be used [CERT_C-ARR39-b-2]
        • Do not add or subtract a scaled integer to a pointer [CERT_C-ARR39-c-2]
      • CERT-CON01_C (REC) Acquire and release synchronization primitives in the same module, at the same level of abstraction [CERT_C-CON01]

      • CERT-CON38_C (RULE) Preserve thread safety and liveness when using condition variables [CERT_C-CON38]
        • Use the 'cnd_signal()' function with a unique condition variable [CERT_C-CON38-a-3]
      • CERT-CON39_C (RULE) Do not join or detach a thread that was previously joined or detached [CERT_C-CON39]
        • Do not join or detach a thread that was previously joined or detached [CERT_C-CON39-a-2]
      • CERT-CON40_C (RULE) Do not refer to an atomic variable twice in an expression [CERT_C-CON40]
        • Do not refer to an atomic variable twice in an expression [CERT_C-CON40-a-2]

        • Wrap functions that can fail spuriously in a loop [CERT_C-CON41-a-3]
      • CERT-CON43_C (RULE) Do not allow data races in multithreaded code [CERT_C-CON43]
        • Do not use global variable with different locks set [CERT_C-CON43-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL00_C (REC) Const-qualify immutable objects [CERT_C-DCL00]
        • Declare local variable as const whenever possible [CERT_C-DCL00-a-3]
        • Declare parameters as const whenever possible [CERT_C-DCL00-b-3]
      • CERT-DCL01_C (REC) Do not reuse variable names in subscopes [CERT_C-DCL01]
        • Identifier declared in a local or function prototype scope shall not hide an identifier declared in a global or namespace scope [CERT_C-DCL01-a-3]
        • Identifiers declared in an inner local scope should not hide identifiers declared in an outer local scope [CERT_C-DCL01-b-3]
      • CERT-DCL02_C (REC) Use visually distinct identifiers [CERT_C-DCL02]
        • Use visually distinct identifiers [CERT_C-DCL02-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL04_C (REC) Do not declare more than one variable per declaration [CERT_C-DCL04]
        • Each variable should be declared in a separate declaration statement [CERT_C-DCL04-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL05_C (REC) Use typedefs of non-pointer types only [CERT_C-DCL05]
        • Declare a type of parameter as typedef to pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [CERT_C-DCL05-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL06_C (REC) Use meaningful symbolic constants to represent literal values [CERT_C-DCL06]
        • Use meaningful symbolic constants to represent literal values [CERT_C-DCL06-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL10_C (REC) Maintain the contract between the writer and caller of variadic functions [CERT_C-DCL10]
        • The number of format specifiers in the format string and the number of corresponding arguments in the invocation of a string formatting function should be equal [CERT_C-DCL10-a-2]
      • CERT-DCL11_C (REC) Understand the type issues associated with variadic functions [CERT_C-DCL11]
        • There should be no mismatch between the '%s' and '%c' format specifiers in the format string and their corresponding arguments in the invocation of a string formatting function [CERT_C-DCL11-a-2]
        • There should be no mismatch between the '%f' format specifier in the format string and its corresponding argument in the invocation of a string formatting function [CERT_C-DCL11-b-2]
        • There should be no mismatch between the '%i' and '%d' format specifiers in the string and their corresponding arguments in the invocation of a string formatting function [CERT_C-DCL11-c-2]
        • There should be no mismatch between the '%u' format specifier in the format string and its corresponding argument in the invocation of a string formatting function [CERT_C-DCL11-d-2]
        • There should be no mismatch between the '%p' format specifier in the format string and its corresponding argument in the invocation of a string formatting function [CERT_C-DCL11-e-2]
        • The number of format specifiers in the format string and the number of corresponding arguments in the invocation of a string formatting function should be equal [CERT_C-DCL11-f-2]
      • CERT-DCL12_C (REC) Implement abstract data types using opaque types [CERT_C-DCL12]
        • If a pointer to a structure or union is never dereferenced within a translation unit, then the implementation of the object should be hidden [CERT_C-DCL12-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL13_C (REC) Declare function parameters that are pointers to values not changed by the function as const [CERT_C-DCL13]
        • A pointer parameter in a function prototype should be declared as pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [CERT_C-DCL13-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL15_C (REC) Declare file-scope objects or functions that do not need external linkage as static [CERT_C-DCL15]
        • Objects or functions with external linkage shall be declared in a header file [CERT_C-DCL15-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL16_C (REC) Use "L," not "l," to indicate a long value [CERT_C-DCL16]
        • Use capital 'L' instead of lowercase 'l' to indicate long [CERT_C-DCL16-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL18_C (REC) Do not begin integer constants with 0 when specifying a decimal value [CERT_C-DCL18]
        • Octal and hexadecimal escape sequences shall be terminated [CERT_C-DCL18-a-3]
        • Octal constants (other than zero) shall not be used [CERT_C-DCL18-b-3]
      • CERT-DCL19_C (REC) Minimize the scope of variables and functions [CERT_C-DCL19]
        • Declare variables as locally as possible [CERT_C-DCL19-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL20_C (REC) Explicitly specify void when a function accepts no arguments [CERT_C-DCL20]
        • The number of arguments passed to a function shall match the number of parameters [CERT_C-DCL20-a-1]
      • CERT-DCL22_C (REC) Use volatile for data that cannot be cached [CERT_C-DCL22]
        • Avoid unused values [CERT_C-DCL22-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL30_C (RULE) Declare objects with appropriate storage durations [CERT_C-DCL30]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be returned from a function [CERT_C-DCL30-a-2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be assigned to another object that may persist after the first object has ceased to exist [CERT_C-DCL30-b-2]
      • CERT-DCL31_C (RULE) Declare identifiers before using them [CERT_C-DCL31]
        • All functions shall be declared before use [CERT_C-DCL31-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL36_C (RULE) Do not declare an identifier with conflicting linkage classifications [CERT_C-DCL36]
        • Identifiers shall not simultaneously have both internal and external linkage in the same translation unit [CERT_C-DCL36-a-2]
      • CERT-DCL37_C (RULE) Do not declare or define a reserved identifier [CERT_C-DCL37]
        • Do not #define or #undef identifiers with names which start with underscore [CERT_C-DCL37-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL38_C (RULE) Use the correct syntax when declaring a flexible array member [CERT_C-DCL38]
        • The final member of a structure should not be an array of size '0' or '1' [CERT_C-DCL38-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL39_C (RULE) Avoid information leakage when passing a structure across a trust boundary [CERT_C-DCL39]
        • A pointer to a structure should not be passed to a function that can copy data to the user space [CERT_C-DCL39-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL40_C (RULE) Do not create incompatible declarations of the same function or object [CERT_C-DCL40]
        • All declarations of an object or function shall have compatible types [CERT_C-DCL40-a-3]
        • If objects or functions are declared more than once their types shall be compatible [CERT_C-DCL40-b-3]
      • CERT-DCL41_C (RULE) Do not declare variables inside a switch statement before the first case label [CERT_C-DCL41]
        • A switch statement shall only contain switch labels and switch clauses, and no other code [CERT_C-DCL41-a-3]
      • CERT-ENV01_C (REC) Do not make assumptions about the size of an environment variable [CERT_C-ENV01]
        • Don't use unsafe C functions that do write to range-unchecked buffers [CERT_C-ENV01-a-1]
        • Avoid using unsafe string functions which may cause buffer overflows [CERT_C-ENV01-b-1]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [CERT_C-ENV01-c-1]
      • CERT-ENV02_C (REC) Beware of multiple environment variables with the same effective name [CERT_C-ENV02]
        • Usage of system properties (environment variables) should be restricted [CERT_C-ENV02-a-3]
      • CERT-ENV30_C (RULE) Do not modify the object referenced by the return value of certain functions [CERT_C-ENV30]
        • The pointers returned by the Standard Library functions 'localeconv', 'getenv', 'setlocale' or, 'strerror' shall only be used as if they have pointer to const-qualified type [CERT_C-ENV30-a-3]
      • CERT-ENV31_C (RULE) Do not rely on an environment pointer following an operation that may invalidate it [CERT_C-ENV31]
        • Do not rely on an environment pointer following an operation that may invalidate it [CERT_C-ENV31-a-3]
      • CERT-ENV32_C (RULE) All exit handlers must return normally [CERT_C-ENV32]
        • Properly define exit handlers [CERT_C-ENV32-a-1]
      • CERT-ENV33_C (RULE) Do not call system() [CERT_C-ENV33]
        • Do not call the 'system()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library with an argument other than '0' (null pointer) [CERT_C-ENV33-a-1]
      • CERT-ENV34_C (RULE) Do not store pointers returned by certain functions [CERT_C-ENV34]
        • Pointers returned by certain Standard Library functions should not be used following a subsequent call to the same or related function [CERT_C-ENV34-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR01_C (REC) Use ferror() rather than errno to check for FILE stream errors [CERT_C-ERR01]
        • The error indicator 'errno' shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR01-a-2]
      • CERT-ERR02_C (REC) Avoid in-band error indicators [CERT_C-ERR02]
        • The Standard Library input/output functions shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR02-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR04_C (REC) Choose an appropriate termination strategy [CERT_C-ERR04]
        • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR04-a-3]
        • The 'exit()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR04-b-3]
        • The 'quick_exit()' and '_Exit()' functions from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR04-c-3]
      • CERT-ERR05_C (REC) Application-independent code should provide error detection without dictating error handling [CERT_C-ERR05]
        • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR05-a-3]
        • The 'exit()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR05-b-3]
        • The 'quick_exit()' and '_Exit()' functions from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR05-c-3]
      • CERT-ERR06_C (REC) Understand the termination behavior of assert() and abort() [CERT_C-ERR06]
        • Do not use assertions [CERT_C-ERR06-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR07_C (REC) Prefer functions that support error checking over equivalent functions that don't [CERT_C-ERR07]
        • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library stdlib.h shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR07-a-2]
        • The library functions 'rewind', 'setbuf' and 'ctime' should not be used [CERT_C-ERR07-b-2]
      • CERT-ERR30_C (RULE) Set errno to zero before calling a library function known to set errno, and check errno only after the function returns a value indicating failure [CERT_C-ERR30]
        • Properly use errno value [CERT_C-ERR30-a-2]
        • Provide error handling for file opening errors right next to the call to fopen [CERT_C-ERR30-b-2]
      • CERT-ERR32_C (RULE) Do not rely on indeterminate values of errno [CERT_C-ERR32]
        • Properly use errno value [CERT_C-ERR32-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR33_C (RULE) Detect and handle standard library errors [CERT_C-ERR33]
        • The value returned by a standard library function that may return an error should be used [CERT_C-ERR33-a-1]
        • Always check the returned value of non-void function [CERT_C-ERR33-d-1]
      • CERT-ERR34_C (RULE) Detect errors when converting a string to a number [CERT_C-ERR34]
        • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library stdlib.h shall not be used [CERT_C-ERR34-a-3]

        • An expression of essentially Boolean type should always be used where an operand is interpreted as a Boolean value [CERT_C-INT31-a-2]
        • An operand of essentially Boolean type should not be used where an operand is interpreted as a numeric value [CERT_C-INT31-b-2]

      • CERT-DCL56_CPP (RULE) Avoid cycles during initialization of static objects [CERT_CPP-DCL56]
