      • CERT-DCL57_CPP (RULE) Do not let exceptions escape from destructors or deallocation functions [CERT_CPP-DCL57]
        • Never allow an exception to be thrown from a destructor, deallocation, and swap [CERT_CPP-DCL57-a-2]
        • Always catch exceptions [CERT_CPP-DCL57-b-2]
      • CERT-DCL58_CPP (RULE) Do not modify the standard namespaces [CERT_CPP-DCL58]
        • Do not modify the standard namespaces 'std' and 'posix' [CERT_CPP-DCL58-a-2]
      • CERT-DCL59_CPP (RULE) Do not define an unnamed namespace in a header file [CERT_CPP-DCL59]
        • There shall be no unnamed namespaces in header files [CERT_CPP-DCL59-a-3]
      • CERT-DCL60_CPP (RULE) Obey the one-definition rule [CERT_CPP-DCL60]
        • The One Definition Rule shall not be violated [CERT_CPP-DCL60-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR50_CPP (RULE) Do not abruptly terminate the program [CERT_CPP-ERR50]
        • The execution of a function registered with 'std::atexit()' or 'std::at_quick_exit()' should not exit via an exception [CERT_CPP-ERR50-a-3]
        • Never allow an exception to be thrown from a destructor, deallocation, and swap [CERT_CPP-ERR50-b-3]
        • Do not throw from within destructor [CERT_CPP-ERR50-c-3]
        • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR50-d-3]
        • An empty throw (throw;) shall only be used in the compound-statement of a catch handler [CERT_CPP-ERR50-e-3]
        • Exceptions shall be raised only after start-up and before termination of the program [CERT_CPP-ERR50-f-3]
        • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [CERT_CPP-ERR50-g-3]
        • Where a function's declaration includes an exception-specification, the function shall only be capable of throwing exceptions of the indicated type(s) [CERT_CPP-ERR50-h-3]
        • Function called in global or namespace scope shall not throw unhandled exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR50-i-3]
        • Always catch exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR50-j-3]
        • Properly define exit handlers [CERT_CPP-ERR50-k-3]
        • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_CPP-ERR50-l-3]
        • Avoid throwing exceptions from functions that are declared not to throw [CERT_CPP-ERR50-m-3]
        • The 'quick_exit()' and '_Exit()' functions from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [CERT_CPP-ERR50-n-3]
      • CERT-ERR51_CPP (RULE) Handle all exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR51]
        • Always catch exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR51-a-3]
        • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [CERT_CPP-ERR51-b-3]
      • CERT-ERR52_CPP (RULE) Do not use setjmp() or longjmp() [CERT_CPP-ERR52]
        • The facilities provided by <setjmp.h> should not be used [CERT_CPP-ERR52-a-3]
        • The standard header files <setjmp.h> or <csetjmp> shall not be used [CERT_CPP-ERR52-b-3]
      • CERT-ERR53_CPP (RULE) Do not reference base classes or class data members in a constructor or destructor function-try-block handler [CERT_CPP-ERR53]
        • Handlers of a function-try-block implementation of a class constructor or destructor shall not reference nonstatic members from this class or its bases [CERT_CPP-ERR53-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR54_CPP (RULE) Catch handlers should order their parameter types from most derived to least derived [CERT_CPP-ERR54]
        • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single try-catch statement or function-try-block for a derived class and some or all of its bases, the handlers shall be ordered most-derived to base class [CERT_CPP-ERR54-a-1]
      • CERT-ERR55_CPP (RULE) Honor exception specifications [CERT_CPP-ERR55]
        • Where a function's declaration includes an exception-specification, the function shall only be capable of throwing exceptions of the indicated type(s) [CERT_CPP-ERR55-a-2]
      • CERT-ERR56_CPP (RULE) Guarantee exception safety [CERT_CPP-ERR56]
        • Always catch exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR56-a-2]
        • Do not leave 'catch' blocks empty [CERT_CPP-ERR56-b-2]
      • CERT-ERR57_CPP (RULE) Do not leak resources when handling exceptions [CERT_CPP-ERR57]
        • Ensure resources are freed [CERT_CPP-ERR57-a-3]
      • CERT-ERR58_CPP (RULE) Handle all exceptions thrown before main() begins executing [CERT_CPP-ERR58]
        • Exceptions shall be raised only after start-up and before termination of the program [CERT_CPP-ERR58-a-2]
      • CERT-ERR59_CPP (RULE) Do not throw an exception across execution boundaries [CERT_CPP-ERR59]
        • Do not throw an exception across execution boundaries [CERT_CPP-ERR59-a-1]
      • CERT-ERR60_CPP (RULE) Exception objects must be nothrow copy constructible [CERT_CPP-ERR60]
        • Exception objects must be nothrow copy constructible [CERT_CPP-ERR60-a-3]
        • An explicitly declared copy constructor for a class that inherits from 'std::exception' should have a non-throwing exception specification [CERT_CPP-ERR60-b-3]
      • CERT-ERR61_CPP (RULE) Catch exceptions by lvalue reference [CERT_CPP-ERR61]
        • A class type exception shall always be caught by reference [CERT_CPP-ERR61-a-3]
        • Throw by value, catch by reference [CERT_CPP-ERR61-b-3]
      • CERT-ERR62_CPP (RULE) Detect errors when converting a string to a number [CERT_CPP-ERR62]
        • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library stdlib.h shall not be used [CERT_CPP-ERR62-a-3]
      • CERT-EXP50_CPP (RULE) Do not depend on the order of evaluation for side effects [CERT_CPP-EXP50]
        • The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [CERT_CPP-EXP50-a-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function arguments [CERT_CPP-EXP50-b-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function designator and function arguments [CERT_CPP-EXP50-c-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of expression that involves a function call [CERT_CPP-EXP50-d-2]
        • Between sequence points an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression [CERT_CPP-EXP50-e-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function calls [CERT_CPP-EXP50-f-2]
      • CERT-EXP51_CPP (RULE) Do not delete an array through a pointer of the incorrect type [CERT_CPP-EXP51]
        • Do not treat arrays polymorphically [CERT_CPP-EXP51-a-3]
      • CERT-EXP52_CPP (RULE) Do not rely on side effects in unevaluated operands [CERT_CPP-EXP52]
        • The operand of the sizeof operator shall not contain any expression which has side effects [CERT_CPP-EXP52-a-3]
        • Object designated by a volatile lvalue should not be accessed in the operand of the sizeof operator [CERT_CPP-EXP52-b-3]
        • The function call that causes the side effect shall not be the operand of the sizeof operator [CERT_CPP-EXP52-c-3]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain any expression that has side effects [CERT_CPP-EXP52-d-3]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain a function call that causes side effects [CERT_CPP-EXP52-e-3]
      • CERT-EXP53_CPP (RULE) Do not read uninitialized memory [CERT_CPP-EXP53]
        • Avoid use before initialization [CERT_CPP-EXP53-a-1]
      • CERT-EXP54_CPP (RULE) Do not access an object outside of its lifetime [CERT_CPP-EXP54]
        • Do not use resources that have been freed [CERT_CPP-EXP54-a-2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be returned from a function [CERT_CPP-EXP54-b-2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be assigned to another object that may persist after the first object has ceased to exist [CERT_CPP-EXP54-c-2]
      • CERT-EXP55_CPP (RULE) Do not access a cv-qualified object through a cv-unqualified type [CERT_CPP-EXP55]
        • A cast shall not remove any 'const' or 'volatile' qualification from the type of a pointer or reference [CERT_CPP-EXP55-a-2]
      • CERT-EXP56_CPP (RULE) Do not call a function with a mismatched language linkage [CERT_CPP-EXP56]
        • Do not call a function with a mismatched language linkage [CERT_CPP-EXP56-a-3]
      • CERT-EXP57_CPP (RULE) Do not cast or delete pointers to incomplete classes [CERT_CPP-EXP57]
        • Do not delete objects with incomplete class at the point of deletion [CERT_CPP-EXP57-a-3]
        • Conversions shall not be performed between a pointer to an incomplete type and any other type [CERT_CPP-EXP57-b-3]
      • CERT-EXP58_CPP (RULE) Pass an object of the correct type to va_start [CERT_CPP-EXP58]
        • Use macros for variable arguments correctly [CERT_CPP-EXP58-a-3]
      • CERT-EXP59_CPP (RULE) Use offsetof() on valid types and members [CERT_CPP-EXP59]
        • Use offsetof() on valid types and members [CERT_CPP-EXP59-a-3]
      • CERT-EXP60_CPP (RULE) Do not pass a nonstandard-layout type object across execution boundaries [CERT_CPP-EXP60]
        • Do not pass a nonstandard-layout type object across execution boundaries [CERT_CPP-EXP60-a-1]
      • CERT-EXP61_CPP (RULE) A lambda object must not outlive any of its reference captured objects [CERT_CPP-EXP61]
        • Never return lambdas that capture local objects by reference [CERT_CPP-EXP61-a-2]
        • Never capture local objects from an outer lambda by reference [CERT_CPP-EXP61-b-2]
        • The lambda that captures local objects by reference should not be assigned to the variable with a greater lifetime [CERT_CPP-EXP61-c-2]
      • CERT-EXP62_CPP (RULE) Do not access the bits of an object representation that are not part of the object's value representation [CERT_CPP-EXP62]
        • Do not compare objects of a class that may contain padding bits with C standard library functions [CERT_CPP-EXP62-a-2]
      • CERT-EXP63_CPP (RULE) Do not rely on the value of a moved-from object [CERT_CPP-EXP63]
        • Do not rely on the value of a moved-from object [CERT_CPP-EXP63-a-2]
      • CERT-FIO50_CPP (RULE) Do not alternately input and output from a file stream without an intervening positioning call [CERT_CPP-FIO50]
        • Do not alternately input and output from a stream without an intervening flush or positioning call [CERT_CPP-FIO50-a-2]
      • CERT-FIO51_CPP (RULE) Close files when they are no longer needed [CERT_CPP-FIO51]
        • Ensure resources are freed [CERT_CPP-FIO51-a-3]
      • CERT-INT50_CPP (RULE) Do not cast to an out-of-range enumeration value [CERT_CPP-INT50]
        • An expression with enum underlying type shall only have values corresponding to the enumerators of the enumeration [CERT_CPP-INT50-a-3]
      • CERT-MEM50_CPP (RULE) Do not access freed memory [CERT_CPP-MEM50]
        • Do not use resources that have been freed [CERT_CPP-MEM50-a-1]
      • CERT-MEM51_CPP (RULE) Properly deallocate dynamically allocated resources [CERT_CPP-MEM51]
        • Use the same form in corresponding calls to new/malloc and delete/free [CERT_CPP-MEM51-a-1]
        • Always provide empty brackets ([]) for delete when deallocating arrays [CERT_CPP-MEM51-b-1]
        • Both copy constructor and copy assignment operator should be declared for classes with a nontrivial destructor [CERT_CPP-MEM51-c-1]
        • Properly deallocate dynamically allocated resources [CERT_CPP-MEM51-d-1]
      • CERT-MEM52_CPP (RULE) Detect and handle memory allocation errors [CERT_CPP-MEM52]
        • Check the return value of new [CERT_CPP-MEM52-a-1]
        • Do not allocate resources in function argument list because the order of evaluation of a function's parameters is undefined [CERT_CPP-MEM52-b-1]
      • CERT-MEM53_CPP (RULE) Explicitly construct and destruct objects when manually managing object lifetime [CERT_CPP-MEM53]
        • Do not invoke malloc/realloc for objects having constructors [CERT_CPP-MEM53-a-1]
      • CERT-MEM54_CPP (RULE) Provide placement new with properly aligned pointers to sufficient storage capacity [CERT_CPP-MEM54]
        • Do not pass a pointer that has insufficient storage capacity or that is not suitably aligned for the object being constructed to placement 'new' [CERT_CPP-MEM54-a-1]
        • An overhead should be used when an array of objects is passed to the placement 'new' allocation function [CERT_CPP-MEM54-b-1]
      • CERT-MEM55_CPP (RULE) Honor replacement dynamic storage management requirements [CERT_CPP-MEM55]
        • The user defined 'new' operator should throw the 'std::bad_alloc' exception when the allocation fails [CERT_CPP-MEM55-a-1]
      • CERT-MEM56_CPP (RULE) Do not store an already-owned pointer value in an unrelated smart pointer [CERT_CPP-MEM56]
        • Do not store an already-owned pointer value in an unrelated smart pointer [CERT_CPP-MEM56-a-1]
      • CERT-MEM57_CPP (RULE) Avoid using default operator new for over-aligned types [CERT_CPP-MEM57]
        • Avoid using the default operator 'new' for over-aligned types [CERT_CPP-MEM57-a-2]
      • CERT-MSC50_CPP (RULE) Do not use std::rand() for generating pseudorandom numbers [CERT_CPP-MSC50]
        • Do not use the rand() function for generating pseudorandom numbers [CERT_CPP-MSC50-a-2]
      • CERT-MSC51_CPP (RULE) Ensure your random number generator is properly seeded [CERT_CPP-MSC51]
        • Properly seed pseudorandom number generators [CERT_CPP-MSC51-a-1]
      • CERT-MSC52_CPP (RULE) Value-returning functions must return a value from all exit paths [CERT_CPP-MSC52]
        • All exit paths from a function, except main(), with non-void return type shall have an explicit return statement with an expression [CERT_CPP-MSC52-a-2]
      • CERT-MSC53_CPP (RULE) Do not return from a function declared [[noreturn]] [CERT_CPP-MSC53]
        • Never return from functions that should not return [CERT_CPP-MSC53-a-3]
      • CERT-MSC54_CPP (RULE) A signal handler must be a plain old function [CERT_CPP-MSC54]
        • Properly define signal handlers [CERT_CPP-MSC54-a-2]
      • CERT-OOP50_CPP (RULE) Do not invoke virtual functions from constructors or destructors [CERT_CPP-OOP50]
        • Avoid calling virtual functions from constructors [CERT_CPP-OOP50-a-3]
        • Avoid calling virtual functions from destructors [CERT_CPP-OOP50-b-3]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under construction [CERT_CPP-OOP50-c-3]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under destruction [CERT_CPP-OOP50-d-3]
      • CERT-OOP51_CPP (RULE) Do not slice derived objects [CERT_CPP-OOP51]
        • Do not slice derived objects [CERT_CPP-OOP51-a-3]
      • CERT-OOP52_CPP (RULE) Do not delete a polymorphic object without a virtual destructor [CERT_CPP-OOP52]
        • Define a virtual destructor in classes used as base classes which have virtual functions [CERT_CPP-OOP52-a-2]
      • CERT-OOP53_CPP (RULE) Write constructor member initializers in the canonical order [CERT_CPP-OOP53]
        • List members in an initialization list in the order in which they are declared [CERT_CPP-OOP53-a-3]
      • CERT-OOP54_CPP (RULE) Gracefully handle self-copy assignment [CERT_CPP-OOP54]
        • Check for assignment to self in operator= [CERT_CPP-OOP54-a-3]
      • CERT-OOP55_CPP (RULE) Do not use pointer-to-member operators to access nonexistent members [CERT_CPP-OOP55]
        • A cast shall not convert a pointer to a function to any other pointer type, including a pointer to function type [CERT_CPP-OOP55-a-2]
      • CERT-OOP56_CPP (RULE) Honor replacement handler requirements [CERT_CPP-OOP56]
        • Properly define terminate handlers [CERT_CPP-OOP56-a-3]
        • Properly define unexpected handlers [CERT_CPP-OOP56-b-3]
        • Properly define new handlers [CERT_CPP-OOP56-c-3]
      • CERT-OOP57_CPP (RULE) Prefer special member functions and overloaded operators to C Standard Library functions [CERT_CPP-OOP57]
        • Do not initialize objects with a non-trivial class type using C standard library functions [CERT_CPP-OOP57-a-2]
        • Do not compare objects of nonstandard-layout class type with C standard library functions [CERT_CPP-OOP57-b-2]
      • CERT-OOP58_CPP (RULE) Copy operations must not mutate the source object [CERT_CPP-OOP58]
        • Copy operations must not mutate the source object [CERT_CPP-OOP58-a-2]
      • CERT-STR50_CPP (RULE) Guarantee that storage for strings has sufficient space for character data and the null terminator [CERT_CPP-STR50]
        • Avoid overflow due to reading a not zero terminated string [CERT_CPP-STR50-b-1]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [CERT_CPP-STR50-c-1]
        • Prevent buffer overflows from tainted data [CERT_CPP-STR50-e-1]
        • Avoid buffer write overflow from tainted data [CERT_CPP-STR50-f-1]
        • Do not use the 'char' buffer to store input from 'std::cin' [CERT_CPP-STR50-g-1]
      • CERT-STR51_CPP (RULE) Do not attempt to create a std::string from a null pointer [CERT_CPP-STR51]
        • Avoid null pointer dereferencing [CERT_CPP-STR51-a-1]
      • CERT-STR52_CPP (RULE) Use valid references, pointers, and iterators to reference elements of a basic_string [CERT_CPP-STR52]
        • Use valid references, pointers, and iterators to reference elements of a basic_string [CERT_CPP-STR52-a-2]
      • CERT-STR53_CPP (RULE) Range check element access [CERT_CPP-STR53]
        • Guarantee that container indices are within the valid range [CERT_CPP-STR53-a-2]
    • Coding Conventions [CODSTA]
      • Coding Conventions for C++ [CODSTA-CPP]
        • Prefer iostream.h to stdio.h [CODSTA-CPP-01-5]
        • Have assignment operator returns a reference to *this; make assignment operator's return type a non-const reference to it's class' type [CODSTA-CPP-02-3]
        • Bitwise operators, comparison operators, logical operators, comma operator should be const [CODSTA-CPP-03-3]
        • Constructors allowing for conversion should be made explicit [CODSTA-CPP-04-1]
        • Do not use user-defined conversion functions [CODSTA-CPP-05-1]
        • Avoid returning handles to class data from member functions [CODSTA-CPP-06-3]
        • Postfix increment and decrement should be implemented in terms of their prefix counterparts [CODSTA-CPP-07-3]
        • Avoid overloading logical operators AND, OR (&&, ||) [CODSTA-CPP-08-3]
        • Avoid using reinterpret_cast [CODSTA-CPP-09-3]
        • Do not define structs that contain member functions [CODSTA-CPP-10-3]
        • Do not compare objects of a class that may contain padding bits with C standard library functions [CODSTA-CPP-100-3]
        • A relational operator shall return a boolean value [CODSTA-CPP-101-3]
        • A binary arithmetic operator and a bitwise operator shall return a 'prvalue' [CODSTA-CPP-102-3]
        • Output parameters shall not be used [CODSTA-CPP-103-3]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain any expression that has side effects [CODSTA-CPP-104-3]
        • The operand of the 'typeid' operator shall not contain a function call that causes side effects [CODSTA-CPP-104_b-3]
        • Define special members as =default when the behavior is equivalent to the compiler's behavior [CODSTA-CPP-105-3]
        • Use delegating constructors to reduce code duplication [CODSTA-CPP-106-3]
        • Comparison operators shall be non-member functions [CODSTA-CPP-107-3]
        • Comparison operators shall be non-member functions with identical parameter types and noexcept [CODSTA-CPP-107_b-3]
        • A parameter of const reference to a 'cheap to copy' type should be passed by value [CODSTA-CPP-108-3]
        • Pass small objects with a trivial copy constructor by value [CODSTA-CPP-108_b-3]
        • A parameter of a type that is not 'cheap to copy' should be passed by reference [CODSTA-CPP-109-3]
        • C-style casts should not be used [CODSTA-CPP-11-3]
        • Member variable names in derived classes should not be the same as member variable names in base classes [CODSTA-CPP-110-3]
        • The 'NULL' identifier should not be used [CODSTA-CPP-111-4]
        • The result of std::remove, std::remove_if, std::unique and empty shall be used [CODSTA-CPP-112-3]
        • The 'std::locale::global' function should not be used [CODSTA-CPP-113-3]
        • Put classes that are used as base classes and classes that are used as member variables into separate include files [CODSTA-CPP-12-3]
        • Put classes that are used as function return type into separate include files [CODSTA-CPP-13-3]
        • Put classes that are used as argument types in function prototypes into separate include files [CODSTA-CPP-14-3]
        • Put functions that are used in the body of inline member function into separate include file [CODSTA-CPP-15-3]
        • When two operators are opposites (such as == and !=), it is appropriate to define both [CODSTA-CPP-16-3]
        • Do not use the 'struct' keyword to declare a variable in C++ [CODSTA-CPP-17-3]
        • Encapsulate global variables and constants, enumerated types, and typedefs in a class [CODSTA-CPP-18-5]
        • Declare at least one constructor to prevent the compiler from doing so [CODSTA-CPP-19-2]
        • If you'd like to support mixed-mode operations make operators a non-member functions [CODSTA-CPP-20-3]
        • Non-static data members should be either all private or all public [CODSTA-CPP-201-4]
        • An enumeration shall be defined with an explicit underlying type [CODSTA-CPP-202-3]
        • An explicit or implicit enumerator value shall not be the result of a narrowing conversion [CODSTA-CPP-203-2]
        • The operand to typeid shall not be an expression of polymorphic class type [CODSTA-CPP-204-2]
        • User-provided copy and move member functions of a class should have appropriate signatures [CODSTA-CPP-205-3]
        • Member functions returning references to their object should be ref-qualified appropriately [CODSTA-CPP-206-3]
        • An argument passed via ellipsis shall have an appropriate type [CODSTA-CPP-207-2]
        • Exception-unfriendly functions shall be noexcept [CODSTA-CPP-208-2]
        • Functions used as initializers of non-constexpr non-local variables shall be noexcept [CODSTA-CPP-209-2]
        • Assignment operator must return const reference [CODSTA-CPP-21-5]
        • Parameters in an overriding virtual function shall not specify different default arguments [CODSTA-CPP-210-2]
        • There shall be no conversion from type bool [CODSTA-CPP-211-3]
        • There shall be no conversion to type bool [CODSTA-CPP-212-3]
        • Prefer non-member non-friend functions to member functions [CODSTA-CPP-22-4]
        • Whenever a global function  is  referenced, use the :: operator [CODSTA-CPP-23-5]
        • Avoid making any assignment operator virtual. Do not return const T& from assignment operator [CODSTA-CPP-24-3]
        • Consider making virtual functions nonpublic, and public functions nonvirtual [CODSTA-CPP-25-3]
        • Keep types and functions in separate namespaces unless they're specifically intended to work together [CODSTA-CPP-26-3]
        • Keep a type and its nonmember function interface in the same namespace [CODSTA-CPP-27-3]
        • When binary arithmetic operators are defined  ( + , - , * , / , ^ , % , | , & ), assignment versions should be provided too [CODSTA-CPP-28-3]
        • Prefer the canonical forms of arithmetic and assignment operators [CODSTA-CPP-29-3]
        • Prefer non-member operators than member ones to support mixed-mode arithmetic [CODSTA-CPP-30-3]
        • Do not use the keyword 'explicit' for a constructor [CODSTA-CPP-31-5]
        • A function definition should not be placed in a class specification unless the function is intended to be inlined [CODSTA-CPP-32-3]
        • Member functions shall not be defined within the template class definition [CODSTA-CPP-33-3]
        • Avoid using static_cast on pointers [CODSTA-CPP-34-3]
        • Avoid dynamic_casts [CODSTA-CPP-35-3]
        • The global namespace shall only contain main() and namespace declarations [CODSTA-CPP-36-3]
        • Do not define class/struct/union inside function implementation [CODSTA-CPP-37-3]
        • Conversion operator, operator->, operator(), operator[] should be const [CODSTA-CPP-38-3]
        • Don't write namespace usings in a header file or before an #include [CODSTA-CPP-39-3]
        • Limiting the number of objects of a class [CODSTA-CPP-40-5]
        • Do not use the 'enum' keyword to declare a variable in C++ [CODSTA-CPP-41-3]
        • Do not declare member variables with the 'mutable' keyword [CODSTA-CPP-42-3]
        • Declare reference parameters as const references whenever possible [CODSTA-CPP-43-3]
        • Have the non-const version call the const version of member function instead of duplicating the const version definition [CODSTA-CPP-44-3]
        • In the private section of a class items shall be declared in the following order: Constructors, Destructor, Member Functions, Member Operator Function, Enumerations and others [CODSTA-CPP-45-3]
        • Order of scopes in class: public before all others [CODSTA-CPP-46-3]
        • Order of scopes in classes: protected before private [CODSTA-CPP-47-3]
        • In the protected section of a class items shall be declared in the following order: Constructors, Destructor, Member Functions, Member Operator Function, Enumerations and others [CODSTA-CPP-48-3]
        • In the public section of a class items shall be declared in the following order: Constructors, Destructor, Member Functions, Member Operator Function, Enumerations and others [CODSTA-CPP-49-3]
        • Do not use static keyword except inside functions and classes [CODSTA-CPP-50-3]
        • Do not define inline functions in source files [CODSTA-CPP-51-3]
        • Consider using the natural relationship between the assignment version of an operator and the stand-alone version [CODSTA-CPP-52-3]
        • Declare local variable as const whenever possible [CODSTA-CPP-53-3]
        • Declare parameters as const whenever possible [CODSTA-CPP-53_b-3]
        • Member functions shall be declared const whenever possible [CODSTA-CPP-54-3]
        • Arrays shall not be used in interfaces [CODSTA-CPP-55-2]
        • Private and protected methods shall not declare parameters with array type [CODSTA-CPP-55_b-2]
        • A class, structure, or enumeration will not be declared in the definition of its type [CODSTA-CPP-56-3]
        • Namespaces will not be nested more than two levels deep [CODSTA-CPP-57-3]
        • The value returned by a function having a non-void return type that is not an overloaded operator shall always be used [CODSTA-CPP-58-3]
        • The C library shall not be used [CODSTA-CPP-59-3]
        • Only those escape sequences that are defined in ISO/IEC 14882:2003 shall be used [CODSTA-CPP-60-3]
        • Only those escape sequences that are defined in ISO/IEC 14882:2014 shall be used [CODSTA-CPP-60_b-3]
        • NULL shall not be used as an integer value [CODSTA-CPP-62-3]
        • Literal zero (0) shall not be used as the null-pointer-constant [CODSTA-CPP-63-3]
        • The condition of an if-statement and the condition of an iteration-statement shall have type bool [CODSTA-CPP-64-3]
        • The first operand of a conditional-operator shall have type bool [CODSTA-CPP-65-1]
        • C-style casts (other than void casts) and functional notation casts (other than explicit constructor calls) shall not be used [CODSTA-CPP-66-3]
        • Each operand of the ! operator, the logical && or the logical || operators shall have type bool [CODSTA-CPP-67-3]
        • The unary & operator shall not be overloaded [CODSTA-CPP-68-3]
        • A for loop shall contain a single loop-counter which shall not have floating type [CODSTA-CPP-69-3]
        • If loop-counter is not modified by -- or ++, then, within condition, the loop-counter shall only be used as an operand to <=, <, > or >= [CODSTA-CPP-70-3]
        • The loop-counter shall be modified by one of: --, ++, -=n, or +=n; where n remains constant for the duration of the loop [CODSTA-CPP-71-3]
        • A loop-control-variable other than the loop-counter shall not be modified within condition or expression [CODSTA-CPP-72-3]
        • A loop-control-variable other than the loop-counter which is modified in statement shall have type bool [CODSTA-CPP-73-3]
        • There shall be no unnamed namespaces in header files [CODSTA-CPP-74-3]
        • using-directives shall not be used [CODSTA-CPP-75-3]
        • Multiple declarations for an identifier in the same namespace shall not straddle a using-declaration for that identifier [CODSTA-CPP-76-3]
        • Const member functions shall not return non-const pointers or references to class-data [CODSTA-CPP-77-3]
        • If a member function can be made static then it shall be made static, otherwise if it can be made const then it shall be made const [CODSTA-CPP-78-3]
        • Neither operand of an equality operator (== or !=) shall be a pointer to a virtual member function [CODSTA-CPP-79-3]
        • Avoid overloading comma operator "," [CODSTA-CPP-80-3]
        • Classes which have only getters/setters (accessors/mutators) are not allowed [CODSTA-CPP-81-4]
        • Avoid unencapsulated global variables (including variables declared in namespaces and public static members) [CODSTA-CPP-82-3]
        • Identifiers declared in a local scope should not hide identifiers declared in a class scope [CODSTA-CPP-83-3]
        • Identifiers declared in a class scope should not hide identifiers declared in a global or namespace scope [CODSTA-CPP-84-3]
        • Identifiers declared in an inner class scope should not hide identifiers declared in outer class scope [CODSTA-CPP-85-3]
        • If two opposite equality operators ('==', '!=') are defined in a class, one shall be defined in terms of the other [CODSTA-CPP-86-3]
        • If an identifier refers to a type, it shall not also refer to an object or a function in the same scope [CODSTA-CPP-87_a-3]
        • If an identifier refers to a type, it shall not also refer to an object or a function in the same scope [CODSTA-CPP-87_b-3]
        • If an identifier refers to a type, it shall not also refer to an object or a function in the same scope [CODSTA-CPP-87_c-3]
        • The name of typedef should not be the same as the name of its basic type [CODSTA-CPP-88-3]
        • Do not assign enumerations to bool [CODSTA-CPP-89-4]
        • using-directives and using-declarations (excluding class scope or function scope using-declarations) shall not be used in header files [CODSTA-CPP-90-3]
        • The overloaded binary operator should be implemented in terms of its corresponding compound assignment operator [CODSTA-CPP-91-3]
        • All accessible entity names within a multiple inheritance hierarchy should be unique [CODSTA-CPP-92-3]
        • Do not initialize objects with a non-trivial class type using C standard library functions [CODSTA-CPP-93-3]
        • Do not compare objects of nonstandard-layout class type with C standard library functions [CODSTA-CPP-94-3]
        • Do not modify the standard namespaces 'std' and 'posix' [CODSTA-CPP-95-3]
        • Do not declare entities in the standard library namespaces: posix, std and stdN [CODSTA-CPP-95_b-3]
        • Do not call a function with a mismatched language linkage [CODSTA-CPP-96-3]
        • Never qualify a reference type with 'const' or 'volatile' [CODSTA-CPP-97-3]
        • Copy operations must not mutate the source object [CODSTA-CPP-98-2]
        • Use offsetof() on valid types and members [CODSTA-CPP-99-3]
      • Coding Conventions for Modern C [CODSTA-MC]
        • The 'alignof' operator should not be used with an array type as its operand [CODSTA-MC-01-3]
        • A declaration of an object should contain at most one explicit alignment specifier [CODSTA-MC-02-3]
        • The zero-alignment specifier should not be used in an object declaration [CODSTA-MC-03-3]
        • Explicit alignment specifiers in all declarations of an object with internal linkage shall be the same [CODSTA-MC-04-3]
        • Every generic selection shall contain a default association [CODSTA-MC-05-3]
        • The default association shall be placed first or last in the association list [CODSTA-MC-06-3]
        • A generic selection shall indicate at least one non-default association [CODSTA-MC-07-3]
        • A generic selection should only be expanded from a macro [CODSTA-MC-08-3]
        • A generic association shall list an appropriate type [CODSTA-MC-09-3]
        • A generic selection used in a macro definition should have a macro parameter in the controlling expression [CODSTA-MC-10-3]
        • Thread objects, thread synchronization objects and thread-specific storage pointers shall not have automatic storage duration [CODSTA-MC-101-3]
        • A generic selection should not depend on implicit pointer type conversion [CODSTA-MC-11-4]
        • The controlling expression of a generic selection shall have an essential type that matches its standard type [CODSTA-MC-12-3]
        • A generic selection that is not expanded from a macro shall not contain potential side effects in the controlling expression [CODSTA-MC-13-3]
        • Enumerated types should not be mixed with integer types in generic selections [CODSTA-MC-14-3]
        • A generic selection that is expanded from a macro shall evaluate its argument only once [CODSTA-MC-15-3]
        • The '_Atomic' qualifier should not be used with the 'void' type [CODSTA-MC-16-3]
        • Members of atomic objects of structure and union types should not be directly accessed [CODSTA-MC-17-3]
        • A cast shall not remove any '_Atomic' qualification from the type of a pointer [CODSTA-MC-18-3]
        • The value of an expression with atomic type should be independent from thread interleaving [CODSTA-MC-19-3]
        • Only 'memory_order_seq_cst' should be used as an explicit memory order argument [CODSTA-MC-20-3]
        • The second argument passed to the 'mtx_init()' function call should be either 'mtx_plain', 'mtx_timed', 'mtx_plain | mtx_recursive', or 'mtx_timed | mtx_recursive' [CODSTA-MC-21-3]
        • Thread objects, thread synchronization objects, and thread-specific storage pointers shall only be accessed by the appropriate Standard Library functions [CODSTA-MC-22-3]
      • Coding Conventions for Modern C++ [CODSTA-MCPP]
        • User-conversion cast operators should be made explicit [CODSTA-MCPP-01-3]
        • Prefer alias declarations to typedefs [CODSTA-MCPP-02-3]
        • Prefer Scoped Enums to Unscoped Enums [CODSTA-MCPP-03-3]
        • Prefer 'nullptr' over 'NULL' or '0'(zero) [CODSTA-MCPP-04-4]
        • Each overriding virtual function shall be declared with the override or final specifier [CODSTA-MCPP-05-3]
        • Declare copy constructor and copy assignment operators with the 'delete' specifier to prevent copying of class [CODSTA-MCPP-06_a-3]
        • Declare copy constructor and copy assignment operators with the 'delete' specifier instead of using a base class with private methods to prevent copying of class [CODSTA-MCPP-06_b-3]
        • Prefer lambdas over std::bind, std::bind1st and std::bind2nd [CODSTA-MCPP-07-2]
        • The 'binder1st' and 'binder2nd' identifiers should not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-07_b-3]
        • Prefer 'auto' to explicit type names in variable declarations [CODSTA-MCPP-08_a-2]
        • Prefer 'auto' to explicit type names for function return types [CODSTA-MCPP-08_b-2]
        • Declare functions 'noexcept' if they will not emit exceptions [CODSTA-MCPP-09-3]
        • A for-range-initializer shall contain at most one function call [CODSTA-MCPP-101-3]
        • Variables should be captured explicitly in a non-transient lambda [CODSTA-MCPP-103-3]
        • A non-transient lambda shall not implicitly capture this [CODSTA-MCPP-104-3]
        • Special member functions shall be provided appropriately [CODSTA-MCPP-105-3]
        • Prefer const iterators to iterators [CODSTA-MCPP-10_a-3]
        • Prefer to use cbegin(), crbegin, cend(), crend() functions [CODSTA-MCPP-10_b-3]
        • Use constexpr to declare const variables whenever possible [CODSTA-MCPP-11_a_cpp11-4]
        • Use constexpr to declare functions whenever possible [CODSTA-MCPP-11_b_cpp11-4]
        • Use std::move() on rvalue references and std::forward() on forwarding references [CODSTA-MCPP-13-3]
        • The 'std::forward' function should be used to forward forwarding references [CODSTA-MCPP-13_b-3]
        • The 'std::forward' function should only be used to forward forwarding references [CODSTA-MCPP-13_c-3]
        • The 'std::move' function should be used to forward rvalue references [CODSTA-MCPP-13_d-3]
        • Avoid Overloading on Forwarding References [CODSTA-MCPP-14-3]
        • Avoid default capture modes [CODSTA-MCPP-15_a-3]
        • Use the 'this' pointer explicitly in lambdas with a default by-reference capture [CODSTA-MCPP-15_b-3]
        • Prefer smart pointer members over raw pointer members [CODSTA-MCPP-16_a-4]
        • Prefer smart pointers over raw pointers for arrays or STL containers [CODSTA-MCPP-16_b-4]
        • Prefer 'std::make_shared' to the direct use of new [CODSTA-MCPP-16_c-3]
        • Prefer to use std::unique_ptr instead of std::auto_ptr [CODSTA-MCPP-16_d-3]
        • 'std::make_unique' shall be used to construct objects owned by 'std::unique_ptr' [CODSTA-MCPP-16_e-3]
        • Never return lambdas that capture local objects by reference [CODSTA-MCPP-17-3]
        • Never capture local objects from an outer lambda by reference [CODSTA-MCPP-17_b-3]
        • The lambda that captures local objects by reference should not be assigned to the variable with a greater lifetime [CODSTA-MCPP-17_c-3]
        • Avoid unnecessary default capture modes in lambda expressions [CODSTA-MCPP-18_a-3]
        • Avoid unnecessary lambda captures [CODSTA-MCPP-18_b-3]
        • Declare assignment operators with the ref-qualifier & [CODSTA-MCPP-19-3]
        • Prefer smart pointers over raw local pointers [CODSTA-MCPP-20-4]
        • Do not call lock() directly on a mutex [CODSTA-MCPP-21-4]
        • Use explicit ref-qualifiers on auto declarations in range-based 'for' loops [CODSTA-MCPP-22-3]
        • If a public destructor of a class is non-virtual, then the class should be declared final [CODSTA-MCPP-23-3]
        • Only one of virtual, override or final should be specified in a member function declaration [CODSTA-MCPP-24-3]
        • Digit sequences separators ' shall only be used consistently [CODSTA-MCPP-25-3]
        • A pointer to member virtual function shall only be tested for equality with null-pointer-constant [CODSTA-MCPP-26-3]
        • All std::hash specializations for user-defined types shall have a noexcept function call operator [CODSTA-MCPP-27-2]
        • A lambda shall not be an operand to typeid [CODSTA-MCPP-28-3]
        • Use smart pointers when passing a pointer to an object in a thread [CODSTA-MCPP-29-3]
        • Consider using 'std::unique_ptr' instead of 'std::shared_ptr' for local objects [CODSTA-MCPP-30-3]
        • Define both sized and unsized versions of operator delete [CODSTA-MCPP-31-3]
        • Static and thread-local objects shall be constant-initialized [CODSTA-MCPP-32-3]
        • User defined literals operators shall only perform conversion of passed parameters [CODSTA-MCPP-33-3]
        • A smart pointer shall only be used as a parameter type if it expresses lifetime semantics [CODSTA-MCPP-34-3]
        • A parameter should only be declared as a non-const lvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' if the function replaces the managed object [CODSTA-MCPP-35-3]
        • Do not declare the type of a parameter as an rvalue reference to 'std::shared_ptr' or 'std::unique_ptr' [CODSTA-MCPP-36-3]
        • Derived classes that do not need further explicit initialization and require all the constructors from the base class shall use inheriting constructors [CODSTA-MCPP-37-3]
        • Braced-initialization {}, without equals sign, shall be used for variable initialization [CODSTA-MCPP-38-3]
        • A variable of type auto shall not be initialized using '{}' or '={}' braced-initialization [CODSTA-MCPP-39-3]
        • Do not overuse 'auto' specifier [CODSTA-MCPP-40-3]
        • The 'random_shuffle' identifier should not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-41-3]
        • Do not use the increment operator (++) on an operand of type 'bool' [CODSTA-MCPP-42-3]
        • The 'set_unexpected' identifier should not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-43-3]
        • Lambda expressions should not be defined inside another lambda expression [CODSTA-MCPP-44-3]
        • Return type of a non-void return type lambda expression should be explicitly specified [CODSTA-MCPP-45-3]
        • Include a parameter list in every lambda expression [CODSTA-MCPP-46-3]
        • Avoid overloading constructors with std::initializer_list [CODSTA-MCPP-47-3]
        • A class shall only define an initializer-list constructor when it is the only constructor [CODSTA-MCPP-47_b-3]
        • Multiple output values from a function should be returned as a struct or tuple [CODSTA-MCPP-48-3]
        • User-defined copy and move assignment operators should use user-defined no-throw swap function [CODSTA-MCPP-49-3]
        • A for-loop that loops through all elements of the container and does not use its loop-counter shall not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-50-3]
        • Use const container calls when the result is immediately converted to a const iterator [CODSTA-MCPP-51-3]
        • Do not introduce virtual functions in a final class [CODSTA-MCPP-52-3]
        • Do not use std::move on objects declared with the const or const & type [CODSTA-MCPP-53-3]
        • Do not create an rvalue reference of std::array [CODSTA-MCPP-54-3]
        • Use std::call_once rather than the Double-Checked Locking pattern [CODSTA-MCPP-55-3]
        • If a class declares a copy or move operation, or a destructor, either via '=default', '=delete', or via a user-provided declaration, then all others of these five special member functions shall be declared as well [CODSTA-MCPP-56-2]
        • The raw pointer constructors of 'std::shared_ptr' and 'std::unique_ptr' should not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-57-3]
        • Do not include headers deprecated in the C++17 standard [CODSTA-MCPP-58-3]
        • The 'uncaught_exception' function deprecated in the C++17 standard should not be used [CODSTA-MCPP-59-3]
        • The condition of a 'switch' statement should only be preceded by an optional simple-declaration [CODSTA-MCPP-60-3]
        • Define =delete functions with parameters of type rvalue reference to const [CODSTA-MCPP-61-3]

      • External identifiers shall be distinct [CODSTA-178-3]
      • Identifiers declared in the file scope and in the same name space shall be distinct (c90) [CODSTA-179_a_c90-3]
      • Identifiers declared in the file scope and in the same name space shall be distinct (c99) [CODSTA-179_a_c99-3]
      • Identifiers declared in the same block scope and name space shall be distinct (c90) [CODSTA-179_b_c90-3]
      • Identifiers declared in the same block scope and name space shall be distinct (c99) [CODSTA-179_b_c99-3]
      • Prefer 'while' statements over 'do' statements [CODSTA-18-5]
      • The +, -, += and -= operators should not be applied to an expression of pointer type [CODSTA-181-4]
      • The 'sizeof' operator shall not have an operand which is a function parameter declared as "array of type" [CODSTA-182-2]
      • The pointer arguments to the Standard Library functions 'memcmp', 'memmove' and 'memcmp' shall be pointers to qualified or unqualified versions of compatible types [CODSTA-183-3]
      • The pointer arguments to the Standard Library function 'memcmp' shall point to either a pointer type, an essentially signed type, an essentially unsigned type, an essentially Boolean type or an essentially enum type [CODSTA-184-3]
      • The pointers returned by the Standard Library functions 'localeconv', 'getenv', 'setlocale' or, 'strerror' shall only be used as if they have pointer to const-qualified type [CODSTA-185_a-2]
      • Strings pointed by members of the structure 'lconv' should not be modified [CODSTA-185_b-3]
      • The address of the 'localeconv', 'getenv', 'setlocale' or, 'strerror' function should not be taken [CODSTA-185_c-3]
      • Where designated initializers are used to initialize an array object the size of the array shall be specified explicitly [CODSTA-186-3]
      • Cast characters to unsigned char before assignment to larger integer sizes [CODSTA-187_a-3]
      • An expressions of the 'signed char' type should not be used as an array index [CODSTA-187_b-3]
      • Cast characters to unsigned char before converting to larger integer sizes [CODSTA-187_c-3]
      • Do not confuse narrow and wide character strings and functions [CODSTA-188-3]
      • Do not add or subtract a scaled integer to a pointer [CODSTA-189-3]
      • 'Do' statements should not be used except in a function-like macro [CODSTA-18_b-4]
      • Use the ctype.h facilities for character test [CODSTA-19-3]
      • Do not use object representations to compare floating-point values [CODSTA-190-3]
      • Wrap functions that can spuriously wake up in a loop [CODSTA-191-3]
      • The final member of a structure should not be an array of size '0' or '1' [CODSTA-192-3]
      • Allocate structures containing a flexible array member dynamically [CODSTA-193-3]
      • Wrap functions that can fail spuriously in a loop [CODSTA-194-3]
      • Do not refer to an atomic variable twice in an expression [CODSTA-195-3]
      • Do not modify objects with temporary lifetime [CODSTA-196-3]
      • Do not specify the bound of a character array initialized with a string literal [CODSTA-197-2]
      • The value of a complex expression of floating type should not be cast to a wider floating type [CODSTA-198-3]
      • The value of a complex expression of floating type should not be cast to an integer type [CODSTA-198_b-3]
      • Do not use assertions [CODSTA-199-3]
      • EOS should be used to terminate a string rather than NULL [CODSTA-20-2]
      • Explicitly specify array bounds in array declarations with initializers [CODSTA-200-3]
      • Do not process structured text data natively [CODSTA-201-3]
      • An inline definition of a function with external linkage shall not contain definitions and uses of static objects [CODSTA-202-2]
      • Do not hard code string literals [CODSTA-203-5]
      • Functions declared as 'noreturn' shall have the 'void' return type [CODSTA-204-3]
      • Do not cast an array to the pointer to a structure of a larger size than the size of the array [CODSTA-205-3]
      • The '_Noreturn' function specifier should not be used [CODSTA-206-3]
      • The <stdnoreturn.h> header file should not be used [CODSTA-207-3]
      • The <stdalign.h> header file shall not be used [CODSTA-208-3]
      • The facilities that are specified as being provided by <stdatomic.h> should not be used [CODSTA-209-3]
      • Do not use the macro ATOMIC_VAR_INIT [CODSTA-209_b-3]
      • When using enum, the values of each member should be explicitly declared [CODSTA-21-5]
      • The '_Thread_local' storage class specifier should not be used [CODSTA-210-3]
      • The facilities that are specified as being provided by <threads.h> should not be used [CODSTA-211-3]
      • The 'rsize_t' type should not be used [CODSTA-212-3]
      • The '_Alignas' alignment specifier and the '_Alignof' operator should not be used [CODSTA-213-3]
      • The '_Atomic' type specifier and the '_Atomic' type qualifier should not be used [CODSTA-214-3]
      • The '__STDC_WANT_LIB_EXT1__' macro should not be defined to the value other than '0' [CODSTA-215-3]
      • The '_Generic' operator should not be used [CODSTA-216-3]
      • The 'errno_t' type should not be used [CODSTA-217-3]
      • Do not use following macros: RSIZE_MAX, L_tmpnam_s, TMP_MAX_S [CODSTA-218-3]
      • Do not use the functions defined in Annex K of ISO/IEC 9899:2011 standard [CODSTA-219-3]
      • Local variable or parameter names and class member variable or parent class/struct member variable names shall differ by more than a single character [CODSTA-22-1]
      • Arguments of integer-constant macros should be decimal, octal, or hexadecimal constants with appropriate values [CODSTA-220-3]
      • The small integer variants of the minimum-width integer constant macros should not be used [CODSTA-220_b-3]
      • Do not include any type qualifiers in the specification of a function type [CODSTA-221-3]
      • Avoid implicit integral conversions from a wider to a narrower type [CODSTA-222-3]
      • Fixed width integer types from <cstdint>, indicating the size and signedness, shall be used in place of the basic numerical types [CODSTA-223-3]
      • A typedef should be used in place of the plain char type [CODSTA-223_b-3]
      • The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used [CODSTA-223_c-3]
      • The conditional operator should not be used as a sub-expression [CODSTA-224-3]
      • Floating-point expressions shall not be explicitly (syntactically) tested for equality (==) or inequality (!=) [CODSTA-225-3]
      • The value returned by a standard library function that may return an error should be used [CODSTA-226_a-3]
      • The standard library functions for which return values need not be checked should be cast to 'void' [CODSTA-226_b-5]
      • The value returned by a POSIX library function that may return an error should be used [CODSTA-227-3]
      • Do not call 'getc()', 'putc()', 'getwc()', or 'putwc()' with a stream argument containing assignments, increment or decrement operators [CODSTA-228_a-3]
      • Do not call 'getc()', 'putc()', 'getwc()', or 'putwc()' with a stream argument containing function calls or function-like macro calls [CODSTA-228_b-5]
      • The operands of the remainder operator '%' should be of unsigned integer types [CODSTA-229-4]
      • All 'if' statements should have an 'else' clause [CODSTA-23-3]
      • Do not cast pointers into more strictly aligned pointer types [CODSTA-230-3]
      • The address of an object with thread storage duration shall not be assigned to an object with static storage duration [CODSTA-231-3]
      • The increment (++) and decrement (--) operators should not be mixed with arithmetic operators in an expression [CODSTA-232-3]
      • Types of bit-fields should have defined sizes [CODSTA-233-3]
      • The 'asm' declaration should not be used [CODSTA-234-3]
      • The library functions 'rewind', 'setbuf' and 'ctime' should not be used [CODSTA-235-3]
      • The built-in unary + operator should not be used [CODSTA-236-3]
      • The character handling functions from <cctype> and <cwctype> shall not be used [CODSTA-237-3]
      • The C++ Standard Library functions 'memcpy', 'memmove' and 'memcmp' from <cstring> should not be used [CODSTA-238-3]
      • The literal value zero shall be the only value assigned to errno [CODSTA-239-3]
      • The macro FALSE should be defined as 0 (zero) [CODSTA-24-5]
      • A cast should not convert a pointer type to 'intptr_t' and 'uintptr_t' types [CODSTA-240-3]
      • All 'if...else-if' constructs shall be terminated with an 'else' clause [CODSTA-241-3]
      • The string handling functions from <cstring>, <cstdlib>, <cwchar> and <cinttypes> shall not be used [CODSTA-242-3]
      • The 'switch' statement should not contain labels other than 'case' and 'default' [CODSTA-243-3]
      • The enumeration constant named 'FALSE' should be explicitly initialized by 0 value [CODSTA-25-5]
      • Avoid magic numbers [CODSTA-26-3]
      • Avoid functions that modify global variables [CODSTA-27-3]
      • Define fields for union declarations [CODSTA-28-5]
      • Use meaningful symbolic constants to represent literal values [CODSTA-29-3]
      • Avoid returning handles to function parameters [CODSTA-30-3]
      • A conversion shall not remove any 'const', 'volatile' or '_Atomic' qualification from the type pointed to by a pointer [CODSTA-301-3]
      • The right-hand operand of a constant expression shift operator shall lie between zero and one less than the width in bits of the essential type of the left-hand operand [CODSTA-302-2]
      • A bit-field shall have an appropriate type [CODSTA-304-1]
      • All enumeration values should be representable within the width of the bit-field [CODSTA-305-1]
      • The volatile qualifier shall be used appropriately [CODSTA-306-1]
      • Operands of bitwise and complement operators shall have an unsigned type [CODSTA-307-4]
      • Operands of shift operators shall have an unsigned type [CODSTA-308-3]
      • A conversion from function type to pointer-to-function type shall only occur in appropriate contexts [CODSTA-309-3]
      • Avoid explicit type conversions (casts) [CODSTA-31-3]
      • Integral promotion and the usual arithmetic conversions shall not change the signedness or the type category of an operand [CODSTA-310-4]
      • The address of an object with automatic storage duration shall not be assigned to an object with a greater lifetime [CODSTA-311-2]
      • Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate [CODSTA-312-4]
      • The numeric value of an unscoped enumeration with no fixed underlying type shall not be used [CODSTA-313-3]
      • The 'assert' macro shall not be used with a constant expression [CODSTA-314-2]
      • Legacy 'for' statements should be simple [CODSTA-315-4]
      • Do not write logical expressions of the type if(test) or if(!test)  when test is a pointer [CODSTA-32-3]
      • Do not use operator ++ or -- in the conditional expression of if, while, or switch [CODSTA-33-3]
      • Use a typedef to simplify program syntax when declaring function pointers [CODSTA-34-3]
      • Always provide a default branch for switch statements [CODSTA-35-3]
      • Pass built-in-types by value unless you are modifying them [CODSTA-36-3]
      • Prefer const objects or enums to #defines for simple constants [CODSTA-37-3]
      • Do not use a #define that prevents the compiler from checking types [CODSTA-38-3]
      • Avoid internal or external name conflict with a C++ reserved word [CODSTA-39-1]
      • 'void' should be used when a function is passed or returns no values [CODSTA-40-3]
      • Avoid switch statements with only one case [CODSTA-41-4]
      • The macro TRUE should be defined as 1 [CODSTA-42-5]
      • The enumeration constant named 'TRUE' should be explicitly initialized by 1 value [CODSTA-43-5]
      • Local variables should not use the same names as member variables [CODSTA-44-1]
      • Parameters should not use the same names as member variables [CODSTA-45-1]
      • Use positive logic rather than negative logic whenever practical [CODSTA-46-5]
      • All structures should be typedef'd [CODSTA-47-3]
      • Do not use the following digraphs: <%, %>, <:, :>, %:, %:%: [CODSTA-48-3]
      • Null initialize or increment expressions in for loops will not be used; a while loop will be used instead [CODSTA-49-3]
      • Hexadecimal constants will be represented using all uppercase letters [CODSTA-50-3]
      • Literal suffixes shall use uppercase rather than lowercase letters [CODSTA-51-2]
      • The initialization expression in a for loop will perform no actions other than to initialize the value of a single for loop parameter [CODSTA-52-3]
      • The increment expression in a for loop will perform no action other than to change a single loop parameter to the next value for the loop [CODSTA-53-3]
      • Every switch statement will have at least two cases and a potential default [CODSTA-54-3]
      • Enumeration types shall be used instead of integer types (and constants) as case labels [CODSTA-55-2]
      • All 'case' and 'default' labels of 'switch' statement should have an explicit 'break' or a 'return' statement, or 'fall through' comment [CODSTA-56-3]
      • Suspicious use of semicolon [CODSTA-57-4]
      • Cast to void is not allowed [CODSTA-58-4]
      • Hardcoded array declarations and 'malloc' calls should not be used [CODSTA-59-4]
      • Avoid comparing values with TRUE macro/enum constant using equality operators ("==", "!=") [CODSTA-60-3]
      • The final clause of a switch statement shall be the default-clause unless all enumeration values are tested [CODSTA-61-3]
      • The first or the last label of a switch statement should be the 'default' label unless all enumeration values are tested [CODSTA-61_b-3]
      • A cast shall not convert a pointer to a function to any other pointer type, including a pointer to function type [CODSTA-62-3]
      • Bitwise operators shall only be applied to operands of unsigned underlying type [CODSTA-63-3]
      • Use bitwise operators only on unsigned operands [CODSTA-63_b-3]
      • An unconditional throw or break statement shall terminate every non-empty switch-clause [CODSTA-64-3]
      • Every switch branch should be unconditionally terminated [CODSTA-64_b-3]
      • An object with integer type or pointer to void type shall not be converted to an object with pointer type [CODSTA-65-3]
      • An object with enumeration type shall not be converted to an object with pointer type [CODSTA-65_b-3]
      • Non-constant operands to a binary bitwise operator shall have the same underlying type [CODSTA-66-3]
      • The types used for an object, a function return type, or a function parameter shall be token-for-token identical in all declarations and re-declarations [CODSTA-67-3]
      • The same type aliases shall be used in all declarations of the same entity [CODSTA-67_b-3]
      • A "U" suffix shall be applied to all octal or hexadecimal integer literals of unsigned type [CODSTA-68-3]
      • Expressions with type (plain) char and wchar_t shall not be used as operands to built-in operators other than  =,  ==, != and the unary & operator [CODSTA-69-3]
      • Expressions with type enum shall not be used as operands to built-in operators other than  [ ],  =, ==, !=, <, <=, >, >=, and the unary & operator [CODSTA-70-3]
      • Named bit-fields with signed integer type shall have a length of more than one bit [CODSTA-71-3]
      • Assembler instructions shall only be introduced using the asm declaration [CODSTA-73-3]
      • Bit-fields shall not have enum type [CODSTA-74-3]
      • Bit-fields shall be either bool type or an explicitly unsigned or signed integral type [CODSTA-75-3]
      • The identifier main shall not be used for a function other than the global function main [CODSTA-76-3]
      • The goto statement shall jump to a label declared later in the same function body [CODSTA-77-3]
      • Any label referenced by a goto statement shall be declared in the same block, or in a block enclosing the goto statement [CODSTA-78-3]
      • For any iteration statement there shall be no more than one break or goto statement used for loop termination [CODSTA-79-3]
      • The continue statement shall only be used within a well formed for loop [CODSTA-80-3]
      • If a function has internal linkage then all re-declarations shall include the 'static' storage class specifier [CODSTA-81-3]
      • Avoid infinite loops [CODSTA-82-3]
      • Do not use empty infinite loops [CODSTA-82_b-3]
      • All loops must have a fixed upper or lower bound [CODSTA-83-3]
      • Avoid exit points within infinite loops [CODSTA-85-3]
      • The validity of parameters must be checked inside each function [CODSTA-86-3]
      • Use no more than one level of dereferencing [CODSTA-87-3]
      • Function pointers are not permitted [CODSTA-88-3]
      • The declaration should not contain more than one level of pointer indirection [CODSTA-89-3]
      • Each operand of a logical '&&' or '||' shall be a postfix-expression [CODSTA-90-3]
      • A function shall have at most one exit point [CODSTA-91-3]
      • The names of standard library macros and objects shall not be reused [CODSTA-92-3]
      • Reserved identifiers, macros and functions in the standard library, shall not be defined, redefined or undefined (C90 code) [CODSTA-92_a-3]
      • Reserved identifiers, macros and functions in the standard library, shall not be defined, redefined or undefined (C99 code) [CODSTA-92_b-3]
      • The names of standard library functions shall not be overridden [CODSTA-93-5]
      • Do not declare pointer or array type [CODSTA-94-3]
      • Do not declare pointer type [CODSTA-95-3]
      • Bit-fields shall have explicitly unsigned integral or enumeration types only [CODSTA-96-3]
      • Use parenthesis to clarify expression order if operators with precedence lower than arithmetic are used [CODSTA-97-3]
      • All 'if...else if' constructs will contain either a final else clause or a comment indicating why a final else clause is not necessary [CODSTA-98-3]
      • Signed and unsigned values shall not be mixed in comparison operations [CODSTA-99-3]
    • Comments [COMMENT]
      • Prefer C++ style comment [COMMENT-01-3]
      • Provide copyright information [COMMENT-02-3]
      • Every source file will be documented with an introductory comment that provides information on the file [COMMENT-03-3]
      • Document functions in comments that precede function definitions [COMMENT-04-3]
      • Document functions in comments that precede function declarations [COMMENT-04_b-3]
      • Each variable declaration should be commented [COMMENT-05-3]
      • Each typedef should be commented [COMMENT-06-3]
      • Each enumeration value should be commented [COMMENT-07-3]
      • Each structure member variable should be commented [COMMENT-08-3]
      • All usage of assembler shall be documented [COMMENT-09-3]
      • Use of floating-point arithmetic shall be documented [COMMENT-10-3]
      • The character sequence // shall not be used within a C-style comment [COMMENT-11-3]
      • The character sequence /* shall not be used within a C++-style comment [COMMENT-12-3]
      • Line-splicing shall not be used in // comments [COMMENT-13-2]
      • All declarations of types, data members, and functions should be preceded by a comment annotated with the '@brief' tag [COMMENT-14-3]
      • Function parameters and return type should be documented in a comment that precedes the function declaration [COMMENT-14_b-3]
      • Every function declaration should have a proper documentation [COMMENT-14_c-3]
