      • CWE-704 Incorrect Type Conversion or Cast [CWE-704]
        • Conversions shall not be performed between a pointer to a function and any other type than pointer to function [CWE-704-a-3]
        • Conversions shall not be performed between non compatible pointer to a function types [CWE-704-b-3]
        • Conversions shall not be performed between a pointer to an incomplete type and any other type [CWE-704-c-3]
        • A cast shall not be performed between a pointer to object type and a pointer to a different object type [CWE-704-d-3]
        • A conversion should not be performed between a pointer to object type and an integer type other than 'uintptr_t' or 'intptr_t' [CWE-704-e-4]
        • A conversion should not be performed from pointer to void into pointer to object [CWE-704-f-4]
        • A cast shall not be performed between pointer to void and an arithmetic type [CWE-704-g-3]
        • An implicit conversion shall not be performed between pointer to void and an arithmetic type [CWE-704-h-3]
        • A cast shall not be performed between pointer to object and a non-integer arithmetic type [CWE-704-i-3]
        • Implicit conversions from wider to narrower integral type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [CWE-704-j-3]
        • Implicit conversions from integral to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [CWE-704-k-3]
        • Implicit conversions from integral constant to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [CWE-704-l-3]
      • CWE-732 Incorrect Permission Assignment for Critical Resource [CWE-732]
        • Call 'umask' before calling 'mkstemp' [CWE-732-a-4]
        • Specify the access permission bits if a file is created using the 'open' or 'openat' system call [CWE-732-b-3]
      • CWE-77: Improper Neutralization of Special Elements used in a Command ('Command Injection') [CWE-77]
        • Protect against command injection [CWE-77-a-1]
      • CWE-770 Allocation of Resources Without Limits or Throttling [CWE-770]
        • Validate potentially tainted data before it is used to determine the size of memory allocation [CWE-770-a-2]
      • CWE-772 Missing Release of Resource after Effective Lifetime [CWE-772]
        • Ensure resources are freed [CWE-772-a-1]
        • Define a virtual destructor in classes used as base classes which have virtual functions [CWE-772-b-1]
      • CWE-78 Improper Neutralization of Special Elements used in an OS Command ('OS Command Injection') [CWE-78]
        • Protect against command injection [CWE-78-a-1]
      • CWE-787 Out-of-bounds Write [CWE-787]
        • Avoid accessing arrays out of bounds [CWE-787-a-2]
        • Avoid accessing arrays and pointers out of bounds [CWE-787-b-2]
        • Avoid buffer overflow due to defining incorrect format limits [CWE-787-c-1]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [CWE-787-d-1]
        • Prevent buffer overflows from tainted data [CWE-787-e-1]
        • Avoid buffer write overflow from tainted data [CWE-787-f-1]
        • Ensure the output buffer is large enough when using path manipulation functions [CWE-787-g-3]
      • CWE-798 Use of Hard-coded Credentials [CWE-798]
        • Do not hard code string literals [CWE-798-a-5]
      • CWE-835 Loop with Unreachable Exit Condition ('Infinite Loop') [CWE-835]
        • Avoid infinite loops [CWE-835-a-3]
      • CWE-843: Access of Resource Using Incompatible Type ('Type Confusion') [CWE-843]
        • A cast should not be performed between a pointer to object type and a different pointer to object type [CWE-843-a-3]
      • CWE-863 Incorrect Authorization [CWE-863]
        • Do not use 'cuserid' function [CWE-863-a-2]
      • CWE-89 Improper Neutralization of Special Elements used in an SQL Command ('SQL Injection') [CWE-89]
        • Protect against SQL injection [CWE-89-a-1]
    • Exceptions [EXCEPT]
      • Never allow an exception to be thrown from a destructor, deallocation, and swap [EXCEPT-01-1]
      • Throw by value, catch by reference [EXCEPT-02-1]
      • Do not throw from within destructor [EXCEPT-03-1]
      • All exceptions should be rethrown or logged with standard logger [EXCEPT-04-2]
      • C++ exceptions shall not be used (i.e. throw, catch and try shall not be used.) [EXCEPT-05-2]
      • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [EXCEPT-06-3]
      • An empty throw (throw;) shall only be used in the compound-statement of a catch handler [EXCEPT-07-3]
      • Exceptions shall be raised only after start-up and before termination of the program [EXCEPT-08-3]
      • An exception object should not have pointer type [EXCEPT-09-3]
      • Control shall not be transferred into a try or catch block using a goto or a switch statement [EXCEPT-10-3]
      • The assignment-expression of a throw statement shall not itself cause an exception to be thrown [EXCEPT-11-1]
      • NULL shall not be thrown explicitly [EXCEPT-12-3]
      • Each exception explicitly thrown in the code shall have a handler of a compatible type in all call paths that could lead to that point [EXCEPT-13-3]
      • Where a function's declaration includes an exception-specification, the function shall only be capable of throwing exceptions of the indicated type(s) [EXCEPT-14-3]
      • A class type exception shall always be caught by reference [EXCEPT-15-3]
      • Handlers of a function-try-block implementation of a class constructor or destructor shall not reference nonstatic members from this class or its bases [EXCEPT-16-3]
      • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single try-catch statement or function-try-block for a derived class and some or all of its bases, the handlers shall be ordered most-derived to base class [EXCEPT-17-3]
      • Function called in global or namespace scope shall not throw unhandled exceptions [EXCEPT-18-3]
      • Exception objects must be nothrow copy constructible [EXCEPT-19-3]
      • An explicitly declared copy constructor for a class that inherits from 'std::exception' should have a non-throwing exception specification [EXCEPT-20-3]
      • All user-provided move constructors and move assignment operators shall not exit with an exception [EXCEPT-21-3]
      • Checked exceptions that could be thrown from a function shall be specified in the comment directly before the function declaration [EXCEPT-22-3]
      • Do not use throw exception specifications [EXCEPT-23-3]
      • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single 'try-catch' statement or 'function-try-block', any ellipsis (catch-all) handler shall occur last [EXCEPT-24-3]
      • Do not leave 'catch' blocks empty [EXCEPT-25-3]
      • Avoid using catch-all exception handlers [EXCEPT-26-3]
      • A 'try' statement of a 'try-block' should contain a potentially-throwing statement [EXCEPT-27-3]
    • Formatting [FORMAT]
      • Tabs that do not use ASCII spaces shall not be used [FORMAT-01-5]
      • Place an opening brace '{' on its own line [FORMAT-02-3]
      • Place a closing brace '}' on its own line [FORMAT-03-3]
      • Physical lines should be less than eighty characters [FORMAT-04-3]
      • The length of a macro should not exceed 10 lines [FORMAT-05-3]
      • Only one statement shall be allowed per line [FORMAT-06-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding assignment operators [FORMAT-07-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character following assignment operators [FORMAT-08-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding bitwise operators [FORMAT-09-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character following bitwise operators [FORMAT-10-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding and following bitwise operator '&' [FORMAT-11-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character between a conditional statement keyword and its opening parenthesis [FORMAT-12-3]
      • There shall be a maximum of 1 ASCII space character following the opening parenthesis in conditional statements [FORMAT-13-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding ternary conditional operator [FORMAT-14-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character following ternary conditional operator [FORMAT-15-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding and following relational and equality operators [FORMAT-16-3]
      • There shall be no white space following '.' or '->' operator [FORMAT-17-3]
      • There shall be no white space preceding '.' or '->' operator [FORMAT-18-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character following all commas [FORMAT-19-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character following all semicolons [FORMAT-20-3]
      • There should be no space between a unary operator "!" or "~" and its operand [FORMAT-21-3]
      • There should be no space between a increment/decrement operator (++/--) and its operand [FORMAT-22-3]
      • There shall be no white spaces between the 'return' statement or the 'sizeof' operator and the following opening parenthesis [FORMAT-23-3]
      • There shall be no spaces after the opening '(' and before closing ')' parenthesis that enclose the operand of the 'return' statement or the 'sizeof' operator [FORMAT-24-3]
      • The operand of the 'sizeof' operator should be enclosed in parentheses [FORMAT-25-3]
      • Parenthesis shall be used with the "return" statement [FORMAT-25_b-3]
      • There shall be a single ASCII space character preceding and following logical operators [FORMAT-26-3]
      • Line should be indented by a multiple of four spaces [FORMAT-27-3]
      • In a function definition, the return type of the function should be written on a separate line directly above the function name [FORMAT-28-3]
      • Multiple variable declarations shall not be allowed on the same line [FORMAT-29-3]
      • Place left parenthesis directly after function name [FORMAT-30-3]
      • Separate logical tests in conditional expressions [FORMAT-31-3]
      • The dereference operator '*' and the address-of operator '&' should be directly connected with the type [FORMAT-32-4]
      • Each variable should be declared in a separate declaration statement [FORMAT-33-3]
      • Braces "{}" which enclose a block should be placed in the same column [FORMAT-34-3]
      • When declaring functions, the leading parenthesis and the first argument are to be written on the same line as the function name [FORMAT-35-3]
      • Sibling statement lines should be indented to the same level [FORMAT-36-3]
      • First line in control statement body should be indented more than control statement keyword [FORMAT-37-3]
      • When declaring functions with more than 2 parameters, the leading parenthesis and the first argument are to be written on the same line as the function name, each additional argument will be written on a separate line [FORMAT-38-3]
      • Sort #include directives in alphabetical order [FORMAT-39-4]
      • White spaces after the opening square bracket '[' and before its closing square bracket ']' shall be used in consistent way [FORMAT-40-5]
      • There shall be no space between '[' opening square bracket and preceding token [FORMAT-41-5]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will have nothing else on the line except comments [FORMAT-42-3]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will be placed in the same column [FORMAT-43-3]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will not have an empty line after "{" nor before "}" [FORMAT-44-3]
      • There should be no space between a unary operator "&", "*", "+", "-" and its operand [FORMAT-45-3]
      • There should be no space between an increment/decrement operator (++/--) and its operand in macro definition [FORMAT-46-3]
      • Place CV-qualifiers on the right hand side of the type they apply to [FORMAT-47_a-3]
      • CV-qualifiers shall be placed on the right hand side of the type that is a typedef or a using name [FORMAT-47_b-3]
      • Parameter names in function declarations should not be enclosed in parentheses [FORMAT-48-3]
      • Local variable names in variable declarations should not be enclosed in parentheses [FORMAT-49-3]
      • Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions [FORMAT-50-3]
    • Global Static Analysis [GLOBAL]
      • Explicit alignment specifiers in all declarations of an object with external linkage shall be the same [GLOBAL-ALIGNDECL-2]
      • Functions and objects should not be defined with external linkage if they are referenced in only one translation unit [GLOBAL-AVOIDEXTERN-4]
      • All declarations of an object or function shall have compatible types [GLOBAL-COMPATDECLS-3]
      • Do not use more than one mutex for concurrent waiting operations on a condition variable [GLOBAL-CONDMUTEXVAR-3]
      • If a function is declared with an exception-specification, then all declarations of the same function (in other translation units) shall be declared with the same set of type-ids [GLOBAL-EXCSPECDECL-3]
      • An identifier with external linkage shall have external definition [GLOBAL-NOEXTERNDEF-3]
      • An inline function that is used in multiple translation units shall be defined in one and only one file [GLOBAL-ONEDEFINLINE-3]
      • The One Definition Rule shall not be violated [GLOBAL-ONEDEFRULE-3]
      • A function template that is used in multiple translation units shall be defined in one and only one file [GLOBAL-ONEDEFTEMPL-3]
      • A type that is used in multiple translation units shall be defined in one and only one file [GLOBAL-ONEDEFTYPE-3]
      • An identifier with external linkage shall have no more then one external definition [GLOBAL-ONEEXTERNDEF-3]
      • A type, object or function that is used in multiple translation units shall be declared in one and only one file [GLOBAL-ONEFILEDECL-3]
      • A project shall not contain non-volatile POD variables having only one use [GLOBAL-ONEUSEVAR-3]
      • Predicates shall not have persistent side effects [GLOBAL-PREDICATENOSE-3]
      • Identifiers that define functions with external linkage shall be unique [GLOBAL-REUSEDEXTFUN-3]
      • Identifiers that define objects with external linkage shall be unique [GLOBAL-REUSEDEXTVAR-3]
      • The identifier name of a non-member object with static storage duration shall not be reused within a namespace [GLOBAL-REUSEDQUALGLOBVAR-3]
      • The identifier name of a non-member static function shall not be reused within a namespace [GLOBAL-REUSEDQUALSTATFUN-3]
      • Identifiers that define functions with internal linkage shall be unique [GLOBAL-REUSEDSTATFUN-3]
      • Identifiers that define objects with internal linkage shall be unique [GLOBAL-REUSEDSTATVAR-3]
      • All class templates, function templates, class template member functions and class template static members shall be instantiated at least one [GLOBAL-TEMPLNOINST-3]
      • A class, union or enum name (including qualification, if any) shall be a unique identifier [GLOBAL-UNIQUETYPE-3]
      • A tag name shall be a unique identifier [GLOBAL-UNIQUETYPEC-3]
      • A typedef name (including qualification, if any) shall be a unique identifier [GLOBAL-UNIQUETYPEDEF-3]
      • A typedef name shall be a unique identifier [GLOBAL-UNIQUETYPEDEFC-3]
      • A project should not contain unused variables with external linkage [GLOBAL-UNUSEDEXTVAR-4]
      • Every defined function with external linkage shall be used at least once [GLOBAL-UNUSEDFUNC-3]
      • A project shall not contain unused type declarations [GLOBAL-UNUSEDTYPE-3]
      • There shall be no unused parameters (named or unnamed) in the set of parameters for a virtual function and all the functions that override it [GLOBAL-UNUSEDVIRTPARAM-3]
      • A base class shall only be declared virtual if it is used in a diamond hierarchy [GLOBAL-VIRTBASECLASS-3]
    • High Integrity C++ [HICPP]
      • HIC++ 10.1.1 Ensure that access to base class subobjects does not require explicit disambiguation [HICPP-10_1_1]
        • For multiple inheritance use virtual common base class [HICPP-10_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 10.2.1 Use the override special identifier when overriding a virtual function [HICPP-10_2_1]
        • Each overriding virtual function shall be declared with the override or final specifier [HICPP-10_2_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 10.3.1 Ensure that a derived class has at most one base class which is not an interface class [HICPP-10_3_1]
        • Ensure that a derived class has at most one base class which is not an interface class [HICPP-10_3_1-a-1]
      • HIC++ 11.1.1 Declare all data members private [HICPP-11_1_1]
        • Avoid "public" data members [HICPP-11_1_1-a-2]
        • Avoid 'protected' data members [HICPP-11_1_1-b-2]
      • HIC++ 11.2.1 Do not use friend declarations [HICPP-11_2_1]
        • Avoid using the friend mechanism [HICPP-11_2_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.1.1 Do not declare implicit user defined conversions [HICPP-12_1_1]
        • Constructors allowing for conversion should be made explicit [HICPP-12_1_1-a-1]
        • User-conversion cast operators should be made explicit [HICPP-12_1_1-b-3]
      • HIC++ 12.2.1 Declare virtual, private or protected the destructor of a type used as a base class [HICPP-12_2_1]
        • Make destructors virtual in base classes [HICPP-12_2_1-a-1]
      • HIC++ 12.3.1 Correctly declare overloads for operator new and delete [HICPP-12_3_1]
        • Write operator delete if you write operator new [HICPP-12_3_1-a-3]
        • Write operator delete[] if you write operator new[] [HICPP-12_3_1-b-3]
      • HIC++ 12.4.1 Do not use the dynamic type of an object unless the object is fully constructed [HICPP-12_4_1]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under construction [HICPP-12_4_1-b-2]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under destruction [HICPP-12_4_1-c-2]
      • HIC++ 12.4.2 Ensure that a constructor initializes explicitly all base classes and non-static data members [HICPP-12_4_2]
        • All member variables should be initialized in constructor [HICPP-12_4_2-a-1]
      • HIC++ 12.4.3 Do not specify both an NSDMI and a member initializer in a constructor for the same non static member [HICPP-12_4_3]
        • Do not specify both an NSDMI and a member initializer in a constructor for the same non-static member [HICPP-12_4_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.4.4 Write members in an initialization list in the order in which they are declared [HICPP-12_4_4]
        • List members in an initialization list in the order in which they are declared [HICPP-12_4_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.4.5 Use delegating constructors to reduce code duplication [HICPP-12_4_5]
        • Use delegating constructors to reduce code duplication [HICPP-12_4_5-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.1 Define explicitly =default or =delete implicit special member functions of concrete classes [HICPP-12_5_1]
        • Explicitly define =default or =delete special member functions of concrete classes implicitly provided by the compiler [HICPP-12_5_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.2 Define special members =default if the behavior is equivalent [HICPP-12_5_2]
        • Define special members as =default when the behavior is equivalent to the compiler's behavior [HICPP-12_5_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.3 Ensure that a user defined move/copy constructor only moves/copies base and member objects [HICPP-12_5_3]
        • A copy constructor shall only initialize its base classes and the non-static members of the class of which it is a member [HICPP-12_5_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.4 Declare noexcept the move constructor and move assignment operator [HICPP-12_5_4]
        • All user-provided move constructors and move assignment operators shall not exit with an exception [HICPP-12_5_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.6 Use an atomic, non-throwing swap operation to implement the copy and move assignment operators [HICPP-12_5_6]
        • User-defined copy and move assignment operators should use user-defined no-throw swap function [HICPP-12_5_6-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.7 Declare assignment operators with the ref-qualifier & [HICPP-12_5_7]
        • Declare assignment operators with the ref-qualifier & [HICPP-12_5_7-a-3]
      • HIC++ 12.5.8 Make the copy assignment operator of an abstract class protected or define it =delete [HICPP-12_5_8]
        • The copy assignment operator shall be declared protected or private in an abstract class [HICPP-12_5_8-a-3]
      • HIC++ 13.1.1 Ensure that all overloads of a function are visible from where it is called [HICPP-13_1_1]
        • Member functions declared in derived class should not hide functions declared in base classes [HICPP-13_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 13.1.2 If a member of a set of callable functions includes a universal reference parameter, ensure that one appears in the same position for all other members [HICPP-13_1_2]
        • Avoid Overloading on Forwarding References [HICPP-13_1_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 13.2.1 Do not overload operators with special semantics [HICPP-13_2_1]
        • Avoid overloading logical operators AND, OR (&&, ||) [HICPP-13_2_1-a-3]
        • Avoid overloading comma operator "," [HICPP-13_2_1-b-3]
      • HIC++ 13.2.2 Ensure that the return type of an overloaded binary operator matches the built-in counterparts [HICPP-13_2_2]
        • A relational operator shall return a boolean value [HICPP-13_2_2-a-3]
        • A binary arithmetic operator and a bitwise operator shall return a 'prvalue' [HICPP-13_2_2-b-3]
      • HIC++ 13.2.3 Declare binary arithmetic and bitwise operators as non-members [HICPP-13_2_3]
        • Declare binary arithmetic and bitwise operators as non-members [HICPP-13_2_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 13.2.4 When overloading the subscript operator (operator[]) implement both const and non-const versions [HICPP-13_2_4]
        • When overloading the subscript operator (operator[]), implement both const and non-const versions [HICPP-13_2_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 13.2.5 Implement a minimal set of operators and use them to implement all other related operators [HICPP-13_2_5]
        • The overloaded binary operator should be implemented in terms of its corresponding compound assignment operator [HICPP-13_2_5-a-3]
      • HIC++ 14.1.1 Use variadic templates rather than an ellipsis [HICPP-14_1_1]
        • Do not use functions with variable numbers of arguments [HICPP-14_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 14.2.1 Declare template specializations in the same file as the primary template they specialize. [HICPP-14_2_1]
        • All partial and explicit specializations for a template shall be declared in the same file as the declaration of their primary template [HICPP-14_2_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 14.2.2 Do not explicitly specialize a function template that is overloaded with other templates [HICPP-14_2_2]
        • Overloaded function templates shall not be explicitly specialized [HICPP-14_2_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 14.2.3 Declare extern an explicitly instantiated template [HICPP-14_2_3]
        • Declare 'extern' an explicitly instantiated template [HICPP-14_2_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 15.1.1 Only use instances of std::exception for exceptions [HICPP-15_1_1]
        • Only use instances of std::exception for exceptions [HICPP-15_1_1-a-3]
        • Always throw the created std::exception object [HICPP-15_1_1-b-3]
      • HIC++ 15.2.1 Do not throw an exception from a destructor [HICPP-15_2_1]
        • Do not throw from within destructor [HICPP-15_2_1-a-1]
      • HIC++ 15.3.1 Do not access non-static members from a catch handler of constructor/destructor function try block [HICPP-15_3_1]
        • Handlers of a function-try-block implementation of a class constructor or destructor shall not reference nonstatic members from this class or its bases [HICPP-15_3_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 15.3.2 Ensure that a program does not result in a call to std::terminate [HICPP-15_3_2]
        • Always catch exceptions [HICPP-15_3_2-a-1]
        • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [HICPP-15_3_2-b-3]
        • Avoid throwing exceptions from functions that are declared not to throw [HICPP-15_3_2-c-2]
      • HIC++ 16.1.1 Use the preprocessor only for implementing include guards, and including header files with include guards [HICPP-16_1_1]
        • Avoid using macro definitions [HICPP-16_1_1-a-3]
        • The #ifndef pre-processor directive will only be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [HICPP-16_1_1-b-3]
        • The #ifdef, #else, #elif preprocessor directives should not be used [HICPP-16_1_1-c-3]
        • Use multiple include guards [HICPP-16_1_1-d-3]
        • The #endif pre-processor directives will only be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [HICPP-16_1_1-e-3]
        • The #if pre-processor directive will only be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [HICPP-16_1_1-f-3]
        • #error directive shall not be used [HICPP-16_1_1-g-3]
        • The #pragma directive shall not be used [HICPP-16_1_1-h-3]
        • #undef shall not be used [HICPP-16_1_1-i-3]
      • HIC++ 16.1.2 Do not include a path specifier in filenames supplied in #include directives [HICPP-16_1_2]
        • Do not allow absolute or relative path names in #include statements [HICPP-16_1_2-a-2]
        • The \ character should not occur in a header file name [HICPP-16_1_2-b-3]
      • HIC++ 16.1.3 Match the filename in a #include directive to the one on the filesystem [HICPP-16_1_3]
        • Match the filename in a #include directive to the one on the filesystem [HICPP-16_1_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 16.1.4 Use <> brackets for system and standard library headers. Use quotes for all other headers [HICPP-16_1_4]
        • Use <> brackets for system and standard library headers. Use quotes for all other headers [HICPP-16_1_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 16.1.5 Include directly the minimum number of headers required for compilation [HICPP-16_1_5]
        • Avoid duplication of #include directives [HICPP-16_1_5-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.1.1 Do not use std::vector [HICPP-17_1_1]
        • Avoid using vector<bool> [HICPP-17_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.2.1 Wrap use of the C Standard Library [HICPP-17_2_1]
        • Wrap use of the C Standard Library [HICPP-17_2_1-a-4]
        • The error indicator 'errno' shall not be used [HICPP-17_2_1-b-3]
      • HIC++ 17.3.1 Do not use std::move on objects declared with const or const & type [HICPP-17_3_1]
        • Do not use std::move on objects declared with the const or const & type [HICPP-17_3_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.3.2 Use std::forward to forward universal references [HICPP-17_3_2]
        • The 'std::forward' function should be used to forward forwarding references [HICPP-17_3_2-a-3]
        • The 'std::forward' function should only be used to forward forwarding references [HICPP-17_3_2-b-3]
        • The 'std::move' function should be used to forward rvalue references [HICPP-17_3_2-c-3]
      • HIC++ 17.3.3 Do not subsequently use the argument to std::forward [HICPP-17_3_3]
        • Do not subsequently use the argument to std::forward [HICPP-17_3_3-a-2]
      • HIC++ 17.3.4 Do not create smart pointers of array type [HICPP-17_3_4]

      • HIC++ 17.3.5 Do not create an rvalue reference of std::array [HICPP-17_3_5]
        • Do not create an rvalue reference of std::array [HICPP-17_3_5-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.4.1 Use const container calls when result is immediately converted to a const iterator [HICPP-17_4_1]
        • Use const container calls when the result is immediately converted to a const iterator [HICPP-17_4_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.4.2 Use API calls that construct objects in place [HICPP-17_4_2]
        • Prefer 'std::make_shared' to the direct use of new [HICPP-17_4_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 17.5.1 Do not ignore the result of std::remove, std::remove if or std::unique [HICPP-17_5_1]
        • Follow remove-like algorithms by erase to remove elements from a container [HICPP-17_5_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 18.1.1 Do not use platform specific multi-threading facilities [HICPP-18_1_1]
        • Do not use platform-specific multi-threading facilities [HICPP-18_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 18.2.1 Use high integrity::thread in place of std::thread [HICPP-18_2_1]
        • Use high_integrity::thread in place of std::thread [HICPP-18_2_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 18.2.2 Synchronize access to data shared between threads using a single lock [HICPP-18_2_2]
        • Do not use global variable with different locks set [HICPP-18_2_2-a-1]
        • Make const member functions thread-safe [HICPP-18_2_2-b-2]
      • HIC++ 18.2.3 Do not share volatile data between threads [HICPP-18_2_3]
        • Do not share volatile data between threads [HICPP-18_2_3-a-3]

      • HIC++ 1.2.1 Ensure that all statements are reachable [HICPP-1_2_1]

      • HIC++ 3.1.1 Do not hide declarations [HICPP-3_1_1]

      • HIC++ 5.1.1 Use symbolic names instead of literal values in code [HICPP-5_1_1]
        • Avoid magic numbers [HICPP-5_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 5.1.2 Do not rely on the sequence of evaluation within an expression [HICPP-5_1_2]
        • The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [HICPP-5_1_2-a-3]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function arguments [HICPP-5_1_2-b-1]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function designator and function arguments [HICPP-5_1_2-c-3]

        • Between sequence points an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression [HICPP-5_1_2-e-3]

        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function calls [HICPP-5_1_2-g-3]
        • The increment (++) and decrement (--) operators should not be mixed with other operators in an expression [HICPP-5_1_2-h-3]

        • The function call that causes the side effect shall not be the operand of the sizeof operator [HICPP-5_1_6-c-3]

        • C-style casts should not be used [HICPP-5_4_1-a-3]
        • Avoid using reinterpret_cast [HICPP-5_4_1-b-3]

        • 'if' and 'else' should be followed by a compound statement [HICPP-6_1_1-b-3]

      • HIC++ 6.2.1 Implement a loop that only uses element values as a range-based loop [HICPP-6_2_1]

      • HIC++ 8.3.4 Define =delete functions with parameters of type rvalue reference to const [HICPP-8_3_4]
        • Define =delete functions with parameters of type rvalue reference to const [HICPP-8_3_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 8.4.1 Do not access an invalid object or an object with indeterminate value [HICPP-8_4_1]
        • Avoid use before initialization [HICPP-8_4_1-a-1]
        • Do not use resources that have been freed [HICPP-8_4_1-b-1]
        • All automatic variables shall have been assigned a value before being used [HICPP-8_4_1-c-3]
      • HIC++ 8.4.2 Ensure that a braced aggregate initializer matches the layout of the aggregate object [HICPP-8_4_2]
        • The initializer for an aggregate or union shall be enclosed in braces [HICPP-8_4_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.1.1 Declare static any member function that does not require this. Alternatively, declare const any member function that does not modify the externally visible state of the object [HICPP-9_1_1]
        • If a member function can be made static then it shall be made static, otherwise if it can be made const then it shall be made const [HICPP-9_1_1-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.1.2 Make default arguments the same or absent when overriding a virtual function [HICPP-9_1_2]
        • Do not redefine an inherited virtual function with a different default parameter value [HICPP-9_1_2-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.1.3 Do not return non-const handles to class data from const member functions [HICPP-9_1_3]
        • Const member functions shall not return non-const pointers or references to class-data [HICPP-9_1_3-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.1.4 Do not write member functions which return non-const handles to data less accessible than the member function [HICPP-9_1_4]
        • Public member functions shall not return non-const handles to private/protected class-data [HICPP-9_1_4-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.1.5 Do not introduce virtual functions in a final class [HICPP-9_1_5]
        • Do not introduce virtual functions in a final class [HICPP-9_1_5-a-3]
      • HIC++ 9.2.1 Declare bit-fields with an explicitly unsigned integral or enumeration type [HICPP-9_2_1]
        • Bit-fields shall have explicitly unsigned integral or enumeration types only [HICPP-9_2_1-a-3]
    • Initialization [INIT]
      • Objects with external linkage should not be initialized in a header file [INIT-01-3]
      • Do not initialize unsigned integer variables with signed constants [INIT-02-3]
      • Initialize all variables [INIT-03-3]
      • Initialize all pointer variables [INIT-04-2]
      • Do not initialize a reference to an object whose address can be changed [INIT-05-1]
      • All member variables should be initialized in constructor [INIT-06-1]
      • Make class members' initialization explicit by providing user-defined constructor [INIT-07-3]
      • User-defined constructor must be provided to ensure the proper initialization of dynamically allocated class objects [INIT-08-3]
      • Initialize static class members [INIT-09-1]
      • List members in an initialization list in the order in which they are declared [INIT-10-3]
      • All non-class variables with automatic storage duration should be explicitly initialized [INIT-101-3]
      • An assignment operator shall assign all data members [INIT-11-2]
      • Avoid initialization order problems across translation units by replacing non-local static objects with local static objects [INIT-12-3]
      • Do not assume that members are initialized in any special order in constructors [INIT-13-3]
      • Do not use uninitialized nonstatic member variables in base class constructors [INIT-13_a-1]
      • Do not use uninitialized nonstatic member variables of nonvirtual base classes in virtual base class constructors [INIT-13_b-1]
      • Do not use possibly uninitialized nonstatic member variables of base classes in base class constructors [INIT-13_c-3]
      • Prefer initialization to assignment in constructors [INIT-14-5]
      • Consider adding constructor to initialize 'struct' member variables [INIT-15-4]
      • The initializer for an aggregate or union shall be enclosed in braces [INIT-16-3]
      • The data members initialized with the same constant values across all constructors should be initialized using NSDMI [INIT-17-3]
      • User-defined constructors that initialize data members with the same constant values across all constructors should initialize using NSDMI instead [INIT-17_b-3]
      • Both NSDMI and a non-static member initializer in a constructor shall not be used in the same type [INIT-18-3]
      • All direct, non-static data members of a non-aggregate class should be initialized at the top of a constructor body [INIT-19-3]
      • All direct, non-static data members of an aggregate class should be initialized as soon as the object is created [INIT-20-3]
    • Joint Strike Fighter [JSF]
      • Any one function (or method) will contain no more than 200 logical source lines of code (L-SLOCs) [JSF-001-3]
      • All functions shall have a cyclomatic complexity number of 20 or less [JSF-003-2]
      • Follow the Essential Complexity limit of 1 [JSF-003_b-2]
      • Only those characters specified in the C++ basic source character set will be used [JSF-009-3]
      • Values of character types will be restricted to a defined and documented subset of ISO 10646-1 [JSF-010-3]
      • Trigraphs will not be used [JSF-011-3]
      • The following digraphs will not be used <%, %>, <:, :>, %:, %:%: [JSF-012-3]
      • Wide string literals (for example L"abc") will not be used [JSF-013-3]
      • Capital 'L' shall be used instead of lowercase 'l' to indicate long [JSF-014-2]
      • Ensure that array indices are within the bounds of the array [JSF-015-2]
      • The error indicator 'errno' shall not be used [JSF-017-2]
      • The macro 'offsetof', in library <stddef.h>, shall not be used [JSF-018-2]
      • 'setlocale' function shall not be used [JSF-019-2]
      • <locale.h> shall not be used [JSF-019_b-2]
      • The 'setjmp' macro and the 'longjmp' function shall not be used [JSF-020-2]
      • The standard header file <setjmp.h> shall not be used [JSF-020_b-2]
      • The standard header file <signal.h> shall not be used [JSF-021-2]
      • The signal handling facilities of <signal.h> shall not be used [JSF-021_b-2]
      • The input/output library <stdio.h> shall not be used [JSF-022-2]
      • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library <stdlib.h> shall not be used [JSF-023-2]
      • The library function 'abort' of <stdlib.h> shall not be used [JSF-024-2]
      • The library function 'exit' of <stdlib.h> shall not be used [JSF-024_b-2]
      • The library function 'getenv' of <stdlib.h> shall not be used [JSF-024_c-2]
      • The library function 'system' of <stdlib.h> shall not be used [JSF-024_d-2]
      • The time handling functions of library <time.h> shall not be used [JSF-025-2]
      • The #ifdef, #else, #elif preprocessor directives should not be used [JSF-026-2]
      • The #if preprocessor directive should not be used [JSF-026_b-2]
      • #error directive shall not be used [JSF-026_c-2]
      • The #pragma directive shall not be used [JSF-026_d-2]
      • #undef shall not be used [JSF-026_e-2]
      • #ifndef, #define and #endif will be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [JSF-027-3]
      • The #ifndef pre-processor directive will only be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [JSF-028-3]
      • The #endif pre-processor directives will only be used to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [JSF-028_b-3]
      • The #define pre-processor directive shall not be used to create inline macros [JSF-029-2]
      • The #define pre-processor directive shall not be used to define constant values [JSF-030-2]
      • The #define pre-processor directive will only be used as part of the technique to prevent multiple inclusions of the same header file [JSF-031-3]
      • The #include pre-processor directive will only be used to include header (*.h) files [JSF-032-3]
      • The #include directive shall use the <filename.h> notation to include header files [JSF-033-2]
      • A header file will contain a mechanism that prevents multiple inclusions of itself [JSF-035-3]
      • A file should directly include only headers containing declarations and definitions needed to a compilation [JSF-037-4]
      • Header files (*.h) will not contain non-const variable definitions or function definitions [JSF-039_a-3]
      • Source lines will be kept to a length of 120 characters or less [JSF-041-3]
      • Each expression-statement will be on a separate line [JSF-042-3]
      • Tabs should be avoided [JSF-043-4]
      • All indentations will be consistent [JSF-044-3]
      • User-specified C++ external identifiers should differ in the first 64 characters [JSF-046_a-2]
      • User-specified C++ internal identifiers should differ from external identifiers in the first 64 characters [JSF-046_b-2]
      • User-specified C++ internal identifiers declared in the same scope should differ in the first 64 characters [JSF-046_c-2]
      • Identifiers will not begin with the underscore character "_" [JSF-047-3]
      • Identifiers will not differ by mixture of case, the underscore character, interchange of the similarly looking letters and numbers [JSF-048-3]
      • Begin class, struct, union, enum, and typedef names with an uppercase letter [JSF-050-3]
      • All letters contained in function and variable names will be composed entirely of lowercase letters [JSF-051-3]
      • Identifiers for constant and enumerator values shall be lowercase [JSF-052-2]
      • Header files will always have a file name extension of ".h" [JSF-053-3]
      • The following character sequences shall not appear in header file names: ', \, /*, //, or "  [JSF-053.1-2]
      • Implementation files will always have a file name extension of ".cpp" [JSF-054-3]
      • The public section of a class will be declared before the protected section and before the private section [JSF-057_a-3]
      • The protected section of a class will be declared before the private section [JSF-057_b-3]
      • When declaring functions with more than 2 parameters, the leading parenthesis and the first argument are to be written on the same line as the function name, each additional argument will be written on a separate line [JSF-058-3]
      • The statements forming the body of a 'while', 'do...while', 'switch' or 'for' statement shall always be enclosed in braces [JSF-059_a-2]
      • The statements forming the body of an 'if', 'else if' or 'else' statement shall always be enclosed in braces [JSF-059_b-2]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will have nothing else on the line except comments [JSF-060_a-3]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will be placed in the same column [JSF-060_b-3]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will not have an empty line after "{" nor before "}" [JSF-060_c-3]
      • Braces ("{}") which enclose a block will have nothing else on the line except comments [JSF-061-3]
      • The dereference operator '*' and the address-of operator '&' will be directly connected with the type-specifier [JSF-062-3]
      • There will be no white space following '.' or '->' operator [JSF-063_a-3]
      • There will be no white space preceding '.' or '->' operator [JSF-063_b-3]
      • There will be no space between a unary operator '!' or '~' and its operand [JSF-063_c-3]
      • There will be no space between a increment/decrement operator (++/--) and its operand [JSF-063_d-3]
      • There will be no space between a unary operator '&', '*', '+', '-' and its operand [JSF-063_e-3]
      • There should be no space between an increment/decrement operator (++/--) and its operand in macro definition [JSF-063_f-3]
      • Public data should only be used in structs, not in classes [JSF-067_a-4]
      • Protected data should only be used in structs, not in classes [JSF-067_b-4]
      • Declare both private copy constructor and copy assignment operator at the same time [JSF-068-2]
      • A member function that does not affect the state of an object will be declared const [JSF-069-3]
      • Avoid using the friend mechanism [JSF-070-4]
      • Freed memory shall not be accessed under any circumstances [JSF-070.1-2]
      • Destructor shall not be called manually [JSF-070.1_b-2]
      • Public and protected methods shall not be invoked by class constructor [JSF-071-2]
      • A class's virtual functions shall not be invoked from any of its constructors [JSF-071.1-2]
      • A class's virtual functions shall not be invoked from its destructor [JSF-071.1_b-2]
      • All member variables shall be initialized in constructor [JSF-071_b-2]
      • A class's virtual functions shall not be invoked from any of its constructors [JSF-071_c-2]
      • Uninitialized nonstatic member variables shall not be used in base class constructors [JSF-071_d-2]
      • Uninitialized nonstatic member variables of nonvirtual base classes shall not be used in virtual base class constructors [JSF-071_e-2]
      • Possibly uninitialized nonstatic member variables of base classes shall not be used in base class constructors [JSF-071_f-2]
      • Initialization of nonstatic class members will be performed through the member initialization list rather than through assignment in the body of a constructor [JSF-074-3]
      • Members of the initialization list shall be listed in the order in which they are declared in the class [JSF-075-2]
      • A copy constructor and a copy assignment operator shall be declared for classes that contain pointers to data items or nontrivial destructors [JSF-076-2]
      • A copy constructor shall copy all data members and bases [JSF-077-2]
      • The definition of a constructor shall not contain default arguments that produce a signature identical to that of the implicitly-declared copy constructor [JSF-077.1-2]
      • All base classes with a virtual function shall define a virtual destructor [JSF-078-2]
      • Call fclose() on pointer member in destructor if the pointer was used to open a file [JSF-079-2]
      • Call delete on pointer members in destructors [JSF-079_b-2]
      • The assignment operator shall handle self-assignment correctly [JSF-081-2]
      • An assignment operator shall return a reference to *this [JSF-082-2]
      • An assignment operator shall assign all data members [JSF-083_a-2]
      • An assignment operator shall assign all data bases [JSF-083_b-2]
      • When two operators are opposites (such as == and !=), both will be defined [JSF-085-3]
      • When one of opposite operators (== and !=) is defined, the other should be defined too and one will be defined in terms of the other [JSF-085_a-3]
      • Hierarchies should be based on abstract classes [JSF-087-4]
      • Multiple inheritance shall be limited to at most 1 protected implementation [JSF-088-2]
      • A stateful virtual base shall be explicitly declared in each derived class that accesses it [JSF-088.1-2]
      • Multiple inheritance shall not use any public implementations [JSF-088_b-2]
      • A base class shall not be both virtual and non-virtual in the same hierarchy [JSF-089-2]
      • An inherited nonvirtual function shall not be redefined in a derived class [JSF-094-2]
      • Member functions declared in derived class shall not hide functions declared in base classes [JSF-094_b-2]
      • An inherited default parameter shall never be redefined [JSF-095-2]
      • Arrays shall not be treated polymorphically [JSF-096-2]
      • Arrays shall not be used in interfaces [JSF-097-2]
      • Neither operand of an equality operator (== or !=) shall be a pointer to a virtual member function [JSF-097.1-2]
      • Arrays shall not be used in private or protected methods [JSF-097_b-2]
      • Arrays shall not be used in global functions [JSF-097_c-2]
      • Arrays shall not be passed to functions as array/pointer parameters [JSF-097_d-2]
      • Functions which are called with array argument shall not be declared with pointer parameter [JSF-097_e-2]
      • Every nonlocal name, except main(), should be placed in some namespace [JSF-098-4]
      • Namespaces will not be nested more than two levels deep [JSF-099-3]
      • Don't write namespace usings in a header file or before an #include [JSF-100-4]
      • All partial and explicit specializations for a template should be declared in the same file as the declaration of their primary template [JSF-104-3]
      • In a class template with a dependent base, any name that may be found in that dependent base should be referred to using a qualifier [JSF-105-4]
      • Functions shall always be declared at file scope [JSF-107-2]
      • Functions with variable numbers of arguments shall not be used [JSF-108-2]
      • A function definition should not be placed in a class specification [JSF-109-4]
      • Functions with more than 7 arguments will not be used [JSF-110-3]
      • A function shall not return a pointer or reference to a non-static local object [JSF-111-2]
      • A function shall not return a pointer or a reference to a parameter that is passed by const reference [JSF-111_a-2]
      • Dereferenced local pointer initialized by new in function scope should not be returned [JSF-112-4]
      • Functions will have a single exit point [JSF-113-3]
      • All exit points of value-returning functions shall be through return statements [JSF-114-2]
      • If a function returns error information, then that error information will be tested [JSF-115-3]
      • Value returned by a function having a non-void return type that is not an overloaded operator shall always be used [JSF-115_a-4]
      • Built-in-types should be passed by value unless you are modifying them [JSF-116-4]
      • Arguments should be passed by reference [JSF-117-4]
      • An object should be passed as const reference if the function should not change the value of the object [JSF-117.1-4]
      • The class object should be passed by reference if the class has non-static pointers and has no declared copy constructor [JSF-117_b-4]
      • A pointer parameter in a function prototype should be declared as pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [JSF-118-4]
      • Declare a type of parameter as typedef to pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [JSF-118_b-4]
      • Functions shall not call themselves, either directly or indirectly [JSF-119-2]
      • Only functions with 1 or 2 statements should be considered candidates for inline functions [JSF-121-4]
      • Trivial accessor and mutator functions should be inlined [JSF-122-4]
      • Classes which have only getters/setters (accessors/mutators) are not allowed [JSF-123-4]
      • Trivial forwarding functions should be inlined [JSF-124-4]
      • Pass and return by reference when possible [JSF-125_a-4]
      • Consider using op= instead of stand-alone op [JSF-125_b-5]
      • Only valid C++ style comments (//) shall be used [JSF-126-2]
      • Code that is not used (commented out) shall be deleted [JSF-127-2]
      • Each variable declaration will be commented [JSF-132_a-3]
      • Each typedef will be commented [JSF-132_b-3]
      • Each enumeration value will be commented [JSF-132_c-3]
      • Each structure member variable will be commented [JSF-132_d-3]
      • Every source file will be documented with an introductory comment that provides information on the file [JSF-133_a-3]
      • Every source file will contain copyright information [JSF-133_b-3]
      • Document functions in comments that precede function definitions [JSF-134-4]
      • Document functions in comments that precede function declarations [JSF-134_b-4]
      • Identifier declared in a local or function prototype scope shall not hide an identifier declared in a global or namespace scope [JSF-135_a-2]
      • Identifiers declared in an inner local scope shall not hide identifiers declared in an outer local scope [JSF-135_b-2]
      • Identifiers declared in a local scope shall not hide identifiers declared in a class scope [JSF-135_c-2]
      • Identifiers declared in a class scope shall not hide identifiers declared in a global or namespace scope [JSF-135_d-2]
      • Identifiers declared in an inner class scope shall not hide identifiers declared in outer class scope [JSF-135_e-2]
      • Objects should be defined at block scope if they are only accessed from within a single function [JSF-136_a-4]
      • Declarations of local variables should be at the smallest feasible scope [JSF-136_b-4]
      • All declarations at file scope should be static where possible [JSF-137-4]
      • Identifiers shall not simultaneously have both internal and external linkage in the same translation unit [JSF-138_a-2]
      • The static storage class specifier shall be used in definitions and declarations of objects and functions that have internal linkage [JSF-138_b-2]
      • External objects will not be declared in more than one file [JSF-139-3]
      • External objects will not be declared in implementation files [JSF-139_b-3]
      • The register storage class specifier shall not be used [JSF-140-2]
      • A class, structure, or enumeration will not be declared in the definition of its type [JSF-141-3]
      • All automatic variables shall have been assigned a value before being used [JSF-142_a-2]
      • All variables shall be initialized before use [JSF-142_b-2]
      • Variables will not be introduced until they can be initialized with meaningful values [JSF-143-3]
      • Avoid unused local variables [JSF-143_a-3]
      • Braces shall be used to indicate and match the structure in the non-zero initialization of arrays and structures [JSF-144-2]
      • In an enumerator list, the '=' construct shall not be used to explicitly initialize members other than the first, unless all items are explicitly initialized [JSF-145-2]
      • The underlying bit representations of floating point numbers shall not be used in any way by the programmer [JSF-147-2]
      • Enumeration types shall be used instead of integer types (and constants) to select from a limited series of choices [JSF-148-2]
      • Octal constants (other than zero) shall not be used [JSF-149-2]
      • Hexadecimal constants will be represented using all uppercase letters [JSF-150-3]
      • Numeric values in code will not be used; symbolic values will be used instead [JSF-151-3]
      • A string literal shall not be modified [JSF-151.1-2]
      • Multiple variable declarations shall not be allowed on the same line [JSF-152-2]
      • Unions shall not be used [JSF-153-2]
      • Bit-fields shall have explicitly unsigned integral or enumeration types only [JSF-154-2]
      • All the members of a structure (or class) shall be named [JSF-156-2]
      • The right hand operand of a && or || operator shall not contain side effects [JSF-157-2]
      • The operands of a logical && or || shall be parenthesized if the operands contain binary operators [JSF-158-2]
      • Operators ||, && shall not be overloaded [JSF-159-2]
      • Operator unary & shall not be overloaded [JSF-159_b-2]
      • An assignment expression shall be used only as the expression in an expression statement [JSF-160-2]
      • Signed and unsigned values shall not be mixed in comparison operations [JSF-162_a-2]
      • Signed and unsigned values shall not be mixed in second and third operand of conditional operator [JSF-162_b-2]
      • Signed and unsigned values shall not be mixed in arithmetic operations [JSF-162_c-2]
      • Unsigned arithmetic shall not be used [JSF-163-2]
      • The right hand operand of a shift operator shall lie between zero and one less than the width in bits of the left-hand operand [JSF-164-2]
      • The left-hand operand of a right-shift operator shall not have a negative value [JSF-164.1-2]
      • The unary minus operator shall not be applied to an unsigned expression [JSF-165-2]
      • The sizeof operator will not be used on expressions that contain side effects [JSF-166-3]
      • The sizeof operator will not be used on expressions that contain side effects [JSF-166_b-3]
      • The sizeof operator will not be used on expressions that contain side effects [JSF-166_c-3]
      • The implementation of integer division shall be documented [JSF-167-3]
      • Don't assign the dividend of two integers to a floating-point type [JSF-167_a-2]
      • The comma operator shall not be used [JSF-168_b-2]
      • Pointers to pointers should be avoided [JSF-169-4]
      • More than 2 levels of pointer indirection shall not be used [JSF-170-2]
      • Relational operators shall not be applied to pointer types except where they point to the same array [JSF-171-2]
      • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be assigned to an object which persists after the object has ceased to exist [JSF-173-2]
      • The null pointer shall not be de-referenced [JSF-174_a-2]
      • The null pointer shall not be de-referenced [JSF-174_b-2]
      • NULL identifier shall not be used; use plain 0 instead [JSF-175-2]
      • A typedef will be used to simplify program syntax when declaring function pointers [JSF-176-3]
      • User-defined conversion functions should be avoided [JSF-177-4]
      • Constructors allowing for conversion should be made explicit [JSF-177_b-4]
      • Down casting (casting from base to derived class) shall not be allowed [JSF-178-2]
      • A pointer to a virtual base class shall not be converted to a pointer to a derived class [JSF-179-2]
      • Implicit conversions from wider to narrower integral type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [JSF-180_a-2]
      • Avoid implicit conversions from floating to integral type [JSF-180_b-2]
      • Avoid implicit conversions from wider to narrower floating type [JSF-180_c-2]
      • Avoid conversions of constant values to a narrower type [JSF-180_d-2]
      • Avoid implicit conversions from signed to unsigned type [JSF-180_e-2]
      • Implicit conversions from integral to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [JSF-180_f-2]
      • Implicit conversions from integral constant to floating type which may result in a loss of information shall not be used [JSF-180_g-2]
      • Redundant explicit casts will not be used [JSF-181_a-3]
      • Avoid explicit cast from derived to a base class [JSF-181_b-3]
      • Type casting from any type to or from pointers shall not be used [JSF-182-2]
      • Every possible measure should be taken to avoid type casting [JSF-183-4]
      • Avoid using static_cast on pointers [JSF-183_a-4]
      • Avoid using reinterpret_cast [JSF-183_b-4]
      • Floating point numbers shall not implicitly be converted to integers [JSF-184_a-2]
      • C-style casts (other than void casts) and functional notation casts (other than explicit constructor calls) shall not be used [JSF-185-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code in 'else' block [JSF-186_a-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code after 'return', 'break', 'continue', and 'goto' statements [JSF-186_b-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code in 'if', 'else', 'while' and 'for' block [JSF-186_c-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code in 'switch' statement [JSF-186_d-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code in 'for' loop [JSF-186_e-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code after 'if' or 'switch' statement [JSF-186_f-2]
      • There shall be no unreachable code after 'if' or 'switch' statement inside 'while', 'for' or 'do...while' loop [JSF-186_g-2]
      • Every defined function with internal linkage shall be used [JSF-186_h-2]
      • All non-null statements shall potentially have a side-effect [JSF-187-2]
      • Labels will not be used, except in switch statements [JSF-188-3]
      • The goto statement shall not be used [JSF-189-2]
      • The continue statement shall not be used [JSF-190-2]
      • The break statement shall not be used (except to terminate the cases of a switch statement) [JSF-191-2]
      • For any iteration statement there shall be no more than one break or goto statement used for loop termination [JSF-191_a-2]
      • All 'if...else if' constructs will contain either a final else clause or a comment indicating why a final else clause is not necessary [JSF-192-3]
      • Every non-empty case clause in a switch statement shall be terminated with a break statement [JSF-193-2]
      • All switch statements that do not intend to test for every enumeration value shall contain a final default clause [JSF-194-2]
      • A switch expression will not represent a Boolean value [JSF-195-3]
      • Every switch statement will have at least two cases and a potential default [JSF-196-3]
      • Floating point variables shall not be used as loop counters [JSF-197-2]
      • The initialization expression in a for loop will perform no actions other than to initialize the value of a single for loop parameter [JSF-198-3]
      • The increment expression in a for loop will perform no action other than to change a single loop parameter to the next value for the loop [JSF-199-3]
      • Null initialize or increment expressions in for loops will not be used; a while loop will be used instead [JSF-200-3]
      • Numeric variables being used within a for loop for iteration counting shall not be modified in the body of the loop [JSF-201-2]
      • Floating point variables shall not be tested for exact equality or inequality [JSF-202-2]
      • Evaluation of expressions shall not lead to overflow/underflow [JSF-203-2]
      • Evaluation of expressions shall not lead to overflow/underflow [JSF-203_b-2]
      • The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [JSF-204.1_a-2]
      • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function arguments [JSF-204.1_b-2]
      • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function designator and function arguments [JSF-204.1_c-2]
      • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of expression that involves a function call [JSF-204.1_d-2]
      • Between sequence points an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression [JSF-204.1_e-2]
      • Do not use more than one volatile in one expression [JSF-204.1_f-2]
      • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function calls [JSF-204.1_g-2]
      • A single operation with side-effect shall only be used in the proper context [JSF-204_a-2]
      • A call of function with side-effect shall only be used in the proper context [JSF-204_b-2]
      • The second or third operand of a ternary operator '?:' shall not contain side effects [JSF-204_d-2]
      • The volatile keyword shall not be used [JSF-205-2]
      • Dynamic heap memory allocation shall not be used [JSF-206-2]
      • Unencapsulated global data will be avoided [JSF-207-3]
      • C++ exceptions shall not be used [JSF-208-2]
      • Typedefs that indicate size and signedness shall be used in place of the basic types [JSF-209-2]
      • Typedefs that indicate size and signedness shall be used in place of the basic types [JSF-209_b-2]
      • Algorithms shall not make assumptions concerning the order of allocation of nonstatic data members separated by an access specifier [JSF-210.1-2]
      • Algorithms shall not assume particular memory alignment [JSF-211-2]
      • Use parenthesis to clarify expression order if operators with precedence lower than arithmetic are used [JSF-213_e-2]
      • Assuming that non-local static objects, in separate translation units, are initialized in a special order shall not be done [JSF-214-2]
      • Pointer arithmetic will not be used [JSF-215-4]
    • Metrics [METRICS]

      • Number of protected data member(s) per class [METRICS-11-3]

      • Number of public data member(s) per class [METRICS-13-3]
      • Number of public methods per class [METRICS-14-3]
      • Avoid functions with more than 5 parameters [METRICS-15-3]
      • Macros should not use more than 5 parameters [METRICS-16-3]
      • Avoid structs, unions, or classes with more than 20 fields [METRICS-17-5]
      • Follow the Cyclomatic Complexity limit of 10 [METRICS-18-3]
      • The percentage of comment lines versus the total number of module lines should be between 20 and 60 [METRICS-19-3]
      • Avoid too long functions (declarations and statements) [METRICS-20-3]
      • Avoid too long functions (blocks) [METRICS-21-3]
      • Avoid functions with over 75 lines of code [METRICS-22-3]
      • Nested block depth should not be higher than 5 [METRICS-23-3]
      • Avoid source files that are longer than 500 lines [METRICS-24-5]
      • Any one function (or method) will contain no more than 200 logical source lines of code (L-SLOCs) [METRICS-25-3]
      • Source lines will be kept to a length of 120 characters or less [METRICS-26-3]
      • Functions with more than 7 parameters will not be used [METRICS-27-3]
      • Follow the Cyclomatic Complexity limit of 20 [METRICS-28-3]
      • Report Cyclomatic Complexity [METRICS-29-5]
      • No function should be longer than 60 lines of code [METRICS-30-3]
      • The assertion density of the code should average to a minimum of two assertions per function [METRICS-31-3]
      • All functions with more than 20 lines should contain at least 2 assertions [METRICS-32-3]

      • Follow the Essential Complexity limit of 4 [METRICS-34-5]
      • Follow the Essential Complexity limit of 10 [METRICS-35-5]
      • A global function should not be called from more than 5 different functions [METRICS-36-3]
      • A function should not call more than 7 different functions [METRICS-37-3]
      • The number of statements within function should be in range 1 - 50 [METRICS-38-3]
      • The value of VOCF metric for a function should not be higher than 4 [METRICS-39-3]
      • Statements within function should not be nested deeper than 4 levels [METRICS-40-3]
      • The number of blocks of comments before and inside function to the number of statements in function should be > 0.2 [METRICS-41-3]
      • Follow the Essential Complexity limit of 1 [METRICS-42-5]
      • Report the value of Halstead's delivered bugs (B) for a function [METRICS-43-3]
      • The number of execution paths in a function should not be higher than 80 [METRICS-44-3]

      • An object shall not be assigned to an overlapping object [MISRA2004-18_2-3]
      • An object shall not be assigned to an overlapping object [MISRA2004-18_2_b-3]
      • Unions shall not be used [MISRA2004-18_4-3]
      • #include statements in a file should only be preceded by other preprocessor directives or comments [MISRA2004-19_1-3]
      • In the definition of a function-like macro each instance of a parameter shall be enclosed in parentheses unless it is used as the operand of # or ## [MISRA2004-19_10-3]
      • Do not use in preprocessor directives #if and #elif macros not defined in translation unit [MISRA2004-19_11_b-3]
      • There shall be at most one occurrence of the # or ## preprocessor operators in a single macro definition [MISRA2004-19_12-3]
      • The # and ## preprocessor operators should not be used [MISRA2004-19_13-3]
      • The defined preprocessor operator shall only be used in one of the two standard forms [MISRA2004-19_14-3]
      • Precautions shall be taken in order to prevent the contents of a header file being included twice [MISRA2004-19_15-3]
      • Preprocessing directives shall be syntactically meaningful even when excluded by the preprocessor [MISRA2004-19_16-3]
      • All #else, #elif and #endif preprocessor directives shall reside in the same file as the #if or #ifdef directive to which they are related [MISRA2004-19_17-3]
      • Non-standard characters should not occur in header file names in #include directives [MISRA2004-19_2-3]
      • The #include directive shall be followed by either a <filename> or "filename" sequence [MISRA2004-19_3-3]
      • Avoid keywords and basic types in macros [MISRA2004-19_4-3]
      • Macros shall not be #define'd or #undef'd within a block [MISRA2004-19_5-3]
      • #undef shall not be used [MISRA2004-19_6-3]
      • A function should be used in preference to a function-like macro [MISRA2004-19_7-3]
      • A function-like macro shall not be invoked without all of its arguments [MISRA2004-19_8-3]
      • Arguments to a function-like macro shall not contain tokens that look like preprocessing directives [MISRA2004-19_9-3]
      • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library stdlib.h shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_10-3]
      • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_11-3]
      • The 'exit()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_11_b-3]
      • The 'getenv()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_11_c-3]
      • The 'system()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_11_d-3]
      • The standard header files <time.h> or <ctime> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_12-3]
      • The time handling functions and macros of the library <time.h> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_12_b-3]
      • The types defined in the library <time.h> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_12_c-3]
      • Do not #define or #undef identifiers with names which start with underscore [MISRA2004-20_1_a-3]
      • Do not redefine reserved words [MISRA2004-20_1_b-3]
      • Reserved identifiers, macros and functions in the standard library, shall not be defined, redefined or undefined (C90 code) [MISRA2004-20_1_c-3]
      • Do not #define nor #undef identifier 'defined' [MISRA2004-20_1_e-3]
      • The names of standard library macros, objects and functions shall not be reused [MISRA2004-20_2-3]
      • The names of standard library macros, objects and functions shall not be reused (C90) [MISRA2004-20_2_a-3]
      • The names of standard library macros, objects and functions shall not be reused (C99) [MISRA2004-20_2_b-3]
      • The validity of values passed to library functions shall be checked [MISRA2004-20_3-3]
      • Dynamic heap memory allocation shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_4-3]
      • The error indicator 'errno' shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_5-3]
      • The macro offsetof, in library stddef.h, shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_6-3]
      • The facilities provided by <setjmp.h> should not be used [MISRA2004-20_7-3]
      • The standard header files <setjmp.h> or <csetjmp> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_7_b-3]
      • The standard header files <signal.h> or <csignal> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_8-3]
      • The signal handling facilities of <signal.h> shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_8_b-3]
      • The input/output library stdio.h shall not be used [MISRA2004-20_9-3]
      • Assembly language shall be encapsulated and isolated [MISRA2004-2_1-3]
      • Source code shall only use /* ... */ style comments [MISRA2004-2_2-3]
      • The character sequence /* shall not be used within a C-style comment [MISRA2004-2_3-3]
      • Sections of code should not be "commented out" [MISRA2004-2_4-4]
      • All uses of the #pragma directive shall be documented and explained [MISRA2004-3_4-3]
      • Do not mix bit-fields and other data within the same structure [MISRA2004-3_5-3]
      • Only those escape sequences that are defined in the ISO C standard shall be used [MISRA2004-4_1-3]
      • Trigraphs shall not be used [MISRA2004-4_2-3]
      • User-specified C external identifiers should differ in the first 31 characters [MISRA2004-5_1_a-3]
      • User-specified C internal identifiers should differ from external identifiers in the first 31 characters [MISRA2004-5_1_b-3]
      • User-specified C internal identifiers declared in the same scope should differ in the first 31 characters [MISRA2004-5_1_c-3]
      • Identifier declared in a local or function prototype scope shall not hide an identifier declared in a global or namespace scope [MISRA2004-5_2_a-3]
      • Identifiers declared in an inner local scope should not hide identifiers declared in an outer local scope [MISRA2004-5_2_b-3]
      • Do not reuse typedef names [MISRA2004-5_3_a-3]
      • Do not reuse typedef names as a typedef name [MISRA2004-5_3_b-3]
      • A tag name shall not be reused for other purpose within the program [MISRA2004-5_4_a-3]
      • A tag name shall not be reused to define a different tag [MISRA2004-5_4_b-3]
      • The name of typedef should not be the same as the name of type that is typedef'd [MISRA2004-5_4_c-3]
      • No object or function identifier with static storage duration should be reused [MISRA2004-5_5_a-4]
      • No object or function identifier with static storage duration should be reused [MISRA2004-5_5_b-4]
      • No identifier in one name space should have the same spelling as an identifier in another name space, with the exception of structure and union member names [MISRA2004-5_6-4]
      • No identifier name should be reused [MISRA2004-5_7-4]
      • The plain char type shall be used only for the storage and use of character values [MISRA2004-6_1-3]
      • signed and unsigned char type shall be used only for the storage and use of numeric values [MISRA2004-6_2-3]
      • typedefs to basic types should contain some digits in their name [MISRA2004-6_3-3]
      • typedefs should be used in place of the basic types [MISRA2004-6_3_b-3]
      • Bit fields shall only be defined to be of type unsigned int or signed int [MISRA2004-6_4-3]
      • Named bit-fields with signed integer type shall have a length of more than one bit [MISRA2004-6_5-3]
      • Unnamed bit-fields with signed integer type shall have a length of more than one bit [MISRA2004-6_5_a-3]
      • Octal constants (other than zero) shall not be used [MISRA2004-7_1_a-3]
      • Octal escape sequences shall not be used [MISRA2004-7_1_b-3]
      • Objects or functions with external linkage shall be declared in a header file [MISRA2004-8_10-4]
      • The static storage class specifier shall be used in definitions and declarations of objects and functions that have internal linkage [MISRA2004-8_11-3]
      • When an array is declared with external linkage, its size shall be stated explicitly or defined implicitly by initialisation [MISRA2004-8_12-3]
      • Functions shall have prototype declarations and the prototype shall be visible at both the function definition and call [MISRA2004-8_1_a-3]
      • Functions shall always have visible prototype at the function call [MISRA2004-8_1_b-3]
      • Whenever a function is declared or defined, its type shall be explicitly stated [MISRA2004-8_2_a-3]
      • Whenever an object is declared or defined, its type shall be explicitly stated [MISRA2004-8_2_b-3]
      • Use identical types in declaration and definition [MISRA2004-8_3_a-3]
      • Use identical types in declaration and definition [MISRA2004-8_3_b-3]
      • If objects or functions are declared more than once their types shall be compatible [MISRA2004-8_4-3]
      • There shall be no definitions of objects or functions in a header file [MISRA2004-8_5-3]
      • Always declare functions at file scope [MISRA2004-8_6-3]
      • Objects shall be defined at block scope if they are only accessed from within a single function [MISRA2004-8_7-3]
      • All automatic variables shall have been assigned a value before being used [MISRA2004-9_1-3]
      • The initializer for an aggregate or union shall be enclosed in braces [MISRA2004-9_2-3]
      • Arrays shall not be partially initialized [MISRA2004-9_2_b-3]
      • The non-zero initialization of structures requires an explicit initializer for each element [MISRA2004-9_2_c-3]
      • In an enumerator list, the "=" construct shall not be used to explicitly initialise members other than the first, unless all items are explicitly initialised [MISRA2004-9_3-3]
