        • The small integer variants of the minimum-width integer constant macros should not be used [MISRAC2012-RULE_7_6-a-2]
      • Rule 8.1 (Required) Types shall be explicitly specified [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_1]
        • Whenever a function is declared or defined, its type shall be explicitly stated [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_1-a-2]
        • Whenever an object is declared or defined, its type shall be explicitly stated [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_1-b-2]
      • Rule 8.10 (Required) An inline function shall be declared with the static storage class [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_10]
        • An inline function shall be declared with the static storage class [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_10-a-2]
      • Rule 8.11 (Advisory) When an array with external linkage is declared, its size should be explicitly specified [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_11]
        • When an array is declared with external linkage, its size shall be stated explicitly or defined implicitly by initialisation [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_11-a-4]
      • Rule 8.12 (Required) Within an enumerator list, the value of an implicitly-specified enumeration constant shall be unique [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_12]
        • Within an enumerator list, the value of an implicitly-specified enumeration constant shall be unique [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_12-a-2]
      • Rule 8.13 (Advisory) A pointer should point to a const-qualified type whenever possible [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_13]
        • A pointer parameter in a function prototype should be declared as pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_13-a-4]
        • Declare a type of parameter as typedef to pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_13-b-4]
      • Rule 8.14 (Required) The restrict type qualifier shall not be used [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_14]
        • The restrict type qualifier shall not be used [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_14-a-2]
      • Rule 8.15 (Required) All declarations of an object with an explicit alignment specification shall specify the same alignment [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_15]
        • Explicit alignment specifiers in all declarations of an object with external linkage shall be the same [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_15-a-2]
        • Explicit alignment specifiers in all declarations of an object with internal linkage shall be the same [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_15-b-2]
      • Rule 8.16 (Advisory) The alignment specification of zero should not appear in an object declaration [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_16]
        • The zero-alignment specifier should not be used in an object declaration [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_16-a-4]
      • Rule 8.17 (Advisory) At most one explicit alignment specifier should appear in an object declaration [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_17]
        • A declaration of an object should contain at most one explicit alignment specifier [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_17-a-4]
      • Rule 8.2 (Required) Function types shall be in prototype form with named parameters [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_2]
        • Identifiers shall be given for all of the parameters in a function prototype declaration [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_2-a-2]
        • Function types shall have named parameters [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_2-b-2]
        • Function types shall be in prototype form [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_2-c-2]
      • Rule 8.3 (Required) All declarations of an object or function shall use the same names and type qualifiers [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_3]
        • If objects or functions are declared more than once their types shall be compatible [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_3-a-2]
        • The identifiers used in the declaration and definition of a function shall be identical [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_3-b-2]
        • All declarations of an object or function shall have compatible types [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_3-c-2]
      • Rule 8.4 (Required) A compatible declaration shall be visible when an object or function with external linkage is defined [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_4]
        • A declaration shall be visible when an object or function with external linkage is defined [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_4-a-2]
        • If objects or functions are declared more than once their types shall be compatible [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_4-b-2]
      • Rule 8.5 (Required) An external object or function shall be declared once in one and only one file [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_5]
        • An external object or function shall not have more than one non-defining declaration in translation unit [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_5-a-2]
      • Rule 8.6 (Required) An identifier with external linkage shall have exactly one external definition [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_6]
        • An identifier with external linkage shall have no more then one external definition [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_6-a-2]
        • An identifier with external linkage shall have external definition [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_6-b-2]
      • Rule 8.7 (Advisory) Functions and objects should not be defined with external linkage if they are referenced in only one translation unit [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_7]
        • Functions and objects should not be defined with external linkage if they are referenced in only one translation unit [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_7-a-4]
      • Rule 8.8 (Required) The static storage class specifier shall be used in all declarations of objects and functions that have internal linkage [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_8]
        • The static storage class specifier shall be used in definitions and declarations of objects and functions that have internal linkage [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_8-a-2]
      • Rule 8.9 (Advisory) An object should be declared at block scope if its identifier only appears in a single function [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_9]
        • Objects shall be defined at block scope if they are only accessed from within a single function [MISRAC2012-RULE_8_9-a-4]
      • Rule 9.1 (Mandatory) The value of an object with automatic storage duration shall not be read before it has been set [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_1]
        • Avoid use before initialization [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_1-a-1]
      • Rule 9.2 (Required) The initializer for an aggregate or union shall be enclosed in braces [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_2]
        • The initializer for an aggregate or union shall be enclosed in braces [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_2-a-2]
      • Rule 9.3 (Required) Arrays shall not be partially initialized [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_3]
        • Arrays shall not be partially initialized [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_3-a-2]
      • Rule 9.4 (Required) An element of an object shall not be initialized more than once [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_4]
        • An element of an object shall not be initialized more than once [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_4-a-2]
      • Rule 9.5 (Required) Where designated initializers are used to initialize an array object the size of the array shall be specified explicitly [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_5]
        • Where designated initializers are used to initialize an array object the size of the array shall be specified explicitly [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_5-a-2]
      • Rule 9.6 (Required) An initializer using chained designators shall not contain initializers without designators [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_6]
        • An initializer using chained designators shall not contain initializers without designators [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_6-a-2]
      • Rule 9.7 (Mandatory) Atomic objects shall be appropriately initialized before being accessed [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_7]
        • Atomic objects shall be properly initialized before being accessed [MISRAC2012-RULE_9_7-a-1]
    • MISRA C++ 2023 [MISRACPP2023]
      • Rule 0.0.1 (Required) A function shall not contain unreachable statements [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1]
        • There shall be no unreachable code in "else" block [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-a-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code after 'return', 'break', 'continue', 'goto', 'throw' statements, and after calls to functions with the 'noreturn' attribute [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-b-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code in "if/else/while/for" block [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-c-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code in switch statement [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-d-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code in 'for' loop [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-e-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code after 'if' or 'switch' statement [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-f-2]
        • There shall be no unreachable code after "if" or "switch" statement inside while/for/do...while loop [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-g-2]
        • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single try-catch statement or function-try-block for a derived class and some or all of its bases, the handlers shall be ordered most-derived to base class [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-h-2]
        • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single 'try-catch' statement or 'function-try-block', any ellipsis (catch-all) handler shall occur last [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-i-2]
        • A 'try' statement of a 'try-block' should contain a potentially-throwing statement [MISRACPP2023-0_0_1-j-2]
      • Rule 0.0.2 (Advisory) Controlling expressions should not be invariant [MISRACPP2023-0_0_2]
        • Avoid conditions that always evaluate to the same value [MISRACPP2023-0_0_2-a-4]
      • Rule 0.1.1 (Advisory) A value should not be unnecessarily written to a local object [MISRACPP2023-0_1_1]
        • Avoid unused values [MISRACPP2023-0_1_1-a-4]
      • Rule 0.1.2 (Required) The value returned by a function shall be used [MISRACPP2023-0_1_2]
        • The value returned by a function having a non-void return type that is not an overloaded operator shall always be used [MISRACPP2023-0_1_2-a-2]
      • Rule 0.2.1 (Advisory) Variables with limited visibility should be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_1]
        • Avoid unused local variables [MISRACPP2023-0_2_1-a-4]
        • A project should not contain unused variables with internal linkage [MISRACPP2023-0_2_1-b-4]
      • Rule 0.2.2 (Required) A named function parameter shall be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_2]
        • Eliminate unused parameters [MISRACPP2023-0_2_2-a-2]
        • There shall be no unused named parameters in virtual functions [MISRACPP2023-0_2_2-b-2]
      • Rule 0.2.3 (Advisory) Types with limited visibility should be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_3]
        • Types declared in an unnamed namespace scope should be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_3-a-4]
        • Types declared in a block scope should be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_3-b-4]
      • Rule 0.2.4 (Advisory) Functions with limited visibility should be used at least once [MISRACPP2023-0_2_4]
        • Avoid unreachable methods [MISRACPP2023-0_2_4-a-4]
      • Dir 0.3.1 (Advisory) Floating-point arithmetic should be used appropriately [MISRACPP2023-0_3_1]
        • Do not use object representations to compare floating-point values [MISRACPP2023-0_3_1-a-4]
        • Floating-point expressions shall not be explicitly (syntactically) tested for equality (==) or inequality (!=) [MISRACPP2023-0_3_1-b-4]
        • Do not use floating point variables as loop counters [MISRACPP2023-0_3_1-c-4]
        • Do not use floating-point expressions which may result in NaN and infinity values [MISRACPP2023-0_3_1-d-4]
      • Dir 0.3.2 (Required) A function call shall not violate the function's preconditions [MISRACPP2023-0_3_2]
        • Do not pass incorrect values to library functions [MISRACPP2023-0_3_2-a-2]
      • Rule 10.0.1 (Advisory) A declaration should not declare more than one variable or member variable [MISRACPP2023-10_0_1]
        • Each variable should be declared in a separate declaration statement [MISRACPP2023-10_0_1-a-4]
      • Rule 10.1.1 (Advisory) The target type of a pointer or lvalue reference parameter should be const-qualified appropriately [MISRACPP2023-10_1_1]
        • A pointer parameter in a function prototype should be declared as pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [MISRACPP2023-10_1_1-a-4]
        • Declare a type of parameter as typedef to pointer to const if the pointer is not used to modify the addressed object [MISRACPP2023-10_1_1-b-4]
        • Declare reference parameters as const references whenever possible [MISRACPP2023-10_1_1-c-4]
      • Rule 10.1.2 (Required) The volatile qualifier shall be used appropriately [MISRACPP2023-10_1_2]
        • The volatile qualifier shall be used appropriately [MISRACPP2023-10_1_2-a-2]
      • Rule 10.2.1 (Required) An enumeration shall be defined with an explicit underlying type [MISRACPP2023-10_2_1]
        • An enumeration shall be defined with an explicit underlying type [MISRACPP2023-10_2_1-a-2]
        • An explicit or implicit enumerator value shall not be the result of a narrowing conversion [MISRACPP2023-10_2_1-b-2]
      • Rule 10.2.2 (Advisory) Unscoped enumerations should not be declared [MISRACPP2023-10_2_2]
        • Prefer Scoped Enums to Unscoped Enums [MISRACPP2023-10_2_2-a-4]
      • Rule 10.2.3 (Required) The numeric value of an unscoped enumeration with no fixed underlying type shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-10_2_3]
        • The numeric value of an unscoped enumeration with no fixed underlying type shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-10_2_3-a-2]
      • Rule 10.3.1 (Advisory) There should be no unnamed namespaces in header files [MISRACPP2023-10_3_1]
        • There shall be no unnamed namespaces in header files [MISRACPP2023-10_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 10.4.1 (Required) The asm declaration shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-10_4_1]
        • The 'asm' declaration should not be used [MISRACPP2023-10_4_1-a-2]
      • Rule 11.3.1 (Advisory) Variables of array type should not be declared [MISRACPP2023-11_3_1]
        • C-style arrays shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-11_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 11.3.2 (Advisory) The declaration of an object should contain no more than two levels of pointer indirection [MISRACPP2023-11_3_2]
        • The declaration of objects should contain no more than 2 levels of pointer indirection [MISRACPP2023-11_3_2-a-4]
      • Rule 11.6.1 (Advisory) All variables should be initialized [MISRACPP2023-11_6_1]
        • All non-class variables with automatic storage duration should be explicitly initialized [MISRACPP2023-11_6_1-a-4]
      • Rule 11.6.2 (Mandatory) The value of an object must not be read before it has been set [MISRACPP2023-11_6_2]
        • Avoid use before initialization [MISRACPP2023-11_6_2-a-1]
      • Rule 11.6.3 (Required) Within an enumerator list, the value of an implicitly-specified enumeration constant shall be unique [MISRACPP2023-11_6_3]
        • Within an enumerator list, the value of an implicitly-specified enumeration constant shall be unique [MISRACPP2023-11_6_3-a-2]
      • Rule 12.2.1 (Advisory) Bit-fields should not be declared [MISRACPP2023-12_2_1]
        • Do not declare member variables as bit-fields [MISRACPP2023-12_2_1-a-4]
      • Rule 12.2.2 (Required) A bit-field shall have an appropriate type [MISRACPP2023-12_2_2]
        • A bit-field shall have an appropriate type [MISRACPP2023-12_2_2-a-2]
        • All enumeration values should be representable within the width of the bit-field [MISRACPP2023-12_2_2-b-2]
      • Rule 12.2.3 (Required) A named bit-field with signed integer type shall not have a length of one bit [MISRACPP2023-12_2_3]
        • Named bit-fields with signed integer type shall have a length of more than one bit [MISRACPP2023-12_2_3-a-2]
      • Rule 12.3.1 (Required) The union keyword shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-12_3_1]
        • The union keyword should not be used [MISRACPP2023-12_3_1-a-2]
      • Rule 13.1.1 (Advisory) Classes should not be inherited virtually [MISRACPP2023-13_1_1]
        • Classes should not be derived from virtual bases [MISRACPP2023-13_1_1-a-4]
      • Rule 13.1.2 (Required) An accessible base class shall not be both virtual and non-virtual in the same hierarchy [MISRACPP2023-13_1_2]
        • A base class shall not be both virtual and non-virtual in the same hierarchy [MISRACPP2023-13_1_2-a-2]
      • Rule 13.3.1 (Required) User-declared member functions shall use the virtual, override and final specifiers appropriately [MISRACPP2023-13_3_1]
        • Each overriding virtual function shall be declared with the override or final specifier [MISRACPP2023-13_3_1-a-2]
        • Only one of virtual, override or final should be specified in a member function declaration [MISRACPP2023-13_3_1-b-2]
      • Rule 13.3.2 (Required) Parameters in an overriding virtual function shall not specify different default arguments [MISRACPP2023-13_3_2]
        • Parameters in an overriding virtual function shall not specify different default arguments [MISRACPP2023-13_3_2-a-2]
      • Rule 13.3.3 (Required) The parameters in all declarations or overrides of a function shall either be unnamed or have identical names [MISRACPP2023-13_3_3]
        • The identifiers used in the declaration and definition of a function shall be identical [MISRACPP2023-13_3_3-a-2]
        • The parameters in all overrides of a function should either be unnamed or have identical names [MISRACPP2023-13_3_3-b-2]
      • Rule 13.3.4 (Required) A comparison of a potentially virtual pointer to member function shall only be with nullptr [MISRACPP2023-13_3_4]
        • A pointer to member virtual function shall only be tested for equality with null-pointer-constant [MISRACPP2023-13_3_4-a-2]
      • Rule 14.1.1 (Advisory) Non-static data members should be either all private or all public [MISRACPP2023-14_1_1]
        • Non-static data members should be either all private or all public [MISRACPP2023-14_1_1-a-4]
      • Rule 15.0.1 (Required) Special member functions shall be provided appropriately [MISRACPP2023-15_0_1]
        • Special member functions shall be provided appropriately [MISRACPP2023-15_0_1-a-2]
        • Destructor shall have a non-empty body [MISRACPP2023-15_0_1-b-2]
      • Rule 15.0.2 (Advisory) User-provided copy and move member functions of a class should have appropriate signatures [MISRACPP2023-15_0_2]
        • User-provided copy and move member functions of a class should have appropriate signatures [MISRACPP2023-15_0_2-a-4]
      • Rule 15.1.1 (Required) An object's dynamic type shall not be used from within its constructor or destructor [MISRACPP2023-15_1_1]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under construction [MISRACPP2023-15_1_1-a-2]
        • Do not use dynamic type of an object under destruction [MISRACPP2023-15_1_1-b-2]
      • Rule 15.1.2 (Advisory) All constructors of a class should explicitly initialize all of its virtual base classes and immediate base classes [MISRACPP2023-15_1_2]
        • All constructors of a class should explicitly call a constructor for all of its immediate base classes and all virtual base classes [MISRACPP2023-15_1_2-a-4]
      • Rule 15.1.3 (Required) Conversion operators and constructors that are callable with a single argument shall be explicit [MISRACPP2023-15_1_3]
        • Constructors allowing for conversion should be made explicit [MISRACPP2023-15_1_3-a-2]
        • User-conversion cast operators should be made explicit [MISRACPP2023-15_1_3-b-2]
      • Rule 15.1.4 (Advisory) All direct, non-static data members of a class should be initialized before the class object is accessible [MISRACPP2023-15_1_4]
        • All direct, non-static data members of a non-aggregate class should be initialized at the top of a constructor body [MISRACPP2023-15_1_4-a-4]
        • All direct, non-static data members of an aggregate class should be initialized as soon as the object is created [MISRACPP2023-15_1_4-b-4]
      • Rule 15.1.5 (Required) A class shall only define an initializer-list constructor when it is the only constructor [MISRACPP2023-15_1_5]
        • A class shall only define an initializer-list constructor when it is the only constructor [MISRACPP2023-15_1_5-a-2]
      • Dir 15.8.1 (Required) User-provided copy assignment operators and move assignment operators shall handle self-assignment [MISRACPP2023-15_8_1]
        • Check for assignment to self in operator= [MISRACPP2023-15_8_1-a-2]
      • Rule 16.5.1 (Required) The logical AND and logical OR operators shall not be overloaded [MISRACPP2023-16_5_1]
        • Avoid overloading logical operators AND, OR (&&, ||) [MISRACPP2023-16_5_1-a-2]
      • Rule 16.5.2 (Required) The address-of operator shall not be overloaded [MISRACPP2023-16_5_2]
        • The unary & operator shall not be overloaded [MISRACPP2023-16_5_2-a-2]
      • Rule 16.6.1 (Advisory) Symmetrical operators should only be implemented as non-member functions [MISRACPP2023-16_6_1]
        • If you'd like to support mixed-mode operations make operators a non-member functions [MISRACPP2023-16_6_1-a-4]
      • Rule 17.8.1 (Required) Function templates shall not be explicitly specialized [MISRACPP2023-17_8_1]
        • Function templates shall not be explicitly specialized [MISRACPP2023-17_8_1-a-2]
      • Rule 18.1.1 (Required) An exception object shall not have pointer type [MISRACPP2023-18_1_1]
        • An exception object should not have pointer type [MISRACPP2023-18_1_1-a-2]
      • Rule 18.1.2 (Required) An empty throw shall only occur within the compound-statement of a catch handler [MISRACPP2023-18_1_2]
        • An empty throw (throw;) shall only be used in the compound-statement of a catch handler [MISRACPP2023-18_1_2-a-2]
      • Rule 18.2.2 (Required) The string handling functions from , , and shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_2_2]
        • The string handling functions from <cstring>, <cstdlib>, <cwchar> and <cinttypes> shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_2_2-a-2]
      • Rule 18.3.1 (Advisory) There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [MISRACPP2023-18_3_1]
        • There should be at least one exception handler to catch all otherwise unhandled exceptions [MISRACPP2023-18_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 18.3.2 (Required) An exception of class type shall be caught by const reference or reference [MISRACPP2023-18_3_2]
        • A class type exception shall always be caught by reference [MISRACPP2023-18_3_2-a-2]
      • Rule 18.3.3 (Required) Handlers for a function-try-block of a constructor or destructor shall not refer to non-static members from their class or its bases [MISRACPP2023-18_3_3]
        • Handlers of a function-try-block implementation of a class constructor or destructor shall not reference nonstatic members from this class or its bases [MISRACPP2023-18_3_3-a-2]
      • Rule 18.4.1 (Required) Exception-unfriendly functions shall be noexcept [MISRACPP2023-18_4_1]
        • Exception-unfriendly functions shall be noexcept [MISRACPP2023-18_4_1-a-2]
        • Functions used as initializers of non-constexpr non-local variables shall be noexcept [MISRACPP2023-18_4_1-b-2]
      • Rule 18.5.1 (Advisory) A noexcept function should not attempt to propagate an exception to the calling function [MISRACPP2023-18_5_1]
        • Avoid throwing exceptions from functions that are declared not to throw [MISRACPP2023-18_5_1-a-4]
      • Rule 18.5.2 (Advisory) Program-terminating functions should not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_5_2]
        • The 'abort()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_5_2-a-4]
        • The 'exit()' function from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_5_2-b-4]
        • The 'quick_exit()' and '_Exit()' functions from the 'stdlib.h' or 'cstdlib' library shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-18_5_2-c-4]
      • Rule 19.0.1 (Required) A line whose first token is # shall be a valid preprocessing directive [MISRACPP2023-19_0_1]
        • Preprocessing directives shall be syntactically meaningful even when excluded by the preprocessor [MISRACPP2023-19_0_1-a-2]
      • Rule 19.0.2 (Required) Function-like macros shall not be defined [MISRACPP2023-19_0_2]
        • Function-like macros shall not be defined [MISRACPP2023-19_0_2-a-2]
      • Rule 19.0.3 (Advisory) #include directives should only be preceded by preprocessor directives or comments [MISRACPP2023-19_0_3]
        • #include statements in a file should only be preceded by other preprocessor directives or comments [MISRACPP2023-19_0_3-a-4]
      • Rule 19.0.4 (Advisory) #undef should only be used for macros defined previously in the same file [MISRACPP2023-19_0_4]
        • #undef should only be used for macros defined previously in the same file [MISRACPP2023-19_0_4-a-4]
      • Rule 19.1.1 (Required) The defined preprocessor operator shall be used appropriately [MISRACPP2023-19_1_1]
        • The defined preprocessor operator shall only be used in one of the two standard forms [MISRACPP2023-19_1_1-a-2]
      • Rule 19.1.2 (Required) All #else, #elif and #endif preprocessor directives shall reside in the same file as the #if, #ifdef or #ifndef directive to which they are related [MISRACPP2023-19_1_2]
        • All #else, #elif and #endif preprocessor directives shall reside in the same file as the #if or #ifdef directive to which they are related [MISRACPP2023-19_1_2-a-2]
      • Rule 19.1.3 (Required) All identifiers used in the controlling expression of #if or #elif preprocessing directives shall be defined prior to evaluation [MISRACPP2023-19_1_3]
        • Do not use in preprocessor directives #if and #elif macros not defined in translation unit [MISRACPP2023-19_1_3-a-2]
      • Rule 19.2.1 (Required) Precautions shall be taken in order to prevent the contents of a header file being included more than once [MISRACPP2023-19_2_1]
        • Use multiple include guards [MISRACPP2023-19_2_1-a-2]
      • Rule 19.2.2 (Required) The #include directive shall be followed by either a or "filename" sequence [MISRACPP2023-19_2_2]
        • The #include directive shall be followed by either a <filename> or "filename" sequence [MISRACPP2023-19_2_2-a-2]
      • Rule 19.2.3 (Required) The ' or " or \ characters and the /* or // character sequences shall not occur in a header file name [MISRACPP2023-19_2_3]
        • Non-standard characters should not occur in header file names in #include directives [MISRACPP2023-19_2_3-a-2]
      • Rule 19.3.1 (Advisory) The # and ## preprocessor operators should not be used [MISRACPP2023-19_3_1]
        • The # and ## preprocessor operators should not be used [MISRACPP2023-19_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 19.3.2 (Required) A macro parameter immediately following a # operator shall not be immediately followed by a ## operator [MISRACPP2023-19_3_2]
        • A macro parameter immediately following a # operator shall not immediately be followed by a ## operator [MISRACPP2023-19_3_2-a-2]
      • Rule 19.3.3 (Required) The argument to a mixed-use macro parameter shall not be subject to further expansion [MISRACPP2023-19_3_3]
        • A macro parameter used as an operand to the # or ## operators, which is itself subject to further macro replacement, shall only be used as an operand to these operators [MISRACPP2023-19_3_3-a-2]
      • Rule 19.3.4 (Required) Parentheses shall be used to ensure macro arguments are expanded appropriately [MISRACPP2023-19_3_4]
        • In the definition of a function-like macro each instance of a parameter shall be enclosed in parentheses unless it is used as the operand of # or ## [MISRACPP2023-19_3_4-a-2]
      • Rule 19.3.5 (Required) Tokens that look like a preprocessing directive shall not occur within a macro argument [MISRACPP2023-19_3_5]
        • Arguments to a function-like macro shall not contain tokens that look like preprocessing directives [MISRACPP2023-19_3_5-a-2]
      • Rule 19.6.1 (Advisory) The #pragma directive and the _Pragma operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-19_6_1]
        • The #pragma directive shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-19_6_1-a-4]
        • The '_Pragma' operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-19_6_1-b-4]
      • Rule 21.10.1 (Required) The features of shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_10_1]
        • The identifiers va_list, va_arg, va_start, va_end, va_copy should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_10_1-a-2]

        • The facilities provided by <setjmp.h> should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_10_2-a-2]
        • The standard header files <setjmp.h> or <csetjmp> shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_10_2-b-2]

        • The signal handling facilities of <signal.h> shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_10_3-a-2]

        • The library functions atof, atoi and atol from library stdlib.h shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_2_1-a-2]

        • The macro offsetof, in library stddef.h, shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_2_4-a-2]
      • Rule 21.6.1 (Advisory) Dynamic memory should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_1]
        • Dynamic heap memory allocation shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_1-a-4]
      • Rule 21.6.2 (Required) Dynamic memory shall be managed automatically [MISRACPP2023-21_6_2]
        • Dynamic heap memory allocation shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_2-a-2]
        • Any member function named 'allocate' or 'deallocate' enclosed by namespace 'std' should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_2-b-2]
        • The 'std::unique_ptr::release' function should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_2-c-2]
      • Rule 21.6.3 (Required) Advanced memory management shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_3]
        • Destructor should not be called manually [MISRACPP2023-21_6_3-a-2]
        • Do not declare the 'new' and 'delete' operators [MISRACPP2023-21_6_3-b-2]
        • The memory management functions from the <new> and <memory> headers should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_3-c-2]
        • Advanced memory management operators 'new' and 'delete' should not be used [MISRACPP2023-21_6_3-d-2]
      • Rule 21.6.4 (Required) If a project defines either a sized or unsized version of a global operator delete, then both shall be defined [MISRACPP2023-21_6_4]
        • Define both sized and unsized versions of operator delete [MISRACPP2023-21_6_4-a-2]
      • Rule 21.6.5 (Required) A pointer to an incomplete class type shall not be deleted [MISRACPP2023-21_6_5]
        • Do not delete objects with incomplete class at the point of deletion [MISRACPP2023-21_6_5-a-2]
      • Rule 22.3.1 (Required) The assert macro shall not be used with a constant-expression [MISRACPP2023-22_3_1]
        • The 'assert' macro shall not be used with a constant expression [MISRACPP2023-22_3_1-a-2]
      • Rule 22.4.1 (Required) The literal value zero shall be the only value assigned to errno [MISRACPP2023-22_4_1]
        • The literal value zero shall be the only value assigned to errno [MISRACPP2023-22_4_1-a-2]
      • Rule 23.11.1 (Advisory) The raw pointer constructors of std::shared_ptr and std::unique_ptr should not be used [MISRACPP2023-23_11_1]
