      • Rule 24.5.1 (Required) The character handling functions from and shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-24_5_1]
        • The character handling functions from <cctype> and <cwctype> shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-24_5_1-a-2]
      • Rule 24.5.2 (Required) The C++ Standard Library functions memcpy, memmove and memcmp from shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-24_5_2]
        • The C++ Standard Library functions 'memcpy', 'memmove' and 'memcmp' from <cstring> should not be used [MISRACPP2023-24_5_2-a-2]
      • Rule 25.5.1 (Required) The setlocale and std::locale::global functions shall not be called [MISRACPP2023-25_5_1]
        • The 'setlocale' function should not be used [MISRACPP2023-25_5_1-a-2]
        • The 'std::locale::global' function should not be used [MISRACPP2023-25_5_1-b-2]
      • Rule 25.5.2 (Mandatory) The pointers returned by the C++ Standard Library functions localeconv, getenv, setlocale or strerror must only be used as if they have pointer to const-qualified type [MISRACPP2023-25_5_2]
        • The pointers returned by the Standard Library functions 'localeconv', 'getenv', 'setlocale' or, 'strerror' shall only be used as if they have pointer to const-qualified type [MISRACPP2023-25_5_2-a-1]
        • Strings pointed by members of the structure 'lconv' should not be modified [MISRACPP2023-25_5_2-b-1]
        • The address of the 'localeconv', 'getenv', 'setlocale' or, 'strerror' function should not be taken [MISRACPP2023-25_5_2-c-1]
      • Rule 25.5.3 (Mandatory) The pointer returned by the C++ Standard Library functions asctime, ctime, gmtime, localtime, localeconv, getenv, setlocale or strerror must not be used following a subsequent call to the same function [MISRACPP2023-25_5_3]
        • Pointers returned by certain Standard Library functions should not be used following a subsequent call to the same or related function [MISRACPP2023-25_5_3-a-1]
      • Rule 26.3.1 (Advisory) std::vector should not be specialized with bool [MISRACPP2023-26_3_1]
        • Avoid using vector<bool> [MISRACPP2023-26_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 28.3.1 (Required) Predicates shall not have persistent side effects [MISRACPP2023-28_3_1]
        • Predicates shall not have persistent side effects [MISRACPP2023-28_3_1-a-2]
      • Rule 28.6.1 (Required) The argument to std::move shall be a non-const lvalue [MISRACPP2023-28_6_1]
        • Do not use std::move on objects declared with the const or const & type [MISRACPP2023-28_6_1-a-2]
      • Rule 28.6.2 (Required) Forwarding references and std::forward shall be used together [MISRACPP2023-28_6_2]
        • The 'std::forward' function should be used to forward forwarding references [MISRACPP2023-28_6_2-a-2]
        • The 'std::forward' function should only be used to forward forwarding references [MISRACPP2023-28_6_2-b-2]
      • Rule 28.6.3 (Required) An object shall not be used while in a potentially moved-from state [MISRACPP2023-28_6_3]
        • Do not subsequently use the argument to std::forward [MISRACPP2023-28_6_3-a-2]
        • Do not rely on the value of a moved-from object [MISRACPP2023-28_6_3-b-2]
      • Rule 28.6.4 (Required) The result of std::remove, std::remove_if, std::unique and empty shall be used [MISRACPP2023-28_6_4]
        • The result of std::remove, std::remove_if, std::unique and empty shall be used [MISRACPP2023-28_6_4-a-2]
      • Rule 30.0.1 (Required) The C Library input/output functions shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-30_0_1]
        • The input/output library stdio.h shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-30_0_1-a-2]
        • Prefer iostream.h to stdio.h [MISRACPP2023-30_0_1-b-2]
      • Rule 30.0.2 (Required) Reads and writes on the same file stream shall be separated by a positioning operation [MISRACPP2023-30_0_2]
        • Do not alternately input and output from a stream without an intervening flush or positioning call [MISRACPP2023-30_0_2-a-2]
      • Rule 4.1.2 (Advisory) Deprecated features should not be used [MISRACPP2023-4_1_2]
        • Do not include headers deprecated in the C++17 standard [MISRACPP2023-4_1_2-a-4]
        • The 'uncaught_exception' function deprecated in the C++17 standard should not be used [MISRACPP2023-4_1_2-b-4]
        • Do not use throw exception specifications [MISRACPP2023-4_1_2-c-4]
        • A constexpr static data member should not be declared outside the class definition [MISRACPP2023-4_1_2-d-4]
      • Rule 4.1.3 (Required) There shall be no occurrence of undefined or critical unspecified behaviour [MISRACPP2023-4_1_3]
        • Avoid incorrect shift operations [MISRACPP2023-4_1_3-a-2]
        • Avoid signed integer overflows [MISRACPP2023-4_1_3-b-2]
        • Avoid null pointer dereferencing [MISRACPP2023-4_1_3-c-2]
        • Avoid division by zero [MISRACPP2023-4_1_3-d-2]
      • Rule 4.6.1 (Required) Operations on a memory location shall be sequenced appropriately [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1]
        • The value of an expression shall be the same under any order of evaluation that the standard permits [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-a-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function arguments [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-b-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function designator and function arguments [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-c-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of expression that involves a function call [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-d-2]
        • Between sequence points an object shall have its stored value modified at most once by the evaluation of an expression [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-e-2]
        • Do not use more than one volatile between two adjacent sequence points [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-f-2]
        • Don't write code that depends on the order of evaluation of function calls [MISRACPP2023-4_6_1-g-2]
      • Rule 5.0.1 (Advisory) Trigraph-like sequences should not be used [MISRACPP2023-5_0_1]
        • Trigraphs shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-5_0_1-a-4]
      • Rule 5.10.1 (Required) User-defined identifiers shall have an appropriate form [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1]
        • Do not declare entities in the standard library namespaces: posix, std and stdN [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-a-2]
        • Do not use identifiers which begin with one or two underscores (`_' or `__') [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-b-2]
        • An identifier shall not contain a double underscore '__' [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-c-2]
        • User defined suffixes of the user defined literal operators shall start with underscore followed by one or more letters [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-d-2]
        • A user-defined literal suffix should be directly preceded by a literal operator [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-e-2]
        • A macro identifier should have an appropriate form [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-f-2]
        • Do not declare identifiers with names reserved in the standard library [MISRACPP2023-5_10_1-g-2]
      • Rule 5.13.1 (Required) Within character literals and non raw-string literals, \ shall only be used to form a defined escape sequence or universal character name [MISRACPP2023-5_13_1]
        • Only those escape sequences that are defined in ISO/IEC 14882:2014 shall be used [MISRACPP2023-5_13_1-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.2 (Required) Octal escape sequences, hexadecimal escape sequences and universal character names shall be terminated [MISRACPP2023-5_13_2]
        • Octal and hexadecimal escape sequences shall be terminated [MISRACPP2023-5_13_2-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.3 (Required) Octal constants shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-5_13_3]
        • Octal constants (other than zero) shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-5_13_3-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.4 (Required) Unsigned integer literals shall be appropriately suffixed [MISRACPP2023-5_13_4]
        • A 'U' suffix shall be applied to all constants of unsigned type [MISRACPP2023-5_13_4-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.5 (Required) The lowercase form of "L" shall not be used as the first character in a literal suffix [MISRACPP2023-5_13_5]
        • Use capital 'L' instead of lowercase 'l' to indicate long [MISRACPP2023-5_13_5-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.6 (Required) An integer-literal of type long long shall not use a single L or l in any suffix [MISRACPP2023-5_13_6]
        • An integer-literal of type long long shall not use a single 'L' or 'l' in any suffix [MISRACPP2023-5_13_6-a-2]
      • Rule 5.13.7 (Required) String literals with different encoding prefixes shall not be concatenated [MISRACPP2023-5_13_7]
        • String literals with different encoding prefixes shall not be concatenated [MISRACPP2023-5_13_7-a-2]
        • String literals with and without encoding prefixes should not be concatenated [MISRACPP2023-5_13_7-b-2]
      • Rule 5.7.1 (Required) The character sequence /* shall not be used within a C-style comment [MISRACPP2023-5_7_1]
        • The character sequence /* shall not be used within a C-style comment [MISRACPP2023-5_7_1-a-2]
      • Dir 5.7.2 (Advisory) Sections of code should not be "commented out" [MISRACPP2023-5_7_2]
        • Sections of code should not be "commented out" [MISRACPP2023-5_7_2-a-4]
      • Rule 5.7.3 (Required) Line-splicing shall not be used in // comments [MISRACPP2023-5_7_3]
        • Line-splicing shall not be used in // comments [MISRACPP2023-5_7_3-a-2]
      • Rule 6.0.1 (Required) Block scope declarations shall not be visually ambiguous [MISRACPP2023-6_0_1]
        • Always declare functions at file scope [MISRACPP2023-6_0_1-a-2]
        • Parameter names in function declarations should not be enclosed in parentheses [MISRACPP2023-6_0_1-b-2]
        • Local variable names in variable declarations should not be enclosed in parentheses [MISRACPP2023-6_0_1-c-2]
      • Rule 6.0.2 (Advisory) When an array with external linkage is declared, its size should be explicitly specified [MISRACPP2023-6_0_2]
        • When an array is declared with external linkage, its size shall be stated explicitly or defined implicitly by initialisation [MISRACPP2023-6_0_2-a-4]
      • Rule 6.0.3 (Advisory) The only declarations in the global namespace should be main, namespace declarations and extern "C" declarations [MISRACPP2023-6_0_3]
        • The global namespace shall only contain main() and namespace declarations [MISRACPP2023-6_0_3-a-4]
      • Rule 6.0.4 (Required) The identifier main shall not be used for a function other than the global function main [MISRACPP2023-6_0_4]
        • The identifier main shall not be used for a function other than the global function main [MISRACPP2023-6_0_4-a-2]
      • Rule 6.2.1 (Required) The one-definition rule shall not be violated [MISRACPP2023-6_2_1]
        • The One Definition Rule shall not be violated [MISRACPP2023-6_2_1-a-2]
      • Rule 6.2.2 (Required) All declarations of a variable or function shall have the same type [MISRACPP2023-6_2_2]
        • All declarations of an object or function shall have compatible types [MISRACPP2023-6_2_2-a-2]
        • If a function is declared with an exception-specification, then all declarations of the same function (in other translation units) shall be declared with the same set of type-ids [MISRACPP2023-6_2_2-b-2]
      • Rule 6.2.3 (Required) The source code used to implement an entity shall appear only once [MISRACPP2023-6_2_3]
        • An identifier with external linkage shall have no more then one external definition [MISRACPP2023-6_2_3-a-2]
        • A type that is used in multiple translation units shall be defined in one and only one file [MISRACPP2023-6_2_3-b-2]
        • An inline function that is used in multiple translation units shall be defined in one and only one file [MISRACPP2023-6_2_3-c-2]
        • Template specialization shall be declared in the same file as the primary template or a user-defined type, for which the specialization is declared [MISRACPP2023-6_2_3-d-2]
      • Rule 6.2.4 (Required) A header file shall not contain definitions of functions or objects that are non-inline and have external linkage [MISRACPP2023-6_2_4]
        • Don't define entities with linkage in a header file [MISRACPP2023-6_2_4-a-2]
      • Rule 6.4.1 (Required) A variable declared in an inner scope shall not hide a variable declared in an outer scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1]
        • Identifier declared in a local or function prototype scope shall not hide an identifier declared in a global or namespace scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-a-2]
        • Identifiers declared in an inner local scope should not hide identifiers declared in an outer local scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-b-2]
        • Identifiers declared in a local scope should not hide identifiers declared in a class scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-c-2]
        • Identifiers declared in a class scope should not hide identifiers declared in a global or namespace scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-d-2]
        • Identifiers declared in an inner class scope should not hide identifiers declared in outer class scope [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-e-2]
        • Member variable names in derived classes should not be the same as member variable names in base classes [MISRACPP2023-6_4_1-f-2]
      • Rule 6.4.2 (Required) Derived classes shall not conceal functions that are inherited from their bases [MISRACPP2023-6_4_2]
        • Never redefine an inherited nonvirtual function [MISRACPP2023-6_4_2-a-2]
        • Member functions declared in derived class should not hide functions declared in base classes [MISRACPP2023-6_4_2-b-2]
      • Rule 6.4.3 (Required) A name that is present in a dependent base shall not be resolved by unqualified lookup [MISRACPP2023-6_4_3]
        • In a class template with a dependent base, any name that may be found in that dependent base shall be referred to using a qualified-id or this-> [MISRACPP2023-6_4_3-a-2]
      • Rule 6.5.1 (Advisory) A function or object with external linkage should be introduced in a header file [MISRACPP2023-6_5_1]
        • Objects or functions with external linkage shall be declared in a header file [MISRACPP2023-6_5_1-a-4]
      • Rule 6.5.2 (Advisory) Internal linkage should be specified appropriately [MISRACPP2023-6_5_2]
        • Do not use static keyword except inside functions and classes [MISRACPP2023-6_5_2-a-4]
        • Identifiers shall not simultaneously have both internal and external linkage in the same translation unit [MISRACPP2023-6_5_2-b-4]
      • Rule 6.7.1 (Required) Local variables shall not have static storage duration [MISRACPP2023-6_7_1]
        • Local variables shall not have static storage duration [MISRACPP2023-6_7_1-a-2]
      • Rule 6.7.2 (Required) Global variables shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-6_7_2]
        • Avoid unencapsulated global variables (including variables declared in namespaces and public static members) [MISRACPP2023-6_7_2-a-2]
      • Rule 6.8.1 (Required) An object shall not be accessed outside of its lifetime [MISRACPP2023-6_8_1]
        • Do not point to a wrapped object that has been freed [MISRACPP2023-6_8_1-a-2]
        • Do not read the value of a non-active union field [MISRACPP2023-6_8_1-b-2]
        • Do not use an object after its lifetime has ended [MISRACPP2023-6_8_1-c-2]
      • Rule 6.8.2 (Mandatory) A function must not return a reference or a pointer to a local variable with automatic storage duration [MISRACPP2023-6_8_2]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage shall not be returned from a function [MISRACPP2023-6_8_2-a-1]
        • Never return lambdas that capture local objects by reference [MISRACPP2023-6_8_2-b-1]
      • Rule 6.8.3 (Required) An assignment operator shall not assign the address of an object with automatic storage duration to an object with a greater lifetime [MISRACPP2023-6_8_3]
        • The address of an object with automatic storage duration shall not be assigned to an object with a greater lifetime [MISRACPP2023-6_8_3-a-2]
      • Rule 6.8.4 (Advisory) Member functions returning references to their object should be ref-qualified appropriately [MISRACPP2023-6_8_4]
        • Member functions returning references to their object should be ref-qualified appropriately [MISRACPP2023-6_8_4-a-4]
      • Rule 6.9.1 (Required) The same type aliases shall be used in all declarations of the same entity [MISRACPP2023-6_9_1]
        • The same type aliases shall be used in all declarations of the same entity [MISRACPP2023-6_9_1-a-2]
      • Rule 6.9.2 (Advisory) The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used [MISRACPP2023-6_9_2]
        • The names of the standard signed integer types and standard unsigned integer types should not be used [MISRACPP2023-6_9_2-a-4]
      • Rule 7.0.1 (Required) There shall be no conversion from type bool [MISRACPP2023-7_0_1]
        • There shall be no conversion from type bool [MISRACPP2023-7_0_1-a-2]
      • Rule 7.0.2 (Required) There shall be no conversion to type bool [MISRACPP2023-7_0_2]
        • There shall be no conversion to type bool [MISRACPP2023-7_0_2-a-2]
      • Rule 7.0.3 (Required) The numerical value of a character shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-7_0_3]
        • The plain char type shall be used only for the storage and use of character values [MISRACPP2023-7_0_3-a-2]
        • signed and unsigned char type shall be used only for the storage and use of numeric values [MISRACPP2023-7_0_3-b-2]
      • Rule 7.0.4 (Required) The operands of bitwise operators and shift operators shall be appropriate [MISRACPP2023-7_0_4]
        • Operands of bitwise and complement operators shall have an unsigned type [MISRACPP2023-7_0_4-a-2]
        • Operands of shift operators shall have an unsigned type [MISRACPP2023-7_0_4-b-2]
      • Rule 7.0.5 (Required) Integral promotion and the usual arithmetic conversions shall not change the signedness or the type category of an operand [MISRACPP2023-7_0_5]
        • Integral promotion and the usual arithmetic conversions shall not change the signedness or the type category of an operand [MISRACPP2023-7_0_5-a-2]
      • Rule 7.0.6 (Required) Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate [MISRACPP2023-7_0_6]
        • Assignment between numeric types shall be appropriate [MISRACPP2023-7_0_6-a-2]
      • Rule 7.11.1 (Required) nullptr shall be the only form of the null-pointer-constant [MISRACPP2023-7_11_1]
        • Prefer 'nullptr' over 'NULL' or '0'(zero) [MISRACPP2023-7_11_1-a-2]
        • The 'NULL' identifier should not be used [MISRACPP2023-7_11_1-b-2]
      • Rule 7.11.2 (Required) An array passed as a function argument shall not decay to a pointer [MISRACPP2023-7_11_2]
        • Do not pass an expression with array type to a function with a pointer or array type parameter [MISRACPP2023-7_11_2-a-2]
      • Rule 7.11.3 (Required) A conversion from function type to pointer-to-function type shall only occur in appropriate contexts [MISRACPP2023-7_11_3]
        • A conversion from function type to pointer-to-function type shall only occur in appropriate contexts [MISRACPP2023-7_11_3-a-2]
      • Rule 8.0.1 (Advisory) Parentheses should be used to make the meaning of an expression appropriately explicit [MISRACPP2023-8_0_1]
        • The operand of the 'sizeof' operator should be enclosed in parentheses [MISRACPP2023-8_0_1-a-4]
        • Use parentheses to indicate the precedence of operators in expressions [MISRACPP2023-8_0_1-b-4]
      • Rule 8.14.1 (Advisory) The right-hand operand of a logical && or || operator should not contain persistent side effects [MISRACPP2023-8_14_1]
        • The right-hand operand of a logical && or || operator shall not contain side effects [MISRACPP2023-8_14_1-a-4]
      • Rule 8.18.1 (Mandatory) An object or subobject must not be copied to an overlapping object [MISRACPP2023-8_18_1]
        • An object shall not be assigned or copied to an overlapping object [MISRACPP2023-8_18_1-a-1]
        • An object shall not be assigned to an overlapping object [MISRACPP2023-8_18_1-b-1]
        • An object shall not be assigned to an overlapping object [MISRACPP2023-8_18_1-c-1]
      • Rule 8.18.2 (Advisory) The result of an assignment operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_18_2]
        • The result of a built-in assignment operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_18_2-a-4]
      • Rule 8.19.1 (Advisory) The comma operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_19_1]
        • The comma operator shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_19_1-a-4]
      • Rule 8.1.1 (Required) A non-transient lambda shall not implicitly capture this [MISRACPP2023-8_1_1]
        • A non-transient lambda shall not implicitly capture this [MISRACPP2023-8_1_1-a-2]
      • Rule 8.1.2 (Advisory) Variables should be captured explicitly in a non-transient lambda [MISRACPP2023-8_1_2]
        • Variables should be captured explicitly in a non-transient lambda [MISRACPP2023-8_1_2-a-4]
      • Rule 8.20.1 (Advisory) An unsigned arithmetic operation with constant operands should not wrap [MISRACPP2023-8_20_1]
        • Evaluation of constant unsigned integer expressions should not lead to wrap-around [MISRACPP2023-8_20_1-a-4]
        • Evaluation of constant unsigned integer expressions in preprocessor directives should not lead to wraparound [MISRACPP2023-8_20_1-b-4]
      • Rule 8.2.1 (Required) A virtual base class shall only be cast to a derived class by means of dynamic_cast [MISRACPP2023-8_2_1]
        • A pointer to a virtual base class shall only be cast to a pointer to a derived class by means of dynamic_cast [MISRACPP2023-8_2_1-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.10 (Required) Functions shall not call themselves, either directly or indirectly [MISRACPP2023-8_2_10]
        • Do not use recursion [MISRACPP2023-8_2_10-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.11 (Required) An argument passed via ellipsis shall have an appropriate type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_11]
        • An argument passed via ellipsis shall have an appropriate type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_11-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.2 (Required) C-style casts and functional notation casts shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_2_2]
        • C-style casts (other than void casts) and functional notation casts (other than explicit constructor calls) shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_2_2-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.3 (Required) A cast shall not remove any const or volatile qualification from the type accessed via a pointer or by reference [MISRACPP2023-8_2_3]
        • A cast shall not remove any 'const' or 'volatile' qualification from the type of a pointer or reference [MISRACPP2023-8_2_3-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.4 (Required) Casts shall not be performed between a pointer to function and any other type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_4]
        • Casts shall not be performed between a pointer to a function and any other type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_4-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.5 (Required) reinterpret_cast shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_2_5]
        • Avoid using reinterpret_cast [MISRACPP2023-8_2_5-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.6 (Required) An object with integral, enumerated, or pointer to void type shall not be cast to a pointer type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_6]
        • An object with integer type or pointer to void type shall not be converted to an object with pointer type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_6-a-2]
        • An object with enumeration type shall not be converted to an object with pointer type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_6-b-2]
      • Rule 8.2.7 (Advisory) A cast should not convert a pointer type to an integral type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_7]
        • A cast should not convert a pointer type to an integral type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_7-a-4]
        • A cast should not convert a pointer type to 'intptr_t' and 'uintptr_t' types [MISRACPP2023-8_2_7-b-4]
      • Rule 8.2.8 (Required) An object pointer type shall not be cast to an integral type other than std::uintptr_t or std::intptr_t [MISRACPP2023-8_2_8]
        • A cast should not convert a pointer type to an integral type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_8-a-2]
      • Rule 8.2.9 (Required) The operand to typeid shall not be an expression of polymorphic class type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_9]
        • The operand to typeid shall not be an expression of polymorphic class type [MISRACPP2023-8_2_9-a-2]
      • Rule 8.3.1 (Advisory) The built-in unary - operator should not be applied to an expression of unsigned type [MISRACPP2023-8_3_1]
        • The unary minus operator shall not be applied to an expression whose underlying type is unsigned [MISRACPP2023-8_3_1-a-4]
      • Rule 8.3.2 (Advisory) The built-in unary + operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_3_2]
        • The built-in unary + operator should not be used [MISRACPP2023-8_3_2-a-4]
      • Rule 8.7.1 (Required) Pointer arithmetic shall not form an invalid pointer [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1]
        • Avoid accessing arrays out of bounds [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1-a-2]
        • A pointer operand and any pointer resulting from pointer arithmetic using that operand shall both address elements of the same array [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1-b-2]
        • Avoid overflow when reading from a buffer [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1-c-2]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1-d-2]
        • Avoid overflow due to reading a not zero terminated string [MISRACPP2023-8_7_1-e-2]
      • Rule 8.7.2 (Required) Subtraction between pointers shall only be applied to pointers that address elements of the same array [MISRACPP2023-8_7_2]
        • Do not subtract two pointers that do not address elements of the same array [MISRACPP2023-8_7_2-a-2]
      • Rule 8.9.1 (Required) The built-in relational operators >, >=, < and <= shall not be applied to objects of pointer type, except where they point to elements of the same array [MISRACPP2023-8_9_1]
        • Do not compare two unrelated pointers [MISRACPP2023-8_9_1-a-2]
      • Rule 9.2.1 (Required) An explicit type conversion shall not be an expression statement [MISRACPP2023-9_2_1]
        • Expression statements shall not be explicit calls to constructors of temporary objects only [MISRACPP2023-9_2_1-a-2]
      • Rule 9.3.1 (Required) The body of an iteration-statement or a selection-statement shall be a compound-statement [MISRACPP2023-9_3_1]
        • The statement forming the body of a 'switch', 'while', 'do...while' or 'for' statement shall be a compound statement [MISRACPP2023-9_3_1-a-2]
        • 'if' and 'else' should be followed by a compound statement [MISRACPP2023-9_3_1-b-2]
      • Rule 9.4.1 (Required) All if ... else if constructs shall be terminated with an else statement [MISRACPP2023-9_4_1]
        • All 'if...else-if' constructs shall be terminated with an 'else' clause [MISRACPP2023-9_4_1-a-2]
      • Rule 9.4.2 (Required) The structure of a switch statement shall be appropriate [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2]
        • The first or the last label of a switch statement should be the 'default' label unless all enumeration values are tested [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-a-2]
        • Every switch branch should be unconditionally terminated [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-b-2]
        • A switch label shall only be used when the most closely-enclosing compound statement is the body of a switch statement [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-c-2]
        • A switch statement shall only contain switch labels and switch clauses, and no other code [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-d-2]
        • Every switch statement shall have at least two switch-clauses [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-e-2]
        • The 'switch' statement should not contain labels other than 'case' and 'default' [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-f-2]
        • The condition of a 'switch' statement should only be preceded by an optional simple-declaration [MISRACPP2023-9_4_2-g-2]
      • Rule 9.5.1 (Advisory) Legacy for statements should be simple [MISRACPP2023-9_5_1]
        • Legacy 'for' statements should be simple [MISRACPP2023-9_5_1-a-4]
      • Rule 9.5.2 (Required) A for-range-initializer shall contain at most one function call [MISRACPP2023-9_5_2]
        • A for-range-initializer shall contain at most one function call [MISRACPP2023-9_5_2-a-2]
      • Rule 9.6.1 (Advisory) The goto statement should not be used [MISRACPP2023-9_6_1]
        • The goto statement shall not be used [MISRACPP2023-9_6_1-a-4]
      • Rule 9.6.2 (Required) A goto statement shall reference a label in a surrounding block [MISRACPP2023-9_6_2]
        • Any label referenced by a goto statement shall be declared in the same block, or in a block enclosing the goto statement [MISRACPP2023-9_6_2-a-2]
      • Rule 9.6.3 (Required) The goto statement shall jump to a label declared later in the function body [MISRACPP2023-9_6_3]
        • The goto statement shall jump to a label declared later in the same function body [MISRACPP2023-9_6_3-a-2]
      • Rule 9.6.4 (Required) A function declared with the [[noreturn]] attribute shall not return [MISRACPP2023-9_6_4]
        • Never return from functions that should not return [MISRACPP2023-9_6_4-a-2]
      • Rule 9.6.5 (Required) A function with non-void return type shall return a value on all paths [MISRACPP2023-9_6_5]
        • All exit paths from a function, except main(), with non-void return type shall have an explicit return statement with an expression [MISRACPP2023-9_6_5-a-2]
    • Memory and Resource Management [MRM]
      • Do not allocate resources in function argument list because the order of evaluation of a function's parameters is undefined [MRM-01-1]
      • Do not allocate more than one resource in a single statement [MRM-02-3]
      • All classes should contain the assignment operator or appropriate comment [MRM-04-3]
      • All classes should contain the copy constructor or appropriate comment [MRM-05-3]
      • Use the same form in corresponding calls to new/malloc and delete/free [MRM-06-1]
      • Don't memcpy or memcmp non-PODs [MRM-07-3]
      • Do not invoke malloc/realloc for objects having constructors [MRM-08-1]
      • Always assign a new value to an expression that points to deallocated memory [MRM-09-3]
      • Always assign a new value to global or member variable that points to deallocated memory [MRM-10-3]
      • Always assign a new value to parameter or local variable that points to deallocated memory [MRM-11-3]
      • Adhere to convention when writing new and delete [MRM-12-3]
      • Adhere to convention when writing new [MRM-13-3]
      • If a class defines any overload of operator new, it should provide overloads of all three of plain, in-place, and non-throwing operator new [MRM-14-3]
      • If a class defines any overload of operator new[], it should provide overloads of all three of plain, in-place, and non-throwing operator new[] [MRM-15-3]
      • If a class defines any overload of operator delete, it should provide overloads of all three of plain, in-place, and non-throwing operator delete [MRM-16-3]
      • If a class defines any overload of operator delete[], it should provide overloads of all three of plain, in-place, and non-throwing operator delete[] [MRM-17-3]
      • Do not allocate memory and expect that someone else will deallocate it later [MRM-18-3]
      • Do not allocate memory and expect that someone else will deallocate it later [MRM-19-3]
      • Do not allocate memory and expect that someone else will deallocate it later [MRM-20-3]
      • Use objects to manage resources [MRM-21-3]
      • Use objects to manage resources [MRM-22-3]
      • Never return a dereferenced local pointer initialized by new in this function scope [MRM-23-2]
      • Store newed objects in smart pointers in standalone statements [MRM-25-3]
      • Write operator delete if you write operator new [MRM-26-3]
      • Write operator delete[] if you write operator new[] [MRM-27-3]
      • Always provide new and delete together [MRM-28-3]
      • Always provide new[] and delete[] together [MRM-29-3]
      • Use allocation by declaration rather than by new or malloc [MRM-30-3]
      • Freed memory shouldn't be accessed under any circumstances [MRM-31-3]
      • Destructor should not be called manually [MRM-31_b-3]
      • Avoid hiding the global new [MRM-32-1]
      • Call delete on pointer members in destructors [MRM-33-2]
      • Check the return value of new [MRM-34-3]
      • Never provide brackets ([]) for delete when deallocating non-arrays [MRM-35-3]
      • Always provide empty brackets ([]) for delete when deallocating arrays [MRM-36-3]
      • Declare a copy assignment operator for classes with dynamically allocated memory [MRM-37-1]
      • Declare a copy constructor for classes with dynamically allocated memory [MRM-38-1]
      • Provide error handling for file opening errors right next to the call to fopen [MRM-39-2]
      • Copy and destroy consistently [MRM-40-3]
      • A copy assignment operator should be declared when a copy constructor is declared (and vice versa) [MRM-40_a-3]
      • Both the copy constructor and copy assignment operator should have the same public/protected/private permission [MRM-40_b-3]
      • If you have a non-trivial copy constructor or copy assignment operator, you should also declare a destructor [MRM-40_c-3]
      • Both copy constructor and copy assignment operator should be declared for classes with a nontrivial destructor [MRM-40_d-3]
      • A copy constructor shall copy all data members and bases [MRM-41-2]
      • Call fclose() on pointer member in destructor if the pointer was used to open a file [MRM-42-2]
      • An assignment operator shall assign all data bases [MRM-43-2]
      • Do not use sizeof operator on pointer type to specify the size of the memory to be allocated via 'malloc', 'calloc' or 'realloc' function [MRM-45-3]
      • Do not use calloc, malloc, realloc and free functions [MRM-46-3]
      • Classes containing at least one non-static member variable should declare the assignment operator or contain appropriate comment [MRM-47-3]
      • Classes containing at least one non-static member variable should declare the copy constructor or contain appropriate comment [MRM-48-3]
      • A copy constructor and a copy assignment operator shall be declared for classes that contain pointers to data items or nontrivial destructors [MRM-49-3]
      • Declare both private copy constructor and copy assignment operator at the same time [MRM-50-4]
      • Do not use 'delete' on pointers to a void type [MRM-51-3]
      • Use RAII to prevent resource leaks [MRM-52-4]
      • The user defined 'new' operator should throw the 'std::bad_alloc' exception when the allocation fails [MRM-53-3]
      • Avoid using the default operator 'new' for over-aligned types [MRM-54-3]
      • Do not pass a pointer that has insufficient storage capacity or that is not suitably aligned for the object being constructed to placement 'new' [MRM-55-2]
      • An overhead should be used when an array of objects is passed to the placement 'new' allocation function [MRM-55_b-3]
      • Copy assignment operators should not have side effects that could affect copying the object [MRM-56-3]
      • Move assignment operators should not have side effects that could affect moving the object [MRM-57-3]
      • The result of the memory allocation function should be cast immediately [MRM-58_a-3]
      • The result of the memory allocation function should be cast immediately into a pointer to the allocated type [MRM-58_b-4]
      • Do not declare the 'new' and 'delete' operators [MRM-59-3]
      • The memory management functions from the <new> and <memory> headers should not be used [MRM-60-3]
      • Advanced memory management operators 'new' and 'delete' should not be used [MRM-61-3]
      • Any member function named 'allocate' or 'deallocate' enclosed by namespace 'std' should not be used [MRM-62_a-3]
      • The 'std::unique_ptr::release' function should not be used [MRM-62_b-3]
    • Naming Conventions [NAMING]
      • Hungarian Notation [NAMING-HN]
        • Hungarian notation for array variables and parameters [NAMING-HN-01-3]
        • Hungarian notation for bool types [NAMING-HN-02-3]
        • Hungarian notation for bool pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-03-3]
        • Hungarian notation for byte types [NAMING-HN-04-3]
        • Hungarian notation for byte pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-05-3]
        • Hungarian notation for char types [NAMING-HN-06-3]
        • Hungarian notation for array of char types [NAMING-HN-07-3]
        • Hungarian notation for pointer, array, or reference to array of char types [NAMING-HN-08-3]
        • Hungarian notation for char pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-09-3]
        • Hungarian notation for char pointer or reference types [NAMING-HN-10-3]
        • Hungarian notation for constant parameters [NAMING-HN-11-3]
        • Hungarian notation for double-precision floating point types [NAMING-HN-12-3]
        • Hungarian notation for double-precision floating point pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-13-3]
        • Hungarian notation for dword types [NAMING-HN-14-3]
        • Hungarian notation for dword pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-15-3]
        • Hungarian notation for dynamically allocated array [NAMING-HN-16-3]
        • Hungarian notation for floating point types [NAMING-HN-17-3]
        • Hungarian notation for floating point pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-18-3]
        • Hungarian notation for class declaration [NAMING-HN-19-3]
        • Hungarian notation for structs declaration [NAMING-HN-20-3]
        • Hungarian notation for ifstream type variables and parameters [NAMING-HN-21-3]
        • Hungarian notation for int types [NAMING-HN-22-3]
        • Hungarian notation for int pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-23-3]
        • Hungarian notation for istream type parameters and variables [NAMING-HN-24-3]
        • Hungarian notation for long int types [NAMING-HN-25-3]
        • Hungarian notation for long double-precision floating point types [NAMING-HN-26-3]
        • Hungarian notation for long double-precision floating point pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-27-3]
        • Hungarian notation for long int pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-28-3]
        • Hungarian notation for member variables [NAMING-HN-29-3]
        • Hungarian notation for int types [NAMING-HN-30-3]
        • Hungarian notation for int pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-31-3]
        • Hungarian notation for ofstream type parameters and variables [NAMING-HN-32-3]
        • Hungarian notation for ostream type parameters and variables [NAMING-HN-33-3]
        • Hungarian notation for pointer [NAMING-HN-34-3]
        • Hungarian notation for reference parameters [NAMING-HN-35-3]
        • Hungarian notation for short int types [NAMING-HN-36-3]
        • Hungarian notation for short int pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-37-3]
        • Hungarian notation for static variables [NAMING-HN-38-3]
        • Hungarian notation for string types [NAMING-HN-39-3]
        • Hungarian notation for string pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-40-3]
        • Hungarian notation for unsigned types [NAMING-HN-41-3]
        • Hungarian notation for void pointer types [NAMING-HN-42-3]
        • Hungarian notation for word types [NAMING-HN-43-3]
        • Hungarian notation for word pointer, array, or reference types [NAMING-HN-44-3]
      • All "#define" constants shall be in uppercase [NAMING-01-3]
      • In an enumerated list, list members (elements) shall be in uppercase and names or tags for the list shall be in lowercase [NAMING-02-3]
      • Use lowercase for file names [NAMING-03-3]
      • Global prefixes should only be used for global variables [NAMING-04-3]
      • Begin local variable names with a lowercase letters [NAMING-05-3]
      • Begin global variable names with a lowercase letters [NAMING-06-3]
      • Begin member variable names with a lowercase letters [NAMING-07-3]
      • Begin all boolean type variables with 'b' [NAMING-08-3]
      • Begin class, struct, union, enum, and typedef names with an uppercase letter [NAMING-09-3]
      • The names of abstract data types, structures, typedefs, and enumerated types are to begin with an uppercase letter [NAMING-10-3]
      • The name of enumeration type shall begin with an uppercase letter and contain a suffix '_t' at the end [NAMING-11-3]
      • The names of structures shall begin with an uppercase letter and contain a suffix '_t' at the end [NAMING-12-3]
      • Begin constant variables with 'c' [NAMING-13-3]
      • Begin class data member names with 'its' [NAMING-14-3]
      • Begin all double type variable with 'd' [NAMING-15-3]
      • Begin all float type variables with 'f' [NAMING-16-3]
      • Begin all function names with uppercase letter [NAMING-17-3]
      • Begin global variable names with 'the' [NAMING-18-3]
      • Begin all integer type variable with 'i' [NAMING-19-3]
      • Functions that begin with 'is' should return boolean values [NAMING-20-3]
      • Begin all long integer variables with 'li' [NAMING-21-3]
      • Prefix a variable type 'pointer' with a 'p' character [NAMING-22-3]
      • Begin all short integer variables with 'si' [NAMING-23-3]
      • Begin all signed character variables with 'c' [NAMING-24-3]
      • Begin all terminated characters string variables with 'sz' [NAMING-25-3]
      • Begin all unsigned character type variables with 'uc' [NAMING-26-3]
      • Begin all unsigned integer type variables with 'ui' [NAMING-27-3]
      • Use lowercase letters for structure and union member names [NAMING-28-3]
      • Append names of non-scalar typedefs with "_t" [NAMING-29-3]
      • Implementation files in C always have the file name extension ".c" [NAMING-30-3]
      • Do not use typenames that differ only by the use of uppercase and lowercase letters [NAMING-31-3]
      • An include file for a class should have a file name of the form <class name> + extension [NAMING-32-3]
      • Do not use identifiers which begin with one or two underscores (`_' or `__') [NAMING-33-3]
      • An identifier shall not contain a double underscore '__' [NAMING-33_b-3]
      • Global function names should start with lowercase [NAMING-34-3]
      • Member function names should start with lowercase [NAMING-35-3]
      • Names of parameters in declaration and definition should be identical [NAMING-36-3]
      • Include files in C++ always have the file name extension '.hh' [NAMING-37-3]
      • Implementation files in C++ always have the file name extension ".cc" [NAMING-38-3]
      • Inline definition files always have the file name extension ".icc" [NAMING-39-3]
      • Only the first word of the name of a class, structure, namespace, enumeration, or typedef will begin with an uppercase letter [NAMING-40-3]
      • Header files will always have a file name extension of '.h' [NAMING-41-3]
      • Identifiers for constant and enumerator values shall be lowercase [NAMING-42-2]
      • File name extension, if present, should be "*.cpp" or "*.h" [NAMING-43-3]
      • All letters contained in function and variable names will be composed entirely of lowercase letters [NAMING-44-3]
      • Identifiers will not differ by mixture of case, the underscore character, interchange of the similarly looking letters and numbers [NAMING-45-3]
      • The ', ", /* or // characters shall not occur in a header file name [NAMING-46-3]
      • Different identifiers shall be typographically unambiguous [NAMING-47-3]
      • The \ character should not occur in a header file name [NAMING-48-3]
      • Implementation files in C++ will always have a file name extension of ".cpp" [NAMING-49-4]
      • Identifiers in the same name space with overlapping visibility should be typographically unambiguous [NAMING-50-4]
      • User defined suffixes of the user defined literal operators shall start with underscore followed by one or more letters [NAMING-51-3]
      • A user-defined literal suffix should be directly preceded by a literal operator [NAMING-51_b-3]
      • Universal character names shall be used only inside character or string literals [NAMING-52-3]
      • Header files should have a file extension of: ".h", ".hpp" or ".hxx" [NAMING-53-3]
      • Use visually distinct identifiers [NAMING-54-3]
      • A macro identifier should have an appropriate form [NAMING-55-3]
      • Do not declare identifiers with names reserved in the standard library [NAMING-56-3]
      • The parameters in all overrides of a function should either be unnamed or have identical names [NAMING-57-3]
    • Object Oriented [OOP]
      • Avoid public copy constructors and assignment operators in base classes [OOP-01-3]
      • Avoid slicing. Consider Clone instead of copying in base classes [OOP-02-3]
      • Class cannot inherit other class more than once unless it is virtual inheritance [OOP-03-1]
      • Do not derive functions with the same name from more than one base class [OOP-04-3]
      • Do not use multiple inheritance [OOP-05-2]
      • For multiple inheritance use virtual common base class [OOP-06-3]
      • Be wary about using multiple inheritance of classes that are not abstract interfaces [OOP-07-1]
      • Multiple inheritance shall be limited to at most 1 protected implementation [OOP-07_a-2]
      • Multiple inheritance shall not use any public implementations [OOP-07_b-2]
      • Ensure that a derived class has at most one base class which is not an interface class [OOP-07_c-1]
      • Do not directly access global data from a constructor [OOP-08-1]
      • Avoid the use of global objects in destructors [OOP-09-3]
      • Avoid using global data in member functions [OOP-10-2]
      • Avoid using the friend mechanism [OOP-11-3]
      • Friend declarations shall not be used except declarations of comparison operators [OOP-11_b-3]
      • Protected member function shall not return non-const handles to private class-data [OOP-12-3]
      • Do not redefine an inherited virtual function with a different default parameter value [OOP-13-3]
      • Consider use composition instead of private inheritance [OOP-14-5]
      • Avoid calling virtual functions from constructors [OOP-16-1]
      • Avoid calling virtual functions from destructors [OOP-16_b-1]
      • Write a using declaration to redeclare overloaded functions [OOP-17-4]
      • Avoid "public" data members [OOP-18-2]
      • Avoid 'protected' data members [OOP-19-2]
      • Avoid explicit cast from derived to a base class [OOP-20-3]
      • Use the virtual keyword if a subclass implements a virtual function [OOP-21-3]
      • Define a virtual destructor in classes used as base classes which have virtual functions [OOP-22-1]
      • If a class has virtual functions it shall have a virtual destructor [OOP-23-2]
      • Make destructors virtual in base classes [OOP-24-1]
      • Avoid declaring virtual functions inline [OOP-25-3]
      • Never convert pointers to objects of a derived class to pointers to objects of a virtual base class [OOP-26-3]
      • Declare copy assignment operator for class with reference or const members [OOP-27-3]
      • Avoid casts down the inheritance hierarchy [OOP-28-2]
      • A pointer to an abstract class shall not be converted to a pointer of a class that inherits from that abstract class [OOP-29-1]
      • Declare the copy constructor and copy assignment operator private not in class itself, but in a specifically designed base class [OOP-30-3]
      • Make base class destructors public and virtual, or protected and nonvirtual [OOP-31-1]
      • Never redefine an inherited nonvirtual function [OOP-32-3]
      • Do not redefine an inherited nonvirtual function with template parameter [OOP-33-3]
      • Check for assignment to self in operator= [OOP-34-4]
      • Down casting (casting from base to derived class) shall not be allowed [OOP-35-2]
      • Public member functions shall not return non-const handles to private/protected class-data [OOP-36-3]
      • Prefer composition when don't need inheritance [OOP-37-5]
      • If a class destructor is called and the class has virtual functions it shall have a virtual destructor [OOP-38-1]
      • A virtual base shall be explicitly declared in each derived class [OOP-39-4]
      • A stateful virtual base shall be explicitly declared in each derived class that accesses it [OOP-39_b-2]
      • Hierarchies should be based on abstract classes [OOP-40-4]
      • A base class shall not be both virtual and non-virtual in the same hierarchy [OOP-41-2]
      • The copy assignment operator shall be declared protected or private in an abstract class [OOP-42-3]
      • A virtual function shall only be overridden by a pure virtual function if it is itself declared as pure virtual [OOP-43-4]
      • There shall be no more than one definition of each virtual function on each path through the inheritance hierarchy [OOP-44-3]
      • All constructors that are callable with a single argument of fundamental type shall be declared explicit [OOP-45-3]
      • A copy constructor shall only initialize its base classes and the non-static members of the class of which it is a member [OOP-46-3]
      • Classes should not be derived from virtual bases [OOP-47-3]
      • Member data in non-POD types shall be private [OOP-48-3]
      • Casts from a base class to a derived class should not be performed on polymorphic types [OOP-49-1]
      • A pointer to a virtual base class shall only be cast to a pointer to a derived class by means of dynamic_cast [OOP-50-3]
      • Use namespace instead of class or structure containing only static functions [OOP-51-5]
      • A pointer to a class may not be converted to a pointer of a second class unless the one inherits from the other [OOP-52-4]
      • Member functions declared in derived class should not hide functions declared in base classes [OOP-53-3]
      • Do not increase the accessibility of overridden or hidden methods [OOP-54-3]
      • A non-POD type should be defined as class [OOP-55-4]
      • A user-defined assignment operator shall not be virtual [OOP-56-3]
      • Structs should only contain public data members and should not be a base or inherit [OOP-57-3]
    • Optimization [OPT]
      • Declare variables as locally as possible [OPT-01-3]
      • Avoid unused local variables [OPT-02-4]
      • Eliminate unused parameters [OPT-03-2]
      • Prefer canonical form of ++ and --. Prefer calling the prefix forms [OPT-04-3]
      • Avoid unused private member variables [OPT-05-3]
      • Avoid unnecessary local variables [OPT-06-4]
      • Prefer "a @= b" than "a = a @ b", where "@" is +, -, *, /, % [OPT-07-3]
      • Prefer "a @= b" than "a = a @ b", where "@" is &, |, ^, <<, >> [OPT-08-3]
      • Remove unnecessary '== true' [OPT-09-5]
      • Do not declare variables in "if", "for", "while", and "do while" statement [OPT-10-3]
      • If a file-level static variable is used/referenced in one function only then include that variable in the function itself [OPT-11-3]
      • If a file-level static variable is used/referenced in one class only then include that variable in the class itself [OPT-12-3]
      • Declare member variables in the descending size order [OPT-13-3]
      • Pass objects by reference instead of by value [OPT-14-3]
      • Consider overloading to avoid implicit type conversions [OPT-15-3]
      • Global function containing recursion, loops or virtual function call should not be inlined [OPT-16-3]
      • Avoid inline constructors and destructors [OPT-17-3]
      • Member function containing recursion or loops should not be inlined [OPT-18-3]
      • Consider using op= instead of stand-alone op [OPT-19-3]
      • Postpone variable definitions as long as possible [OPT-20-3]
      • Every switch statement shall have at least one non-empty case clause [OPT-21-3]
      • Useless case statement shall not be permitted [OPT-22-3]
      • Trivial accessor and mutator functions should be inlined [OPT-23-4]
      • Trivial forwarding functions should be inlined [OPT-24-4]
      • Only functions with 1 or 2 statements should be considered candidates for inline functions [OPT-25-4]
      • Variables will not be introduced until they can be initialized with meaningful values [OPT-26-2]
      • The number of accessor and mutator functions should be minimized [OPT-27-4]
      • 'strlen' function should not be used to check string against NULL/non-NULL [OPT-28-3]
      • Redundant explicit cast to the same type is not allowed [OPT-29-4]
      • Every defined function with internal linkage shall be used at least once [OPT-30-3]
      • There shall be no unused parameters (named or unnamed) in non-virtual functions [OPT-31-3]
      • All non-empty functions with void return type shall have external side effect(s) [OPT-32-3]
      • Functions with void return type shall not be empty [OPT-32_b-4]
      • Consider returning object by reference instead of by value [OPT-33-5]
      • Do not assign a variable to itself [OPT-35-3]
      • Do not use a variable inside its own initializer [OPT-36-3]
      • A function should not contain unused label declarations [OPT-37-4]
      • There should be no unused parameters in functions [OPT-38-4]
      • Every switch statement shall have at least two switch-clauses [OPT-39-3]
      • The same code (after preprocessing) in two branches of if-else-if chain [OPT-40_a-4]
      • The same code (after preprocessing) in different clauses of switch statement [OPT-40_b-4]
      • A file should directly include only the headers that contain declarations and definitions required to compile that file [OPT-41-4]
      • There shall be no unused named parameters in virtual functions [OPT-42-3]
      • A project should not contain unused variables with internal linkage [OPT-43-4]
      • A constexpr static data member should not be declared outside the class definition [OPT-44-3]
      • Non-const objects with internal linkage should be defined at function scope if they are only accessed from within a single function [OPT-45-3]
      • Types declared in an unnamed namespace scope should be used at least once [OPT-46-3]
      • Types declared in a block scope should be used at least once [OPT-47-3]
      • Destructor shall have a non-empty body [OPT-48-4]
    • OWASP Top 10 Most Critical Web Application Security Risks (2017) [OWASP2017]
      • OWASP A1 Injection [OWASP2017-A1]
        • Avoid passing unvalidated binary data to log methods [OWASP2017-A1-a-2]
        • Protect against command injection [OWASP2017-A1-b-1]
        • Avoid printing tainted data on the output console [OWASP2017-A1-c-1]
        • Protect against environment injection [OWASP2017-A1-d-1]
        • Exclude unsanitized user input from format strings [OWASP2017-A1-e-1]
        • Protect against SQL injection [OWASP2017-A1-f-1]
      • OWASP A10 Insufficient Logging&Monitoring [OWASP2017-A10]
        • All exceptions should be rethrown or logged with standard logger [OWASP2017-A10-a-2]
      • OWASP A2 Broken Authentication [OWASP2017-A2]
        • Do not use weak encryption functions [OWASP2017-A2-a-2]
      • OWASP A3 Sensitive Data Exposure [OWASP2017-A3]
        • Properly seed pseudorandom number generators [OWASP2017-A3-a-2]
      • OWASP A4 XML External Entities (XXE) [OWASP2017-A4]
        • Disable resolving XML external entities (XXE) in libxerces-c [OWASP2017-A4-a-2]
      • OWASP A5 Broken Access Control [OWASP2017-A5]
        • Protect against file name injection [OWASP2017-A5-a-1]
        • Observe correct revocation order while relinquishing privileges [OWASP2017-A5-b-3]
        • Ensure that privilege relinquishment is successful [OWASP2017-A5-c-3]
      • OWASP A6 Security Misconfiguration [OWASP2017-A6]
        • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single try-catch statement or function-try-block for a derived class and some or all of its bases, the handlers shall be ordered most-derived to base class [OWASP2017-A6-a-3]
        • Do not leave 'catch' blocks empty [OWASP2017-A6-b-3]
        • Properly use errno value [OWASP2017-A6-c-2]
    • OWASP API Security Top 10 (2019) [OWASP2019]
      • OWASP API10 Insufficient Logging & Monitoring [OWASP2019-API10]
        • All exceptions should be rethrown or logged with standard logger [OWASP2019-API10-a-2]
        • Do not use 'syslog' function for logging purposes [OWASP2019-API10-b-2]
      • OWASP API2 Broken User Authentication [OWASP2019-API2]
        • Do not use weak encryption functions [OWASP2019-API2-a-2]
      • OWASP API3 Excessive Data Exposure [OWASP2019-API3]
        • Do not pass empty container iterators to std algorithms as destinations [OWASP2019-API3-a-2]
        • Avoid accessing arrays out of bounds [OWASP2019-API3-b-2]
        • Avoid accessing arrays and pointers out of bounds [OWASP2019-API3-c-2]
        • Avoid buffer overflow due to defining incorrect format limits [OWASP2019-API3-d-1]
        • Avoid overflow due to reading a not zero terminated string [OWASP2019-API3-e-1]
        • Avoid overflow when reading from a buffer [OWASP2019-API3-f-1]
        • Avoid overflow when writing to a buffer [OWASP2019-API3-g-1]
        • Avoid buffer overflow from tainted data due to defining incorrect format limits [OWASP2019-API3-h-1]
        • Avoid buffer read overflow from tainted data [OWASP2019-API3-i-1]
        • Avoid buffer write overflow from tainted data [OWASP2019-API3-j-1]
        • Properly seed pseudorandom number generators [OWASP2019-API3-k-2]
        • Avoid passing sensitive data to functions that write to log files [OWASP2019-API3-l-2]
        • Avoid race conditions while checking for the existence of a symbolic link [OWASP2019-API3-m-1]
        • Usage of system properties (environment variables) should be restricted [OWASP2019-API3-n-4]
        • Avoid functions which use time from MFC library [OWASP2019-API3-o-3]
        • Do not print potentially sensitive information, resulting from an application error into exception messages [OWASP2019-API3-p-2]
        • A pointer to a structure should not be passed to a function that can copy data to the user space [OWASP2019-API3-q-3]
      • OWASP API4 Lack of Resources & Rate Limiting [OWASP2019-API4]
        • Validate potentially tainted data before it is used to determine the size of memory allocation [OWASP2019-API4-a-2]
        • Ensure resources are freed [OWASP2019-API4-b-1]
      • OWASP API7 Security Misconfiguration [OWASP2019-API7]
        • Properly use errno value [OWASP2019-API7-a-2]
        • Where multiple handlers are provided in a single try-catch statement or function-try-block for a derived class and some or all of its bases, the handlers shall be ordered most-derived to base class [OWASP2019-API7-b-3]
        • Do not leave 'catch' blocks empty [OWASP2019-API7-c-3]
      • OWASP API8 Injection [OWASP2019-API8]
        • Protect against command injection [OWASP2019-API8-a-1]
        • Avoid printing tainted data on the output console [OWASP2019-API8-b-1]
        • Protect against environment injection [OWASP2019-API8-c-1]
        • Protect against file name injection [OWASP2019-API8-d-1]
        • Exclude unsanitized user input from format strings [OWASP2019-API8-e-1]
        • Protect against SQL injection [OWASP2019-API8-f-1]
        • Disable resolving XML external entities (XXE) in libxerces-c [OWASP2019-API8-g-2]
        • Use care to ensure that LoadLibrary() will load the correct library [OWASP2019-API8-h-2]
        • Avoid passing dynamically created strings into exec [OWASP2019-API8-i-2]
        • Avoid passing user input into methods as parameters [OWASP2019-API8-j-2]
      • OWASP API9 Improper Assets Management [OWASP2019-API9]
        • Assert liberally to document internal assumptions and invariants [OWASP2019-API9-a-5]
        • When using enum, the values of each member should be explicitly declared [OWASP2019-API9-b-5]
        • All usage of assembler shall be documented [OWASP2019-API9-c-3]
        • Use of floating-point arithmetic shall be documented [OWASP2019-API9-d-3]
        • Objects or functions with external linkage shall be declared in a header file [OWASP2019-API9-e-4]
        • Document integer division [OWASP2019-API9-f-5]
        • All uses of the #pragma directive shall be documented and explained [OWASP2019-API9-g-3]
